canbe10{_}667{_}Suddenly I heard the voice of my poor husband in exclamations of astonishment, with that of my son in reassurance and dissuasion; and there by the shadow of a group of trees they stood--near, so near!
canbe10{_}668{_}Their faces were toward me, the eyes of the elder man fixed upon mine.
canbe10{_}669{_}He saw me--at last, at last, he saw me!
canbe10{_}670{_}In the consciousness of that, my terror fled as a cruel dream.
canbe10{_}671{_}The death-spell was broken:  Love had conquered Law!
canbe10{_}672{_}Mad with exultation I shouted--I MUST have shouted, "He sees, he sees: he will understand!"
canbe10{_}673{_}Then, controlling myself, I moved forward, smiling and consciously beautiful, to offer myself to his arms, to comfort him with endearments, and, with my son's hand in mine, to speak words that should restore the broken bonds between the living and the dead.
canbe10{_}674{_}Alas!
canbe10{_}675{_}alas!
canbe10{_}676{_}his face went white with fear, his eyes were as those of a hunted animal.
canbe10{_}677{_}He backed away from me, as I advanced, and at last turned and fled into the wood--whither, it is not given to me to know.
canbe10{_}678{_}To my poor boy, left doubly desolate, I have never been able to impart a sense of my presence.
canbe10{_}679{_}Soon he, too, must pass to this Life Invisible and be lost to me forever.
canbe10{_}680{_}A DIAGNOSIS OF DEATH    "I am not so superstitious as some of your physicians--men of science, as you are pleased to be called," said Hawver, replying to an accusation that had not been made.
canbe10{_}681{_}"Some of you--only a few, I confess--believe in the immortality of the soul, and in apparitions which you have not the honesty to call ghosts.
canbe10{_}682{_}I go no further than a conviction that the living are sometimes seen where they are not, but have been--where they have lived so long, perhaps so intensely, as to have left their impress on everything about them.
canbe10{_}683{_}I know, indeed, that one's environment may be so affected by one's personality as to yield, long afterward, an image of one's self to the eyes of another.
canbe10{_}684{_}Doubtless the impressing personality has to be the right kind of personality as the perceiving eyes have to be the right kind of eyes--mine, for example."
canbe10{_}685{_}"Yes, the right kind of eyes, conveying sensations to the wrong kind of brain," said Dr. Frayley, smiling.
canbe10{_}686{_}"Thank you; one likes to have an expectation gratified; that is about the reply that I supposed you would have the civility to make."
canbe10{_}687{_}"Pardon me.
canbe10{_}688{_}But you say that you know.
canbe10{_}689{_}That is a good deal to say, don't you think?
canbe10{_}690{_}Perhaps you will not mind the trouble of saying how you learned."
canbe10{_}691{_}"You will call it an hallucination," Hawver said, "but that does not matter."
canbe10{_}692{_}And he told the story.
canbe10{_}693{_}"Last summer I went, as you know, to pass the hot weather term in the town of Meridian.
canbe10{_}694{_}The relative at whose house I had intended to stay was ill, so I sought other quarters.
canbe10{_}695{_}After some difficulty I succeeded in renting a vacant dwelling that had been occupied by an eccentric doctor of the name of Mannering, who had gone away years before, no one knew where, not even his agent.
canbe10{_}696{_}He had built the house himself and had lived in it with an old servant for about ten years.
canbe10{_}697{_}His practice, never very extensive, had after a few years been given up entirely.
canbe10{_}698{_}Not only so, but he had withdrawn himself almost altogether from social life and become a recluse.
canbe10{_}699{_}I was told by the village doctor, about the only person with whom he held any relations, that during his retirement he had devoted himself to a single line of study, the result of which he had expounded in a book that did not commend itself to the approval of his professional brethren, who, indeed, considered him not entirely sane.
canbe10{_}700{_}I have not seen the book and cannot now recall the title of it, but I am told that it expounded a rather startling theory.
canbe10{_}701{_}He held that it was possible in the case of many a person in good health to forecast his death with precision, several months in advance of the event.
canbe10{_}702{_}The limit, I think, was eighteen months.
canbe10{_}703{_}There were local tales of his having exerted his powers of prognosis, or perhaps you would say diagnosis; and it was said that in every instance the person whose friends he had warned had died suddenly at the appointed time, and from no assignable cause.
canbe10{_}704{_}All this, however, has nothing to do with what I have to tell; I thought it might amuse a physician.
canbe10{_}705{_}"The house was furnished, just as he had lived in it.
canbe10{_}706{_}It was a rather gloomy dwelling for one who was neither a recluse nor a student, and I think it gave something of its character to me-- perhaps some of its former occupant's character; for always I felt in it a certain melancholy that was not in my natural disposition, nor, I think, due to loneliness.
canbe10{_}707{_}I had no servants that slept in the house, but I have always been, as you know, rather fond of my own society, being much addicted to reading, though little to study.
canbe10{_}708{_}Whatever was the cause, the effect was dejection and a sense of impending evil; this was especially so in Dr. Mannering's study, although that room was the lightest and most airy in the house.
canbe10{_}709{_}The doctor's life-size portrait in oil hung in that room, and seemed completely to dominate it.
canbe10{_}710{_}There was nothing unusual in the picture; the man was evidently rather good looking, about fifty years old, with iron-gray hair, a smooth-shaven face and dark, serious eyes.
canbe10{_}711{_}Something in the picture always drew and held my attention.
canbe10{_}712{_}The man's appearance became familiar to me, and rather 'haunted' me.
canbe10{_}713{_}"One evening I was passing through this room to my bedroom, with a lamp--there is no gas in Meridian.
canbe10{_}714{_}I stopped as usual before the portrait, which seemed in the lamplight to have a new expression, not easily named, but distinctly uncanny.
canbe10{_}715{_}It interested but did not disturb me.
canbe10{_}716{_}I moved the lamp from one side to the other and observed the effects of the altered light.
canbe10{_}717{_}While so engaged I felt an impulse to turn round.
canbe10{_}718{_}As I did so I saw a man moving across the room directly toward me!
canbe10{_}719{_}As soon as he came near enough for the lamplight to illuminate the face I saw that it was Dr. Mannering himself; it was as if the portrait were walking!
canbe10{_}720{_}"'I beg your pardon,' I said, somewhat coldly, 'but if you knocked I did not hear.'
canbe10{_}721{_}"He passed me, within an arm's length, lifted his right forefinger, as in warning, and without a word went on out of the room, though I observed his exit no more than I had observed his entrance.
canbe10{_}722{_}"Of course, I need not tell you that this was what you will call an hallucination and I call an apparition.
canbe10{_}723{_}That room had only two doors, of which one was locked; the other led into a bedroom, from which there was no exit.
canbe10{_}724{_}My feeling on realizing this is not an important part of the incident.
canbe10{_}725{_}"Doubtless this seems to you a very commonplace 'ghost story'--one constructed on the regular lines laid down by the old masters of the art.
canbe10{_}726{_}If that were so I should not have related it, even if it were true.
canbe10{_}727{_}The man was not dead; I met him to-day in Union street.
canbe10{_}728{_}He passed me in a crowd."
canbe10{_}729{_}Hawver had finished his story and both men were silent.
canbe10{_}730{_}Dr. Frayley absently drummed on the table with his fingers.
canbe10{_}731{_}"Did he say anything to-day?"
canbe10{_}732{_}he asked--"anything from which you inferred that he was not dead?"
canbe10{_}733{_}Hawver stared and did not reply.
canbe10{_}734{_}"Perhaps," continued Frayley, "he made a sign, a gesture--lifted a finger, as in warning.
canbe10{_}735{_}It's a trick he had--a habit when saying something serious--announcing the result of a diagnosis, for example."
canbe10{_}736{_}"Yes, he did--just as his apparition had done.
canbe10{_}737{_}But, good God!
canbe10{_}738{_}did you ever know him?"
canbe10{_}739{_}Hawver was apparently growing nervous.
canbe10{_}740{_}"I knew him.
canbe10{_}741{_}I have read his book, as will every physician some day.
canbe10{_}742{_}It is one of the most striking and important of the century's contributions to medical science.
canbe10{_}743{_}Yes, I knew him; I attended him in an illness three years ago.
canbe10{_}744{_}He died."
canbe10{_}745{_}Hawver sprang from his chair, manifestly disturbed.
canbe10{_}746{_}He strode forward and back across the room; then approached his friend, and in a voice not altogether steady, said:  "Doctor, have you anything to say to me--as a physician?"
canbe10{_}747{_}"No, Hawver; you are the healthiest man I ever knew.
canbe10{_}748{_}As a friend I advise you to go to your room.
canbe10{_}749{_}You play the violin like an angel.
canbe10{_}750{_}Play it; play something light and lively.
canbe10{_}751{_}Get this cursed bad business off your mind."
canbe10{_}752{_}The next day Hawver was found dead in his room, the violin at his neck, the bow upon the strings, his music open before him at Chopin's funeral march.
canbe10{_}753{_}MOXON'S MASTER    "Are you serious?--do you really believe that a machine thinks?"
canbe10{_}754{_}I got no immediate reply; Moxon was apparently intent upon the coals in the grate, touching them deftly here and there with the fire-poker till they signified a sense of his attention by a brighter glow.
canbe10{_}755{_}For several weeks I had been observing in him a growing habit of delay in answering even the most trivial of commonplace questions.
canbe10{_}756{_}His air, however, was that of preoccupation rather than deliberation:  one might have said that he had "something on his mind."
canbe10{_}757{_}Presently he said:  "What is a 'machine'?
canbe10{_}758{_}The word has been variously defined.
canbe10{_}759{_}Here is one definition from a popular dictionary:  'Any instrument or organization by which power is applied and made effective, or a desired effect produced.'
canbe10{_}760{_}Well, then, is not a man a machine?
canbe10{_}761{_}And you will admit that he thinks--or thinks he thinks."
canbe10{_}762{_}"If you do not wish to answer my question," I said, rather testily, "why not say so?--all that you say is mere evasion.
canbe10{_}763{_}You know well enough that when I say 'machine' I do not mean a man, but something that man has made and controls."
canbe10{_}764{_}"When it does not control him," he said, rising abruptly and looking out of a window, whence nothing was visible in the blackness of a stormy night.
canbe10{_}765{_}A moment later he turned about and with a smile said: "I beg your pardon; I had no thought of evasion.
canbe10{_}766{_}I considered the dictionary man's unconscious testimony suggestive and worth something in the discussion.
canbe10{_}767{_}I can give your question a direct answer easily enough:  I do believe that a machine thinks about the work that it is doing."
canbe10{_}768{_}That was direct enough, certainly.
canbe10{_}769{_}It was not altogether pleasing, for it tended to confirm a sad suspicion that Moxon's devotion to study and work in his machine-shop had not been good for him.
canbe10{_}770{_}I knew, for one thing, that he suffered from insomnia, and that is no light affliction.
canbe10{_}771{_}Had it affected his mind?
canbe10{_}772{_}His reply to my question seemed to me then evidence that it had; perhaps I should think differently about it now.
canbe10{_}773{_}I was younger then, and among the blessings that are not denied to youth is ignorance.
canbe10{_}774{_}Incited by that great stimulant to controversy, I said:  "And what, pray, does it think with--in the absence of a brain?"
canbe10{_}775{_}The reply, coming with less than his customary delay, took his favorite form of counter-interrogation:  "With what does a plant think--in the absence of a brain?"
canbe10{_}776{_}"Ah, plants also belong to the philosopher class!
canbe10{_}777{_}I should be pleased to know some of their conclusions; you may omit the premises."
canbe10{_}778{_}"Perhaps," he replied, apparently unaffected by my foolish irony, "you may be able to infer their convictions from their acts.
canbe10{_}779{_}I will spare you the familiar examples of the sensitive mimosa, the several insectivorous flowers and those whose stamens bend down and shake their pollen upon the entering bee in order that he may fertilize their distant mates.
canbe10{_}780{_}But observe this.
canbe10{_}781{_}In an open spot in my garden I planted a climbing vine.
canbe10{_}782{_}When it was barely above the surface I set a stake into the soil a yard away.
canbe10{_}783{_}The vine at once made for it, but as it was about to reach it after several days I removed it a few feet.
canbe10{_}784{_}The vine at once altered its course, making an acute angle, and again made for the stake.
canbe10{_}785{_}This manoeuvre was repeated several times, but finally, as if discouraged, the vine abandoned the pursuit and ignoring further attempts to divert it traveled to a small tree, further away, which it climbed.
canbe10{_}786{_}"Roots of the eucalyptus will prolong themselves incredibly in search of moisture.
canbe10{_}787{_}A well-known horticulturist relates that one entered an old drain pipe and followed it until it came to a break, where a section of the pipe had been removed to make way for a stone wall that had been built across its course.
canbe10{_}788{_}The root left the drain and followed the wall until it found an opening where a stone had fallen out.
canbe10{_}789{_}It crept through and following the other side of the wall back to the drain, entered the unexplored part and resumed its journey."
canbe10{_}790{_}"And all this?"
canbe10{_}791{_}"Can you miss the significance of it?
canbe10{_}792{_}It shows the consciousness of plants.
canbe10{_}793{_}It proves that they think."
canbe10{_}794{_}"Even if it did--what then?
canbe10{_}795{_}We were speaking, not of plants, but of machines.
canbe10{_}796{_}They may be composed partly of wood--wood that has no longer vitality--or wholly of metal.
canbe10{_}797{_}Is thought an attribute also of the mineral kingdom?"
canbe10{_}798{_}"How else do you explain the phenomena, for example, of crystallization?"
canbe10{_}799{_}"I do not explain them."
canbe10{_}800{_}"Because you cannot without affirming what you wish to deny, namely, intelligent cooperation among the constituent elements of the crystals.
canbe10{_}801{_}When soldiers form lines, or hollow squares, you call it reason.
canbe10{_}802{_}When wild geese in flight take the form of a letter V you say instinct.
canbe10{_}803{_}When the homogeneous atoms of a mineral, moving freely in solution, arrange themselves into shapes mathematically perfect, or particles of frozen moisture into the symmetrical and beautiful forms of snowflakes, you have nothing to say.
canbe10{_}804{_}You have not even invented a name to conceal your heroic unreason."
canbe10{_}805{_}Moxon was speaking with unusual animation and earnestness.
canbe10{_}806{_}As he paused I heard in an adjoining room known to me as his "machine- shop," which no one but himself was permitted to enter, a singular thumping sound, as of some one pounding upon a table with an open hand.
canbe10{_}807{_}Moxon heard it at the same moment and, visibly agitated, rose and hurriedly passed into the room whence it came.
canbe10{_}808{_}I thought it odd that any one else should be in there, and my interest in my friend-- with doubtless a touch of unwarrantable curiosity--led me to listen intently, though, I am happy to say, not at the keyhole.
canbe10{_}809{_}There were confused sounds, as of a struggle or scuffle; the floor shook.
canbe10{_}810{_}I distinctly heard hard breathing and a hoarse whisper which said "Damn you!"
canbe10{_}811{_}Then all was silent, and presently Moxon reappeared and said, with a rather sorry smile:  "Pardon me for leaving you so abruptly.
canbe10{_}812{_}I have a machine in there that lost its temper and cut up rough."
canbe10{_}813{_}Fixing my eyes steadily upon his left cheek, which was traversed by four parallel excoriations showing blood, I said:  "How would it do to trim its nails?"
canbe10{_}814{_}I could have spared myself the jest; he gave it no attention, but seated himself in the chair that he had left and resumed the interrupted monologue as if nothing had occurred:  "Doubtless you do not hold with those (I need not name them to a man of your reading) who have taught that all matter is sentient, that every atom is a living, feeling, conscious being.
canbe10{_}815{_}_I_ do.
canbe10{_}816{_}There is no such thing as dead, inert matter:  it is all alive; all instinct with force, actual and potential; all sensitive to the same forces in its environment and susceptible to the contagion of higher and subtler ones residing in such superior organisms as it may be brought into relation with, as those of man when he is fashioning it into an instrument of his will.
canbe10{_}817{_}It absorbs something of his intelligence and purpose--more of them in proportion to the complexity of the resulting machine and that of its work.
canbe10{_}818{_}"Do you happen to recall Herbert Spencer's definition of 'Life'?
canbe10{_}819{_}I read it thirty years ago.
canbe10{_}820{_}He may have altered it afterward, for anything I know, but in all that time I have been unable to think of a single word that could profitably be changed or added or removed.
canbe10{_}821{_}It seems to me not only the best definition, but the only possible one.
canbe10{_}822{_}"'Life,' he says, 'is a definite combination of heterogeneous changes, both simultaneous and successive, in correspondence with external coexistences and sequences.'"
canbe10{_}823{_}"That defines the phenomenon," I said, "but gives no hint of its cause."
canbe10{_}824{_}"That," he replied, "is all that any definition can do.
canbe10{_}825{_}As Mill points out, we know nothing of cause except as an antecedent--nothing of effect except as a consequent.
canbe10{_}826{_}Of certain phenomena, one never occurs without another, which is dissimilar:  the first in point of time we call cause, the second, effect.
canbe10{_}827{_}One who had many times seen a rabbit pursued by a dog, and had never seen rabbits and dogs otherwise, would think the rabbit the cause of the dog.
canbe10{_}828{_}"But I fear," he added, laughing naturally enough, "that my rabbit is leading me a long way from the track of my legitimate quarry:  I'm indulging in the pleasure of the chase for its own sake.
canbe10{_}829{_}What I want you to observe is that in Herbert Spencer's definition of 'life' the activity of a machine is included--there is nothing in the definition that is not applicable to it.
canbe10{_}830{_}According to this sharpest of observers and deepest of thinkers, if a man during his period of activity is alive, so is a machine when in operation.
canbe10{_}831{_}As an inventor and constructor of machines I know that to be true."
canbe10{_}832{_}Moxon was silent for a long time, gazing absently into the fire.
canbe10{_}833{_}It was growing late and I thought it time to be going, but somehow I did not like the notion of leaving him in that isolated house, all alone except for the presence of some person of whose nature my conjectures could go no further than that it was unfriendly, perhaps malign.
canbe10{_}834{_}Leaning toward him and looking earnestly into his eyes while making a motion with my hand through the door of his workshop, I said:  "Moxon, whom have you in there?"
canbe10{_}835{_}Somewhat to my surprise he laughed lightly and answered without hesitation:  "Nobody; the incident that you have in mind was caused by my folly in leaving a machine in action with nothing to act upon, while I undertook the interminable task of enlightening your understanding.
canbe10{_}836{_}Do you happen to know that Consciousness is the creature of Rhythm?"
canbe10{_}837{_}"O bother them both!"
canbe10{_}838{_}I replied, rising and laying hold of my overcoat.
canbe10{_}839{_}"I'm going to wish you good night; and I'll add the hope that the machine which you inadvertently left in action will have her gloves on the next time you think it needful to stop her."
canbe10{_}840{_}Without waiting to observe the effect of my shot I left the house.
canbe10{_}841{_}Rain was falling, and the darkness was intense.
canbe10{_}842{_}In the sky beyond the crest of a hill toward which I groped my way along precarious plank sidewalks and across miry, unpaved streets I could see the faint glow of the city's lights, but behind me nothing was visible but a single window of Moxon's house.
canbe10{_}843{_}It glowed with what seemed to me a mysterious and fateful meaning.
canbe10{_}844{_}I knew it was an uncurtained aperture in my friend's "machine-shop," and I had little doubt that he had resumed the studies interrupted by his duties as my instructor in mechanical consciousness and the fatherhood of Rhythm.
canbe10{_}845{_}Odd, and in some degree humorous, as his convictions seemed to me at that time, I could not wholly divest myself of the feeling that they had some tragic relation to his life and character--perhaps to his destiny--although I no longer entertained the notion that they were the vagaries of a disordered mind.
canbe10{_}846{_}Whatever might be thought of his views, his exposition of them was too logical for that.
canbe10{_}847{_}Over and over, his last words came back to me:  "Consciousness is the creature of Rhythm."
canbe10{_}848{_}Bald and terse as the statement was, I now found it infinitely alluring.
canbe10{_}849{_}At each recurrence it broadened in meaning and deepened in suggestion.
canbe10{_}850{_}Why, here, (I thought) is something upon which to found a philosophy.
canbe10{_}851{_}If consciousness is the product of rhythm all things ARE conscious, for all have motion, and all motion is rhythmic.
canbe10{_}852{_}I wondered if Moxon knew the significance and breadth of his thought--the scope of this momentous generalization; or had he arrived at his philosophic faith by the tortuous and uncertain road of observation?
canbe10{_}853{_}That faith was then new to me, and all Moxon's expounding had failed to make me a convert; but now it seemed as if a great light shone about me, like that which fell upon Saul of Tarsus; and out there in the storm and darkness and solitude I experienced what Lewes calls "The endless variety and excitement of philosophic thought."
canbe10{_}854{_}I exulted in a new sense of knowledge, a new pride of reason.
canbe10{_}855{_}My feet seemed hardly to touch the earth; it was as if I were uplifted and borne through the air by invisible wings.
canbe10{_}856{_}Yielding to an impulse to seek further light from him whom I now recognized as my master and guide, I had unconsciously turned about, and almost before I was aware of having done so found myself again at Moxon's door.
canbe10{_}857{_}I was drenched with rain, but felt no discomfort.
canbe10{_}858{_}Unable in my excitement to find the doorbell I instinctively tried the knob.
canbe10{_}859{_}It turned and, entering, I mounted the stairs to the room that I had so recently left.
canbe10{_}860{_}All was dark and silent; Moxon, as I had supposed, was in the adjoining room--the "machine-shop."
canbe10{_}861{_}Groping along the wall until I found the communicating door I knocked loudly several times, but got no response, which I attributed to the uproar outside, for the wind was blowing a gale and dashing the rain against the thin walls in sheets.
canbe10{_}862{_}The drumming upon the shingle roof spanning the unceiled room was loud and incessant.
canbe10{_}863{_}I had never been invited into the machine-shop--had, indeed, been denied admittance, as had all others, with one exception, a skilled metal worker, of whom no one knew anything except that his name was Haley and his habit silence.
canbe10{_}864{_}But in my spiritual exaltation, discretion and civility were alike forgotten and I opened the door.
canbe10{_}865{_}What I saw took all philosophical speculation out of me in short order.
canbe10{_}866{_}Moxon sat facing me at the farther side of a small table upon which a single candle made all the light that was in the room.
canbe10{_}867{_}Opposite him, his back toward me, sat another person.
canbe10{_}868{_}On the table between the two was a chessboard; the men were playing.
canbe10{_}869{_}I knew little of chess, but as only a few pieces were on the board it was obvious that the game was near its close.
canbe10{_}870{_}Moxon was intensely interested--not so much, it seemed to me, in the game as in his antagonist, upon whom he had fixed so intent a look that, standing though I did directly in the line of his vision, I was altogether unobserved.
canbe10{_}871{_}His face was ghastly white, and his eyes glittered like diamonds.
canbe10{_}872{_}Of his antagonist I had only a back view, but that was sufficient; I should not have cared to see his face.
canbe10{_}873{_}He was apparently not more than five feet in height, with proportions suggesting those of a gorilla--a tremendous breadth of shoulders, thick, short neck and broad, squat head, which had a tangled growth of black hair and was topped with a crimson fez.
canbe10{_}874{_}A tunic of the same color, belted tightly to the waist, reached the seat--apparently a box--upon which he sat; his legs and feet were not seen.
canbe10{_}875{_}His left forearm appeared to rest in his lap; he moved his pieces with his right hand, which seemed disproportionately long.
canbe10{_}876{_}I had shrunk back and now stood a little to one side of the doorway and in shadow.
canbe10{_}877{_}If Moxon had looked farther than the face of his opponent he could have observed nothing now, except that the door was open.
canbe10{_}878{_}Something forbade me either to enter or to retire, a feeling-- I know not how it came--that I was in the presence of an imminent tragedy and might serve my friend by remaining.
canbe10{_}879{_}With a scarcely conscious rebellion against the indelicacy of the act I remained.
canbe10{_}880{_}The play was rapid.
canbe10{_}881{_}Moxon hardly glanced at the board before making his moves, and to my unskilled eye seemed to move the piece most convenient to his hand, his motions in doing so being quick, nervous and lacking in precision.
canbe10{_}882{_}The response of his antagonist, while equally prompt in the inception, was made with a slow, uniform, mechanical and, I thought, somewhat theatrical movement of the arm, that was a sore trial to my patience.
canbe10{_}883{_}There was something unearthly about it all, and I caught myself shuddering.
canbe10{_}884{_}But I was wet and cold.
canbe10{_}885{_}Two or three times after moving a piece the stranger slightly inclined his head, and each time I observed that Moxon shifted his king.
canbe10{_}886{_}All at once the thought came to me that the man was dumb.
canbe10{_}887{_}And then that he was a machine--an automaton chess-player!
canbe10{_}888{_}Then I remembered that Moxon had once spoken to me of having invented such a piece of mechanism, though I did not understand that it had actually been constructed.
canbe10{_}889{_}Was all his talk about the consciousness and intelligence of machines merely a prelude to eventual exhibition of this device--only a trick to intensify the effect of its mechanical action upon me in my ignorance of its secret?
canbe10{_}890{_}A fine end, this, of all my intellectual transports--my "endless variety and excitement of philosophic thought!"
canbe10{_}891{_}I was about to retire in disgust when something occurred to hold my curiosity.
canbe10{_}892{_}I observed a shrug of the thing's great shoulders, as if it were irritated:  and so natural was this--so entirely human--that in my new view of the matter it startled me.
canbe10{_}893{_}Nor was that all, for a moment later it struck the table sharply with its clenched hand.
canbe10{_}894{_}At that gesture Moxon seemed even more startled than I:  he pushed his chair a little backward, as in alarm.
canbe10{_}895{_}Presently Moxon, whose play it was, raised his hand high above the board, pounced upon one of his pieces like a sparrow-hawk and with the exclamation "checkmate!"
canbe10{_}896{_}rose quickly to his feet and stepped behind his chair.
canbe10{_}897{_}The automaton sat motionless.
canbe10{_}898{_}The wind had now gone down, but I heard, at lessening intervals and progressively louder, the rumble and roll of thunder.
canbe10{_}899{_}In the pauses between I now became conscious of a low humming or buzzing which, like the thunder, grew momentarily louder and more distinct.
canbe10{_}900{_}It seemed to come from the body of the automaton, and was unmistakably a whirring of wheels.
canbe10{_}901{_}It gave me the impression of a disordered mechanism which had escaped the repressive and regulating action of some controlling part--an effect such as might be expected if a pawl should be jostled from the teeth of a ratchet-wheel.
canbe10{_}902{_}But before I had time for much conjecture as to its nature my attention was taken by the strange motions of the automaton itself.
canbe10{_}903{_}A slight but continuous convulsion appeared to have possession of it.
canbe10{_}904{_}In body and head it shook like a man with palsy or an ague chill, and the motion augmented every moment until the entire figure was in violent agitation.
canbe10{_}905{_}Suddenly it sprang to its feet and with a movement almost too quick for the eye to follow shot forward across table and chair, with both arms thrust forth to their full length--the posture and lunge of a diver.
canbe10{_}906{_}Moxon tried to throw himself backward out of reach, but he was too late:  I saw the horrible thing's hands close upon his throat, his own clutch its wrists.
canbe10{_}907{_}Then the table was overturned, the candle thrown to the floor and extinguished, and all was black dark.
canbe10{_}908{_}But the noise of the struggle was dreadfully distinct, and most terrible of all were the raucous, squawking sounds made by the strangled man's efforts to breathe.
canbe10{_}909{_}Guided by the infernal hubbub, I sprang to the rescue of my friend, but had hardly taken a stride in the darkness when the whole room blazed with a blinding white light that burned into my brain and heart and memory a vivid picture of the combatants on the floor, Moxon underneath, his throat still in the clutch of those iron hands, his head forced backward, his eyes protruding, his mouth wide open and his tongue thrust out; and--horrible contrast!--upon the painted face of his assassin an expression of tranquil and profound thought, as in the solution of a problem in chess!
canbe10{_}910{_}This I observed, then all was blackness and silence.
canbe10{_}911{_}Three days later I recovered consciousness in a hospital.
canbe10{_}912{_}As the memory of that tragic night slowly evolved in my ailing brain recognized in my attendant Moxon's confidential workman, Haley.
canbe10{_}913{_}Responding to a look he approached, smiling.
canbe10{_}914{_}"Tell me about it," I managed to say, faintly--"all about it."
canbe10{_}915{_}"Certainly," he said; "you were carried unconscious from a burning house--Moxon's.
canbe10{_}916{_}Nobody knows how you came to be there.
canbe10{_}917{_}You may have to do a little explaining.
canbe10{_}918{_}The origin of the fire is a bit mysterious, too.
canbe10{_}919{_}My own notion is that the house was struck by lightning."
canbe10{_}920{_}"And Moxon?"
canbe10{_}921{_}"Buried yesterday--what was left of him."
canbe10{_}922{_}Apparently this reticent person could unfold himself on occasion.
canbe10{_}923{_}When imparting shocking intelligence to the sick he was affable enough.
canbe10{_}924{_}After some moments of the keenest mental suffering I ventured to ask another question:  "Who rescued me?"
canbe10{_}925{_}"Well, if that interests you--I did."
canbe10{_}926{_}"Thank you, Mr. Haley, and may God bless you for it.
canbe10{_}927{_}Did you rescue, also, that charming product of your skill, the automaton chess-player that murdered its inventor?"
canbe10{_}928{_}The man was silent a long time, looking away from me.
canbe10{_}929{_}Presently he turned and gravely said:  "Do you know that?"
canbe10{_}930{_}"I do," I replied; "I saw it done."
canbe10{_}931{_}That was many years ago.
canbe10{_}932{_}If asked to-day I should answer less confidently.
canbe10{_}933{_}A TOUGH TUSSLE    One night in the autumn of 1861 a man sat alone in the heart of a forest in western Virginia.
canbe10{_}934{_}The region was one of the wildest on the continent--the Cheat Mountain country.
canbe10{_}935{_}There was no lack of people close at hand, however; within a mile of where the man sat was the now silent camp of a whole Federal brigade.
canbe10{_}936{_}Somewhere about--it might be still nearer--was a force of the enemy, the numbers unknown.
canbe10{_}937{_}It was this uncertainty as to its numbers and position that accounted for the man's presence in that lonely spot; he was a young officer of a Federal infantry regiment and his business there was to guard his sleeping comrades in the camp against a surprise.
canbe10{_}938{_}He was in command of a detachment of men constituting a picket-guard.
canbe10{_}939{_}These men he had stationed just at nightfall in an irregular line, determined by the nature of the ground, several hundred yards in front of where he now sat.
canbe10{_}940{_}The line ran through the forest, among the rocks and laurel thickets, the men fifteen or twenty paces apart, all in concealment and under injunction of strict silence and unremitting vigilance.
canbe10{_}941{_}In four hours, if nothing occurred, they would be relieved by a fresh detachment from the reserve now resting in care of its captain some distance away to the left and rear.
canbe10{_}942{_}Before stationing his men the young officer of whom we are writing had pointed out to his two sergeants the spot at which he would be found if it should be necessary to consult him, or if his presence at the front line should be required.
canbe10{_}943{_}It was a quiet enough spot--the fork of an old wood-road, on the two branches of which, prolonging themselves deviously forward in the dim moonlight, the sergeants were themselves stationed, a few paces in rear of the line.
canbe10{_}944{_}If driven sharply back by a sudden onset of the enemy--and pickets are not expected to make a stand after firing--the men would come into the converging roads and naturally following them to their point of intersection could be rallied and "formed."
canbe10{_}945{_}In his small way the author of these dispositions was something of a strategist; if Napoleon had planned as intelligently at Waterloo he would have won that memorable battle and been overthrown later.
canbe10{_}946{_}Second-Lieutenant Brainerd Byring was a brave and efficient officer, young and comparatively inexperienced as he was in the business of killing his fellow-men.
canbe10{_}947{_}He had enlisted in the very first days of the war as a private, with no military knowledge whatever, had been made first-sergeant of his company on account of his education and engaging manner, and had been lucky enough to lose his captain by a Confederate bullet; in the resulting promotions he had gained a commission.
canbe10{_}948{_}He had been in several engagements, such as they were-- at Philippi, Rich Mountain, Carrick's Ford and Greenbrier--and had borne himself with such gallantry as not to attract the attention of his superior officers.
canbe10{_}949{_}The exhilaration of battle was agreeable to him, but the sight of the dead, with their clay faces, blank eyes and stiff bodies, which when not unnaturally shrunken were unnaturally swollen, had always intolerably affected him.
canbe10{_}950{_}He felt toward them a kind of reasonless antipathy that was something more than the physical and spiritual repugnance common to us all.
canbe10{_}951{_}Doubtless this feeling was due to his unusually acute sensibilities--his keen sense of the beautiful, which these hideous things outraged.
canbe10{_}952{_}Whatever may have been the cause, he could not look upon a dead body without a loathing which had in it an element of resentment.
canbe10{_}953{_}What others have respected as the dignity of death had to him no existence--was altogether unthinkable.
canbe10{_}954{_}Death was a thing to be hated.
canbe10{_}955{_}It was not picturesque, it had no tender and solemn side--a dismal thing, hideous in all its manifestations and suggestions.
canbe10{_}956{_}Lieutenant Byring was a braver man than anybody knew, for nobody knew his horror of that which he was ever ready to incur.
canbe10{_}957{_}Having posted his men, instructed his sergeants and retired to his station, he seated himself on a log, and with senses all alert began his vigil.
canbe10{_}958{_}For greater ease he loosened his sword-belt and taking his heavy revolver from his holster laid it on the log beside him.
canbe10{_}959{_}He felt very comfortable, though he hardly gave the fact a thought, so intently did he listen for any sound from the front which might have a menacing significance--a shout, a shot, or the footfall of one of his sergeants coming to apprise him of something worth knowing.
canbe10{_}960{_}From the vast, invisible ocean of moonlight overhead fell, here and there, a slender, broken stream that seemed to plash against the intercepting branches and trickle to earth, forming small white pools among the clumps of laurel.
canbe10{_}961{_}But these leaks were few and served only to accentuate the blackness of his environment, which his imagination found it easy to people with all manner of unfamiliar shapes, menacing, uncanny, or merely grotesque.
canbe10{_}962{_}He to whom the portentous conspiracy of night and solitude and silence in the heart of a great forest is not an unknown experience needs not to be told what another world it all is--how even the most commonplace and familiar objects take on another character.
canbe10{_}963{_}The trees group themselves differently; they draw closer together, as if in fear.
canbe10{_}964{_}The very silence has another quality than the silence of the day.
canbe10{_}965{_}And it is full of half-heard whispers--whispers that startle--ghosts of sounds long dead.
canbe10{_}966{_}There are living sounds, too, such as are never heard under other conditions:  notes of strange night-birds, the cries of small animals in sudden encounters with stealthy foes or in their dreams, a rustling in the dead leaves--it may be the leap of a wood-rat, it may be the footfall of a panther.
canbe10{_}967{_}What caused the breaking of that twig?--what the low, alarmed twittering in that bushful of birds?
canbe10{_}968{_}There are sounds without a name, forms without substance, translations in space of objects which have not been seen to move, movements wherein nothing is observed to change its place.
canbe10{_}969{_}Ah, children of the sunlight and the gaslight, how little you know of the world in which you live!
canbe10{_}970{_}Surrounded at a little distance by armed and watchful friends, Byring felt utterly alone.
canbe10{_}971{_}Yielding himself to the solemn and mysterious spirit of the time and place, he had forgotten the nature of his connection with the visible and audible aspects and phases of the night.
canbe10{_}972{_}The forest was boundless; men and the habitations of men did not exist.
canbe10{_}973{_}The universe was one primeval mystery of darkness, without form and void, himself the sole, dumb questioner of its eternal secret.
canbe10{_}974{_}Absorbed in thoughts born of this mood, he suffered the time to slip away unnoted.
canbe10{_}975{_}Meantime the infrequent patches of white light lying amongst the tree-trunks had undergone changes of size, form and place.
canbe10{_}976{_}In one of them near by, just at the roadside, his eye fell upon an object that he had not previously observed.
canbe10{_}977{_}It was almost before his face as he sat; he could have sworn that it had not before been there.
canbe10{_}978{_}It was partly covered in shadow, but he could see that it was a human figure.
canbe10{_}979{_}Instinctively he adjusted the clasp of his sword-belt and laid hold of his pistol--again he was in a world of war, by occupation an assassin.
canbe10{_}980{_}The figure did not move.
canbe10{_}981{_}Rising, pistol in hand, he approached.
canbe10{_}982{_}The figure lay upon its back, its upper part in shadow, but standing above it and looking down upon the face, he saw that it was a dead body.
canbe10{_}983{_}He shuddered and turned from it with a feeling of sickness and disgust, resumed his seat upon the log, and forgetting military prudence struck a match and lit a cigar.
canbe10{_}984{_}In the sudden blackness that followed the extinction of the flame he felt a sense of relief; he could no longer see the object of his aversion.
canbe10{_}985{_}Nevertheless, he kept his eyes set in that direction until it appeared again with growing distinctness.
canbe10{_}986{_}It seemed to have moved a trifle nearer.
canbe10{_}987{_}"Damn the thing!"
canbe10{_}988{_}he muttered.
canbe10{_}989{_}"What does it want?"
canbe10{_}990{_}It did not appear to be in need of anything but a soul.
canbe10{_}991{_}Byring turned away his eyes and began humming a tune, but he broke off in the middle of a bar and looked at the dead body.
canbe10{_}992{_}Its presence annoyed him, though he could hardly have had a quieter neighbor.
canbe10{_}993{_}He was conscious, too, of a vague, indefinable feeling that was new to him.
canbe10{_}994{_}It was not fear, but rather a sense of the supernatural--in which he did not at all believe.
canbe10{_}995{_}"I have inherited it," he said to himself.
canbe10{_}996{_}"I suppose it will require a thousand ages--perhaps ten thousand--for humanity to outgrow this feeling.
canbe10{_}997{_}Where and when did it originate?
canbe10{_}998{_}Away back, probably, in what is called the cradle of the human race--the plains of Central Asia.
canbe10{_}999{_}What we inherit as a superstition our barbarous ancestors must have held as a reasonable conviction.
canbe10{_}1000{_}Doubtless they believed themselves justified by facts whose nature we cannot even conjecture in thinking a dead body a malign thing endowed with some strange power of mischief, with perhaps a will and a purpose to exert it.
canbe10{_}1001{_}Possibly they had some awful form of religion of which that was one of the chief doctrines, sedulously taught by their priesthood, as ours teach the immortality of the soul.
canbe10{_}1002{_}As the Aryans moved slowly on, to and through the Caucasus passes, and spread over Europe, new conditions of life must have resulted in the formulation of new religions.
canbe10{_}1003{_}The old belief in the malevolence of the dead body was lost from the creeds and even perished from tradition, but it left its heritage of terror, which is transmitted from generation to generation--is as much a part of us as are our blood and bones."
canbe10{_}1004{_}In following out his thought he had forgotten that which suggested it; but now his eye fell again upon the corpse.
canbe10{_}1005{_}The shadow had now altogether uncovered it.
canbe10{_}1006{_}He saw the sharp profile, the chin in the air, the whole face, ghastly white in the moonlight.
canbe10{_}1007{_}The clothing was gray, the uniform of a Confederate soldier.
canbe10{_}1008{_}The coat and waistcoat, unbuttoned, had fallen away on each side, exposing the white shirt.
canbe10{_}1009{_}The chest seemed unnaturally prominent, but the abdomen had sunk in, leaving a sharp projection at the line of the lower ribs.
canbe10{_}1010{_}The arms were extended, the left knee was thrust upward.
canbe10{_}1011{_}The whole posture impressed Byring as having been studied with a view to the horrible.
canbe10{_}1012{_}"Bah!"
canbe10{_}1013{_}he exclaimed; "he was an actor--he knows how to be dead."
canbe10{_}1014{_}He drew away his eyes, directing them resolutely along one of the roads leading to the front, and resumed his philosophizing where he had left off.
canbe10{_}1015{_}"It may be that our Central Asian ancestors had not the custom of burial.
canbe10{_}1016{_}In that case it is easy to understand their fear of the dead, who really were a menace and an evil.
canbe10{_}1017{_}They bred pestilences.
canbe10{_}1018{_}Children were taught to avoid the places where they lay, and to run away if by inadvertence they came near a corpse.
canbe10{_}1019{_}I think, indeed, I'd better go away from this chap."
canbe10{_}1020{_}He half rose to do so, then remembered that he had told his men in front and the officer in the rear who was to relieve him that he could at any time be found at that spot.
canbe10{_}1021{_}It was a matter of pride, too.
canbe10{_}1022{_}If he abandoned his post he feared they would think he feared the corpse.
canbe10{_}1023{_}He was no coward and he was unwilling to incur anybody's ridicule.
canbe10{_}1024{_}So he again seated himself, and to prove his courage looked boldly at the body.
canbe10{_}1025{_}The right arm--the one farthest from him- -was now in shadow.
canbe10{_}1026{_}He could barely see the hand which, he had before observed, lay at the root of a clump of laurel.
canbe10{_}1027{_}There had been no change, a fact which gave him a certain comfort, he could not have said why.
canbe10{_}1028{_}He did not at once remove his eyes; that which we do not wish to see has a strange fascination, sometimes irresistible.
canbe10{_}1029{_}Of the woman who covers her eyes with her hands and looks between the fingers let it be said that the wits have dealt with her not altogether justly.
canbe10{_}1030{_}Byring suddenly became conscious of a pain in his right hand.
canbe10{_}1031{_}He withdrew his eyes from his enemy and looked at it.
canbe10{_}1032{_}He was grasping the hilt of his drawn sword so tightly that it hurt him.
canbe10{_}1033{_}He observed, too, that he was leaning forward in a strained attitude-- crouching like a gladiator ready to spring at the throat of an antagonist.
canbe10{_}1034{_}His teeth were clenched and he was breathing hard.
canbe10{_}1035{_}This matter was soon set right, and as his muscles relaxed and he drew a long breath he felt keenly enough the ludicrousness of the incident.
canbe10{_}1036{_}It affected him to laughter.
canbe10{_}1037{_}Heavens!
canbe10{_}1038{_}what sound was that?
canbe10{_}1039{_}what mindless devil was uttering an unholy glee in mockery of human merriment?
canbe10{_}1040{_}He sprang to his feet and looked about him, not recognizing his own laugh.

canbe10{_}1042{_}He would have run from the spot, but his legs refused their office; they gave way beneath him and he sat again upon the log, violently trembling.
canbe10{_}1043{_}His face was wet, his whole body bathed in a chill perspiration.
canbe10{_}1044{_}He could not even cry out.
canbe10{_}1045{_}Distinctly he heard behind him a stealthy tread, as of some wild animal, and dared not look over his shoulder.
canbe10{_}1046{_}Had the soulless living joined forces with the soulless dead?--was it an animal?
canbe10{_}1047{_}Ah, if he could but be assured of that!
canbe10{_}1048{_}But by no effort of will could he now unfix his gaze from the face of the dead man.
canbe10{_}1049{_}I repeat that Lieutenant Byring was a brave and intelligent man.
canbe10{_}1050{_}But what would you have?
canbe10{_}1051{_}Shall a man cope, single-handed, with so monstrous an alliance as that of night and solitude and silence and the dead,--while an incalculable host of his own ancestors shriek into the ear of his spirit their coward counsel, sing their doleful death-songs in his heart, and disarm his very blood of all its iron?
canbe10{_}1052{_}The odds are too great--courage was not made for so rough use as that.

canbe10{_}1058{_}The horrible thing was visibly moving!
canbe10{_}1059{_}At that moment a single shot rang out upon the picket-line--a lonelier and louder, though more distant, shot than ever had been heard by mortal ear!
canbe10{_}1060{_}It broke the spell of that enchanted man; it slew the silence and the solitude, dispersed the hindering host from Central Asia and released his modern manhood.

canbe10{_}1062{_}Shot after shot now came from the front.
canbe10{_}1063{_}There were shoutings and confusion, hoof-beats and desultory cheers.
canbe10{_}1064{_}Away to the rear, in the sleeping camp, were a singing of bugles and grumble of drums.
canbe10{_}1065{_}Pushing through the thickets on either side the roads came the Federal pickets, in full retreat, firing backward at random as they ran.

canbe10{_}1067{_}At headlong speed these mounted madmen shot past the spot where Byring had sat, and vanished round an angle of the road, shouting and firing their pistols.
canbe10{_}1068{_}A moment later there was a roar of musketry, followed by dropping shots--they had encountered the reserve-guard in line; and back they came in dire confusion, with here and there an empty saddle and many a maddened horse, bullet- stung, snorting and plunging with pain.
canbe10{_}1069{_}It was all over--"an affair of outposts."

canbe10{_}1093{_}ONE OF TWINS A LETTER FOUND AMONG THE PAPERS OF THE LATE MORTIMER BARR    You ask me if in my experience as one of a pair of twins I ever observed anything unaccountable by the natural laws with which we have acquaintance.
canbe10{_}1094{_}As to that you shall judge; perhaps we have not all acquaintance with the same natural laws.
canbe10{_}1095{_}You may know some that I do not, and what is to me unaccountable may be very clear to you.
canbe10{_}1096{_}You knew my brother John--that is, you knew him when you knew that I was not present; but neither you nor, I believe, any human being could distinguish between him and me if we chose to seem alike.
canbe10{_}1097{_}Our parents could not; ours is the only instance of which I have any knowledge of so close resemblance as that.
canbe10{_}1098{_}I speak of my brother John, but I am not at all sure that his name was not Henry and mine John.
canbe10{_}1099{_}We were regularly christened, but afterward, in the very act of tattooing us with small distinguishing marks, the operator lost his reckoning; and although I bear upon my forearm a small "H" and he bore a "J," it is by no means certain that the letters ought not to have been transposed.
canbe10{_}1100{_}During our boyhood our parents tried to distinguish us more obviously by our clothing and other simple devices, but we would so frequently exchange suits and otherwise circumvent the enemy that they abandoned all such ineffectual attempts, and during all the years that we lived together at home everybody recognized the difficulty of the situation and made the best of it by calling us both "Jehnry."
canbe10{_}1101{_}I have often wondered at my father's forbearance in not branding us conspicuously upon our unworthy brows, but as we were tolerably good boys and used our power of embarrassment and annoyance with commendable moderation, we escaped the iron.
canbe10{_}1102{_}My father was, in fact, a singularly good-natured man, and I think quietly enjoyed nature's practical joke.
canbe10{_}1103{_}Soon after we had come to California, and settled at San Jose (where the only good fortune that awaited us was our meeting with so kind a friend as you) the family, as you know, was broken up by the death of both my parents in the same week.
canbe10{_}1104{_}My father died insolvent and the homestead was sacrificed to pay his debts.
canbe10{_}1105{_}My sisters returned to relatives in the East, but owing to your kindness John and I, then twenty-two years of age, obtained employment in San Francisco, in different quarters of the town.
canbe10{_}1106{_}Circumstances did not permit us to live together, and we saw each other infrequently, sometimes not oftener than once a week.
canbe10{_}1107{_}As we had few acquaintances in common, the fact of our extraordinary likeness was little known.
canbe10{_}1108{_}I come now to the matter of your inquiry.
canbe10{_}1109{_}One day soon after we had come to this city I was walking down Market street late in the afternoon, when I was accosted by a well-dressed man of middle age, who after greeting me cordially said:  "Stevens, I know, of course, that you do not go out much, but I have told my wife about you, and she would be glad to see you at the house.
canbe10{_}1110{_}I have a notion, too, that my girls are worth knowing.
canbe10{_}1111{_}Suppose you come out to-morrow at six and dine with us, en famille; and then if the ladies can't amuse you afterward I'll stand in with a few games of billiards."
canbe10{_}1112{_}This was said with so bright a smile and so engaging a manner that I had not the heart to refuse, and although I had never seen the man in my life I promptly replied:  "You are very good, sir, and it will give me great pleasure to accept the invitation.
canbe10{_}1113{_}Please present my compliments to Mrs. Margovan and ask her to expect me."
canbe10{_}1114{_}With a shake of the hand and a pleasant parting word the man passed on.
canbe10{_}1115{_}That he had mistaken me for my brother was plain enough.
canbe10{_}1116{_}That was an error to which I was accustomed and which it was not my habit to rectify unless the matter seemed important.
canbe10{_}1117{_}But how had I known that this man's name was Margovan?

canbe10{_}1119{_}In point of fact, the name was as strange to me as the man.
canbe10{_}1120{_}The next morning I hastened to where my brother was employed and met him coming out of the office with a number of bills that he was to collect.
canbe10{_}1121{_}I told him how I had "committed" him and added that if he didn't care to keep the engagement I should be delighted to continue the impersonation.
canbe10{_}1122{_}"That's queer," he said thoughtfully.
canbe10{_}1123{_}"Margovan is the only man in the office here whom I know well and like.

canbe10{_}1125{_}I got the address, but what under the sun I was to do with it, I did not know until now.

canbe10{_}1127{_}He ate a number of dinners at the same place--more than were good for him, I may add without disparaging their quality; for he fell in love with Miss Margovan, proposed marriage to her and was heartlessly accepted.

canbe10{_}1212{_}THE HAUNTED VALLEY    I--HOW TREES ARE FELLED IN CHINA  A half-mile north from Jo.
canbe10{_}1213{_}Dunfer's, on the road from Hutton's to Mexican Hill, the highway dips into a sunless ravine which opens out on either hand in a half-confidential manner, as if it had a secret to impart at some more convenient season.
canbe10{_}1214{_}I never used to ride through it without looking first to the one side and then to the other, to see if the time had arrived for the revelation.
canbe10{_}1215{_}If I saw nothing--and I never did see anything--there was no feeling of disappointment, for I knew the disclosure was merely withheld temporarily for some good reason which I had no right to question.
canbe10{_}1216{_}That I should one day be taken into full confidence I no more doubted than I doubted the existence of Jo.
canbe10{_}1217{_}Dunfer himself, through whose premises the ravine ran.
canbe10{_}1218{_}It was said that Jo.
canbe10{_}1219{_}had once undertaken to erect a cabin in some remote part of it, but for some reason had abandoned the enterprise and constructed his present hermaphrodite habitation, half residence and half groggery, at the roadside, upon an extreme corner of his estate; as far away as possible, as if on purpose to show how radically he had changed his mind.
canbe10{_}1220{_}This Jo.
canbe10{_}1221{_}Dunfer--or, as he was familiarly known in the neighborhood, Whisky Jo.--was a very important personage in those parts.
canbe10{_}1222{_}He was apparently about forty years of age, a long, shock-headed fellow, with a corded face, a gnarled arm and a knotty hand like a bunch of prison-keys.
canbe10{_}1223{_}He was a hairy man, with a stoop in his walk, like that of one who is about to spring upon something and rend it.
canbe10{_}1224{_}Next to the peculiarity to which he owed his local appellation, Mr. Dunfer's most obvious characteristic was a deep-seated antipathy to the Chinese.
canbe10{_}1225{_}I saw him once in a towering rage because one of his herdsmen had permitted a travel-heated Asian to slake his thirst at the horse-trough in front of the saloon end of Jo.
canbe10{_}1226{_}'s establishment.
canbe10{_}1227{_}I ventured faintly to remonstrate with Jo.
canbe10{_}1228{_}for his unchristian spirit, but he merely explained that there was nothing about Chinamen in the New Testament, and strode away to wreak his displeasure upon his dog, which also, I suppose, the inspired scribes had overlooked.
canbe10{_}1229{_}Some days afterward, finding him sitting alone in his barroom, I cautiously approached the subject, when, greatly to my relief, the habitual austerity of his expression visibly softened into something that I took for condescension.
canbe10{_}1230{_}"You young Easterners," he said, "are a mile-and-a-half too good for this country, and you don't catch on to our play.
canbe10{_}1231{_}People who don't know a Chileno from a Kanaka can afford to hang out liberal ideas about Chinese immigration, but a fellow that has to fight for his bone with a lot of mongrel coolies hasn't any time for foolishness."
canbe10{_}1232{_}This long consumer, who had probably never done an honest day's-work in his life, sprung the lid of a Chinese tobacco-box and with thumb and forefinger forked out a wad like a small haycock.
canbe10{_}1233{_}Holding this reinforcement within supporting distance he fired away with renewed confidence.
canbe10{_}1234{_}"They're a flight of devouring locusts, and they're going for everything green in this God blest land, if you want to know."

canbe10{_}1236{_}"I had one of them on this ranch five years ago, and I'll tell you about it, so that you can see the nub of this whole question.
canbe10{_}1237{_}I didn't pan out particularly well those days--drank more whisky than was prescribed for me and didn't seem to care for my duty as a patriotic American citizen; so I took that pagan in, as a kind of cook.
canbe10{_}1238{_}But when I got religion over at the Hill and they talked of running me for the Legislature it was given to me to see the light.
canbe10{_}1239{_}But what was I to do?
canbe10{_}1240{_}If I gave him the go somebody else would take him, and mightn't treat him white.
canbe10{_}1241{_}WHAT was I to do?
canbe10{_}1242{_}What would any good Christian do, especially one new to the trade and full to the neck with the brotherhood of Man and the fatherhood of God?"
canbe10{_}1243{_}Jo.
canbe10{_}1244{_}paused for a reply, with an expression of unstable satisfaction, as of one who has solved a problem by a distrusted method.
canbe10{_}1245{_}Presently he rose and swallowed a glass of whisky from a full bottle on the counter, then resumed his story.
canbe10{_}1246{_}"Besides, he didn't count for much--didn't know anything and gave himself airs.
canbe10{_}1247{_}They all do that.
canbe10{_}1248{_}I said him nay, but he muled it through on that line while he lasted; but after turning the other cheek seventy and seven times I doctored the dice so that he didn't last forever.
canbe10{_}1249{_}And I'm almighty glad I had the sand to do it.
canbe10{_}1250{_}Jo.
canbe10{_}1251{_}'s gladness, which somehow did not impress me, was duly and ostentatiously celebrated at the bottle.
canbe10{_}1252{_}"About five years ago I started in to stick up a shack.
canbe10{_}1253{_}That was before this one was built, and I put it in another place.
canbe10{_}1254{_}I set Ah Wee and a little cuss named Gopher to cutting the timber.
canbe10{_}1255{_}Of course I didn't expect Ah Wee to help much, for he had a face like a day in June and big black eyes--I guess maybe they were the damn'dest eyes in this neck o' woods."
canbe10{_}1256{_}While delivering this trenchant thrust at common sense Mr. Dunfer absently regarded a knot-hole in the thin board partition separating the bar from the living-room, as if that were one of the eyes whose size and color had incapacitated his servant for good service.
canbe10{_}1257{_}"Now you Eastern galoots won't believe anything against the yellow devils," he suddenly flamed out with an appearance of earnestness not altogether convincing, "but I tell you that Chink was the perversest scoundrel outside San Francisco.
canbe10{_}1258{_}The miserable pigtail Mongolian went to hewing away at the saplings all round the stems, like a worm o' the dust gnawing a radish.
canbe10{_}1259{_}I pointed out his error as patiently as I knew how, and showed him how to cut them on two sides, so as to make them fall right; but no sooner would I turn my back on him, like this"--and he turned it on me, amplifying the illustration by taking some more liquor--"than he was at it again.
canbe10{_}1260{_}It was just this way: while I looked at him, SO"--regarding me rather unsteadily and with evident complexity of vision--"he was all right; but when I looked away, SO"--taking a long pull at the bottle--"he defied me.
canbe10{_}1261{_}Then I'd gaze at him reproachfully, SO, and butter wouldn't have melted in his mouth."
canbe10{_}1262{_}Doubtless Mr. Dunfer honestly intended the look that he fixed upon me to be merely reproachful, but it was singularly fit to arouse the gravest apprehension in any unarmed person incurring it; and as I had lost all interest in his pointless and interminable narrative, I rose to go.
canbe10{_}1263{_}Before I had fairly risen, he had again turned to the counter, and with a barely audible "so," had emptied the bottle at a gulp.
canbe10{_}1264{_}Heavens!
canbe10{_}1265{_}what a yell!
canbe10{_}1266{_}It was like a Titan in his last, strong agony.
canbe10{_}1267{_}Jo.
canbe10{_}1268{_}staggered back after emitting it, as a cannon recoils from its own thunder, and then dropped into his chair, as if he had been "knocked in the head" like a beef--his eyes drawn sidewise toward the wall, with a stare of terror.
canbe10{_}1269{_}Looking in the same direction, I saw that the knot-hole in the wall had indeed become a human eye--a full, black eye, that glared into my own with an entire lack of expression more awful than the most devilish glitter.
canbe10{_}1270{_}I think I must have covered my face with my hands to shut out the horrible illusion, if such it was, and Jo.
canbe10{_}1271{_}'s little white man-of-all-work coming into the room broke the spell, and I walked out of the house with a sort of dazed fear that delirium tremens might be infectious.
canbe10{_}1272{_}My horse was hitched at the watering-trough, and untying him I mounted and gave him his head, too much troubled in mind to note whither he took me.
canbe10{_}1273{_}I did not know what to think of all this, and like every one who does not know what to think I thought a great deal, and to little purpose.
canbe10{_}1274{_}The only reflection that seemed at all satisfactory, was, that on the morrow I should be some miles away, with a strong probability of never returning.
canbe10{_}1275{_}A sudden coolness brought me out of my abstraction, and looking up I found myself entering the deep shadows of the ravine.
canbe10{_}1276{_}The day was stifling; and this transition from the pitiless, visible heat of the parched fields to the cool gloom, heavy with pungency of cedars and vocal with twittering of the birds that had been driven to its leafy asylum, was exquisitely refreshing.
canbe10{_}1277{_}I looked for my mystery, as usual, but not finding the ravine in a communicative mood, dismounted, led my sweating animal into the undergrowth, tied him securely to a tree and sat down upon a rock to meditate.
canbe10{_}1278{_}I began bravely by analyzing my pet superstition about the place.
canbe10{_}1279{_}Having resolved it into its constituent elements I arranged them in convenient troops and squadrons, and collecting all the forces of my logic bore down upon them from impregnable premises with the thunder of irresistible conclusions and a great noise of chariots and general intellectual shouting.
canbe10{_}1280{_}Then, when my big mental guns had overturned all opposition, and were growling almost inaudibly away on the horizon of pure speculation, the routed enemy straggled in upon their rear, massed silently into a solid phalanx, and captured me, bag and baggage.
canbe10{_}1281{_}An indefinable dread came upon me.
canbe10{_}1282{_}I rose to shake it off, and began threading the narrow dell by an old, grass-grown cow-path that seemed to flow along the bottom, as a substitute for the brook that Nature had neglected to provide.
canbe10{_}1283{_}The trees among which the path straggled were ordinary, well-behaved plants, a trifle perverted as to trunk and eccentric as to bough, but with nothing unearthly in their general aspect.
canbe10{_}1284{_}A few loose bowlders, which had detached themselves from the sides of the depression to set up an independent existence at the bottom, had dammed up the pathway, here and there, but their stony repose had nothing in it of the stillness of death.
canbe10{_}1285{_}There was a kind of death- chamber hush in the valley, it is true, and a mysterious whisper above:  the wind was just fingering the tops of the trees--that was all.
canbe10{_}1286{_}I had not thought of connecting Jo.
canbe10{_}1287{_}Dunfer's drunken narrative with what I now sought, and only when I came into a clear space and stumbled over the level trunks of some small trees did I have the revelation.
canbe10{_}1288{_}This was the site of the abandoned "shack."
canbe10{_}1289{_}The discovery was verified by noting that some of the rotting stumps were hacked all round, in a most unwoodmanlike way, while others were cut straight across, and the butt ends of the corresponding trunks had the blunt wedge-form given by the axe of a master.
canbe10{_}1290{_}The opening among the trees was not more than thirty paces across.
canbe10{_}1291{_}At one side was a little knoll--a natural hillock, bare of shrubbery but covered with wild grass, and on this, standing out of the grass, the headstone of a grave!
canbe10{_}1292{_}I do not remember that I felt anything like surprise at this discovery.
canbe10{_}1293{_}I viewed that lonely grave with something of the feeling that Columbus must have had when he saw the hills and headlands of the new world.
canbe10{_}1294{_}Before approaching it I leisurely completed my survey of the surroundings.
canbe10{_}1295{_}I was even guilty of the affectation of winding my watch at that unusual hour, and with needless care and deliberation.
canbe10{_}1296{_}Then I approached my mystery.
canbe10{_}1297{_}The grave--a rather short one--was in somewhat better repair than was consistent with its obvious age and isolation, and my eyes, I dare say, widened a trifle at a clump of unmistakable garden flowers showing evidence of recent watering.
canbe10{_}1298{_}The stone had clearly enough done duty once as a doorstep.
canbe10{_}1299{_}In its front was carved, or rather dug, an inscription.

canbe10{_}1302{_}Worked for Jo.
canbe10{_}1303{_}Dunfer.
canbe10{_}1304{_}This monument is erected by him to keep the Chink's memory green.
canbe10{_}1305{_}Likewise as a warning to Celestials not to take on airs.
canbe10{_}1306{_}Devil take 'em!
canbe10{_}1307{_}She Was a Good Egg.

canbe10{_}1309{_}The meagre but sufficient identification of the deceased; the impudent candor of confession; the brutal anathema; the ludicrous change of sex and sentiment--all marked this record as the work of one who must have been at least as much demented as bereaved.
canbe10{_}1310{_}I felt that any further disclosure would be a paltry anti-climax, and with an unconscious regard for dramatic effect turned squarely about and walked away.
canbe10{_}1311{_}Nor did I return to that part of the county for four years.
canbe10{_}1312{_}II--WHO DRIVES SANE OXEN SHOULD HIMSELF BE SANE   "Gee-up, there, old Fuddy-Duddy!"
canbe10{_}1313{_}This unique adjuration came from the lips of a queer little man perched upon a wagonful of firewood, behind a brace of oxen that were hauling it easily along with a simulation of mighty effort which had evidently not imposed on their lord and master.
canbe10{_}1314{_}As that gentleman happened at the moment to be staring me squarely in the face as I stood by the roadside it was not altogether clear whether he was addressing me or his beasts; nor could I say if they were named Fuddy and Duddy and were both subjects of the imperative verb "to gee-up."
canbe10{_}1315{_}Anyhow the command produced no effect on us, and the queer little man removed his eyes from mine long enough to spear Fuddy and Duddy alternately with a long pole, remarking, quietly but with feeling: "Dern your skin," as if they enjoyed that integument in common.
canbe10{_}1316{_}Observing that my request for a ride took no attention, and finding myself falling slowly astern, I placed one foot upon the inner circumference of a hind wheel and was slowly elevated to the level of the hub, whence I boarded the concern, sans ceremonie, and scrambling forward seated myself beside the driver--who took no notice of me until he had administered another indiscriminate castigation to his cattle, accompanied with the advice to "buckle down, you derned Incapable!"
canbe10{_}1317{_}Then, the master of the outfit (or rather the former master, for I could not suppress a whimsical feeling that the entire establishment was my lawful prize) trained his big, black eyes upon me with an expression strangely, and somewhat unpleasantly, familiar, laid down his rod--which neither blossomed nor turned into a serpent, as I half expected--folded his arms, and gravely demanded, "W'at did you do to W'isky?"
canbe10{_}1318{_}My natural reply would have been that I drank it, but there was something about the query that suggested a hidden significance, and something about the man that did not invite a shallow jest.
canbe10{_}1319{_}And so, having no other answer ready, I merely held my tongue, but felt as if I were resting under an imputation of guilt, and that my silence was being construed into a confession.
canbe10{_}1320{_}Just then a cold shadow fell upon my cheek, and caused me to look up.
canbe10{_}1321{_}We were descending into my ravine!
canbe10{_}1322{_}I cannot describe the sensation that came upon me:  I had not seen it since it unbosomed itself four years before, and now I felt like one to whom a friend has made some sorrowing confession of crime long past, and who has basely deserted him in consequence.
canbe10{_}1323{_}The old memories of Jo.
canbe10{_}1324{_}Dunfer, his fragmentary revelation, and the unsatisfying explanatory note by the headstone, came back with singular distinctness.
canbe10{_}1325{_}I wondered what had become of Jo., and--I turned sharply round and asked my prisoner.
canbe10{_}1326{_}He was intently watching his cattle, and without withdrawing his eyes replied:  "Gee-up, old Terrapin!
canbe10{_}1327{_}He lies aside of Ah Wee up the gulch.
canbe10{_}1328{_}Like to see it?
canbe10{_}1329{_}They always come back to the spot--I've been expectin' you.
canbe10{_}1330{_}H-woa!"
canbe10{_}1331{_}At the enunciation of the aspirate, Fuddy-Duddy, the incapable terrapin, came to a dead halt, and before the vowel had died away up the ravine had folded up all his eight legs and lain down in the dusty road, regardless of the effect upon his derned skin.
canbe10{_}1332{_}The queer little man slid off his seat to the ground and started up the dell without deigning to look back to see if I was following.
canbe10{_}1333{_}But I was.
canbe10{_}1334{_}It was about the same season of the year, and at near the same hour of the day, of my last visit.

canbe10{_}1340{_}It was as if the Old-World barbarism and the New-World civilization had reconciled their differences by the arbitration of an impartial decay--as is the way of civilizations.
canbe10{_}1341{_}The knoll was there, but the Hunnish brambles had overrun and all but obliterated its effete grasses; and the patrician garden-violet had capitulated to his plebeian brother--perhaps had merely reverted to his original type.

canbe10{_}1345{_}DONE FOR.
canbe10{_}1346{_}I turned from it with indifference, and brushing away the leaves from the tablet of the dead pagan restored to light the mocking words which, fresh from their long neglect, seemed to have a certain pathos.

canbe10{_}1350{_}"My friend," I said, pointing to the smaller grave, "did Jo.

canbe10{_}1352{_}He was leaning against a tree and looking across the open space into the top of another, or into the blue sky beyond.

canbe10{_}1357{_}Doesn't everybody know that?
