canbe10{_}1410{_}A JUG OF SIRUP    This narrative begins with the death of its hero.
canbe10{_}1411{_}Silas Deemer died on the 16th day of July, 1863, and two days later his remains were buried.
canbe10{_}1412{_}As he had been personally known to every man, woman and well-grown child in the village, the funeral, as the local newspaper phrased it, "was largely attended."
canbe10{_}1413{_}In accordance with a custom of the time and place, the coffin was opened at the graveside and the entire assembly of friends and neighbors filed past, taking a last look at the face of the dead.
canbe10{_}1414{_}And then, before the eyes of all, Silas Deemer was put into the ground.
canbe10{_}1415{_}Some of the eyes were a trifle dim, but in a general way it may be said that at that interment there was lack of neither observance nor observation; Silas was indubitably dead, and none could have pointed out any ritual delinquency that would have justified him in coming back from the grave.
canbe10{_}1416{_}Yet if human testimony is good for anything (and certainly it once put an end to witchcraft in and about Salem) he came back.
canbe10{_}1417{_}I forgot to state that the death and burial of Silas Deemer occurred in the little village of Hillbrook, where he had lived for thirty-one years.
canbe10{_}1418{_}He had been what is known in some parts of the Union (which is admittedly a free country) as a "merchant"; that is to say, he kept a retail shop for the sale of such things as are commonly sold in shops of that character.
canbe10{_}1419{_}His honesty had never been questioned, so far as is known, and he was held in high esteem by all.
canbe10{_}1420{_}The only thing that could be urged against him by the most censorious was a too close attention to business.
canbe10{_}1421{_}It was not urged against him, though many another, who manifested it in no greater degree, was less leniently judged.
canbe10{_}1422{_}The business to which Silas was devoted was mostly his own--that, possibly, may have made a difference.
canbe10{_}1423{_}At the time of Deemer's death nobody could recollect a single day, Sundays excepted, that he had not passed in his "store," since he had opened it more than a quarter-century before.
canbe10{_}1424{_}His health having been perfect during all that time, he had been unable to discern any validity in whatever may or might have been urged to lure him astray from his counter and it is related that once when he was summoned to the county seat as a witness in an important law case and did not attend, the lawyer who had the hardihood to move that he be "admonished" was solemnly informed that the Court regarded the proposal with "surprise."
canbe10{_}1425{_}Judicial surprise being an emotion that attorneys are not commonly ambitious to arouse, the motion was hastily withdrawn and an agreement with the other side effected as to what Mr. Deemer would have said if he had been there--the other side pushing its advantage to the extreme and making the supposititious testimony distinctly damaging to the interests of its proponents.
canbe10{_}1426{_}In brief, it was the general feeling in all that region that Silas Deemer was the one immobile verity of Hillbrook, and that his translation in space would precipitate some dismal public ill or strenuous calamity.
canbe10{_}1427{_}Mrs. Deemer and two grown daughters occupied the upper rooms of the building, but Silas had never been known to sleep elsewhere than on a cot behind the counter of the store.
canbe10{_}1428{_}And there, quite by accident, he was found one night, dying, and passed away just before the time for taking down the shutters.
canbe10{_}1429{_}Though speechless, he appeared conscious, and it was thought by those who knew him best that if the end had unfortunately been delayed beyond the usual hour for opening the store the effect upon him would have been deplorable.
canbe10{_}1430{_}Such had been Silas Deemer--such the fixity and invariety of his life and habit, that the village humorist (who had once attended college) was moved to bestow upon him the sobriquet of "Old Ibidem," and, in the first issue of the local newspaper after the death, to explain without offence that Silas had taken "a day off."
canbe10{_}1431{_}It was more than a day, but from the record it appears that well within a month Mr. Deemer made it plain that he had not the leisure to be dead.
canbe10{_}1432{_}One of Hillbrook's most respected citizens was Alvan Creede, a banker.
canbe10{_}1433{_}He lived in the finest house in town, kept a carriage and was a most estimable man variously.
canbe10{_}1434{_}He knew something of the advantages of travel, too, having been frequently in Boston, and once, it was thought, in New York, though he modestly disclaimed that glittering distinction.
canbe10{_}1435{_}The matter is mentioned here merely as a contribution to an understanding of Mr. Creede's worth, for either way it is creditable to him--to his intelligence if he had put himself, even temporarily, into contact with metropolitan culture; to his candor if he had not.
canbe10{_}1436{_}One pleasant summer evening at about the hour of ten Mr. Creede, entering at his garden gate, passed up the gravel walk, which looked very white in the moonlight, mounted the stone steps of his fine house and pausing a moment inserted his latchkey in the door.
canbe10{_}1437{_}As he pushed this open he met his wife, who was crossing the passage from the parlor to the library.
canbe10{_}1438{_}She greeted him pleasantly and pulling the door further back held it for him to enter.
canbe10{_}1439{_}Instead he turned and, looking about his feet in front of the threshold, uttered an exclamation of surprise.
canbe10{_}1440{_}"Why!--what the devil," he said, "has become of that jug?"
canbe10{_}1441{_}"What jug, Alvan?"
canbe10{_}1442{_}his wife inquired, not very sympathetically.
canbe10{_}1443{_}"A jug of maple sirup--I brought it along from the store and set it down here to open the door.
canbe10{_}1444{_}What the--"  "There, there, Alvan, please don't swear again," said the lady, interrupting.
canbe10{_}1445{_}Hillbrook, by the way, is not the only place in Christendom where a vestigial polytheism forbids the taking in vain of the Evil One's name.
canbe10{_}1446{_}The jug of maple sirup which the easy ways of village life had permitted Hillbrook's foremost citizen to carry home from the store was not there.
canbe10{_}1447{_}"Are you quite sure, Alvan?"
canbe10{_}1448{_}"My dear, do you suppose a man does not know when he is carrying a jug?
canbe10{_}1449{_}I bought that sirup at Deemer's as I was passing.
canbe10{_}1450{_}Deemer himself drew it and lent me the jug, and I--"  The sentence remains to this day unfinished.
canbe10{_}1451{_}Mr. Creede staggered into the house, entered the parlor and dropped into an armchair, trembling in every limb.
canbe10{_}1452{_}He had suddenly remembered that Silas Deemer was three weeks dead.
canbe10{_}1453{_}Mrs. Creede stood by her husband, regarding him with surprise and anxiety.
canbe10{_}1454{_}"For Heaven's sake," she said, "what ails you?"
canbe10{_}1455{_}Mr. Creede's ailment having no obvious relation to the interests of the better land he did not apparently deem it necessary to expound it on that demand; he said nothing--merely stared.
canbe10{_}1456{_}There were long moments of silence broken by nothing but the measured ticking of the clock, which seemed somewhat slower than usual, as if it were civilly granting them an extension of time in which to recover their wits.
canbe10{_}1457{_}"Jane, I have gone mad--that is it."
canbe10{_}1458{_}He spoke thickly and hurriedly.
canbe10{_}1459{_}"You should have told me; you must have observed my symptoms before they became so pronounced that I have observed them myself.
canbe10{_}1460{_}I thought I was passing Deemer's store; it was open and lit up--that is what I thought; of course it is never open now.
canbe10{_}1461{_}Silas Deemer stood at his desk behind the counter.
canbe10{_}1462{_}My God, Jane, I saw him as distinctly as I see you.
canbe10{_}1463{_}Remembering that you had said you wanted some maple sirup, I went in and bought some--that is all--I bought two quarts of maple sirup from Silas Deemer, who is dead and underground, but nevertheless drew that sirup from a cask and handed it to me in a jug.
canbe10{_}1464{_}He talked with me, too, rather gravely, I remember, even more so than was his way, but not a word of what he said can I now recall.
canbe10{_}1465{_}But I saw him--good Lord, I saw and talked with him--and he is dead!
canbe10{_}1466{_}So I thought, but I'm mad, Jane, I'm as crazy as a beetle; and you have kept it from me."
canbe10{_}1467{_}This monologue gave the woman time to collect what faculties she had.
canbe10{_}1468{_}"Alvan," she said, "you have given no evidence of insanity, believe me.
canbe10{_}1469{_}This was undoubtedly an illusion--how should it be anything else?
canbe10{_}1470{_}That would be too terrible!
canbe10{_}1471{_}But there is no insanity; you are working too hard at the bank.
canbe10{_}1472{_}You should not have attended the meeting of directors this evening; any one could see that you were ill; I knew something would occur."
canbe10{_}1473{_}It may have seemed to him that the prophecy had lagged a bit, awaiting the event, but he said nothing of that, being concerned with his own condition.
canbe10{_}1474{_}He was calm now, and could think coherently.
canbe10{_}1475{_}"Doubtless the phenomenon was subjective," he said, with a somewhat ludicrous transition to the slang of science.
canbe10{_}1476{_}"Granting the possibility of spiritual apparition and even materialization, yet the apparition and materialization of a half-gallon brown clay jug--a piece of coarse, heavy pottery evolved from nothing--that is hardly thinkable."
canbe10{_}1477{_}As he finished speaking, a child ran into the room--his little daughter.
canbe10{_}1478{_}She was clad in a bedgown.
canbe10{_}1479{_}Hastening to her father she threw her arms about his neck, saying:  "You naughty papa, you forgot to come in and kiss me.
canbe10{_}1480{_}We heard you open the gate and got up and looked out.
canbe10{_}1481{_}And, papa dear, Eddy says mayn't he have the little jug when it is empty?"
canbe10{_}1482{_}As the full import of that revelation imparted itself to Alvan Creede's understanding he visibly shuddered.
canbe10{_}1483{_}For the child could not have heard a word of the conversation.
canbe10{_}1484{_}The estate of Silas Deemer being in the hands of an administrator who had thought it best to dispose of the "business" the store had been closed ever since the owner's death, the goods having been removed by another "merchant" who had purchased them en bloc.
canbe10{_}1485{_}The rooms above were vacant as well, for the widow and daughters had gone to another town.
canbe10{_}1486{_}On the evening immediately after Alvan Creede's adventure (which had somehow "got out") a crowd of men, women and children thronged the sidewalk opposite the store.
canbe10{_}1487{_}That the place was haunted by the spirit of the late Silas Deemer was now well known to every resident of Hillbrook, though many affected disbelief.
canbe10{_}1488{_}Of these the hardiest, and in a general way the youngest, threw stones against the front of the building, the only part accessible, but carefully missed the unshuttered windows.
canbe10{_}1489{_}Incredulity had not grown to malice.
canbe10{_}1490{_}A few venturesome souls crossed the street and rattled the door in its frame; struck matches and held them near the window; attempted to view the black interior.
canbe10{_}1491{_}Some of the spectators invited attention to their wit by shouting and groaning and challenging the ghost to a footrace.
canbe10{_}1492{_}After a considerable time had elapsed without any manifestation, and many of the crowd had gone away, all those remaining began to observe that the interior of the store was suffused with a dim, yellow light.
canbe10{_}1493{_}At this all demonstrations ceased; the intrepid souls about the door and windows fell back to the opposite side of the street and were merged in the crowd; the small boys ceased throwing stones.
canbe10{_}1494{_}Nobody spoke above his breath; all whispered excitedly and pointed to the now steadily growing light.
canbe10{_}1495{_}How long a time had passed since the first faint glow had been observed none could have guessed, but eventually the illumination was bright enough to reveal the whole interior of the store; and there, standing at his desk behind the counter, Silas Deemer was distinctly visible!
canbe10{_}1496{_}The effect upon the crowd was marvelous.
canbe10{_}1497{_}It began rapidly to melt away at both flanks, as the timid left the place.
canbe10{_}1498{_}Many ran as fast as their legs would let them; others moved off with greater dignity, turning occasionally to look backward over the shoulder.
canbe10{_}1499{_}At last a score or more, mostly men, remained where they were, speechless, staring, excited.
canbe10{_}1500{_}The apparition inside gave them no attention; it was apparently occupied with a book of accounts.
canbe10{_}1501{_}Presently three men left the crowd on the sidewalk as if by a common impulse and crossed the street.
canbe10{_}1502{_}One of them, a heavy man, was about to set his shoulder against the door when it opened, apparently without human agency, and the courageous investigators passed in.
canbe10{_}1503{_}No sooner had they crossed the threshold than they were seen by the awed observers outside to be acting in the most unaccountable way.
canbe10{_}1504{_}They thrust out their hands before them, pursued devious courses, came into violent collision with the counter, with boxes and barrels on the floor, and with one another.
canbe10{_}1505{_}They turned awkwardly hither and thither and seemed trying to escape, but unable to retrace their steps.
canbe10{_}1506{_}Their voices were heard in exclamations and curses.
canbe10{_}1507{_}But in no way did the apparition of Silas Deemer manifest an interest in what was going on.
canbe10{_}1508{_}By what impulse the crowd was moved none ever recollected, but the entire mass--men, women, children, dogs--made a simultaneous and tumultuous rush for the entrance.
canbe10{_}1509{_}They congested the doorway, pushing for precedence--resolving themselves at length into a line and moving up step by step.
canbe10{_}1510{_}By some subtle spiritual or physical alchemy observation had been transmuted into action--the sightseers had become participants in the spectacle--the audience had usurped the stage.
canbe10{_}1511{_}To the only spectator remaining on the other side of the street-- Alvan Creede, the banker--the interior of the store with its inpouring crowd continued in full illumination; all the strange things going on there were clearly visible.
canbe10{_}1512{_}To those inside all was black darkness.
canbe10{_}1513{_}It was as if each person as he was thrust in at the door had been stricken blind, and was maddened by the mischance.
canbe10{_}1514{_}They groped with aimless imprecision, tried to force their way out against the current, pushed and elbowed, struck at random, fell and were trampled, rose and trampled in their turn.
canbe10{_}1515{_}They seized one another by the garments, the hair, the beard--fought like animals, cursed, shouted, called one another opprobrious and obscene names.
canbe10{_}1516{_}When, finally, Alvan Creede had seen the last person of the line pass into that awful tumult the light that had illuminated it was suddenly quenched and all was as black to him as to those within.
canbe10{_}1517{_}He turned away and left the place.
canbe10{_}1518{_}In the early morning a curious crowd had gathered about "Deemer's."
canbe10{_}1519{_}It was composed partly of those who had run away the night before, but now had the courage of sunshine, partly of honest folk going to their daily toil.
canbe10{_}1520{_}The door of the store stood open; the place was vacant, but on the walls, the floor, the furniture, were shreds of clothing and tangles of hair.
canbe10{_}1521{_}Hillbrook militant had managed somehow to pull itself out and had gone home to medicine its hurts and swear that it had been all night in bed.
canbe10{_}1522{_}On the dusty desk, behind the counter, was the sales-book.
canbe10{_}1523{_}The entries in it, in Deemer's handwriting, had ceased on the 16th day of July, the last of his life.
canbe10{_}1524{_}There was no record of a later sale to Alvan Creede.
canbe10{_}1525{_}That is the entire story--except that men's passions having subsided and reason having resumed its immemorial sway, it was confessed in Hillbrook that, considering the harmless and honorable character of his first commercial transaction under the new conditions, Silas Deemer, deceased, might properly have been suffered to resume business at the old stand without mobbing.
canbe10{_}1526{_}In that judgment the local historian from whose unpublished work these facts are compiled had the thoughtfulness to signify his concurrence.
canbe10{_}1527{_}STALEY FLEMING'S HALLUCINATION    Of two men who were talking one was a physician.
canbe10{_}1528{_}"I sent for you, Doctor," said the other, "but I don't think you can do me any good.
canbe10{_}1529{_}May be you can recommend a specialist in psychopathy.
canbe10{_}1530{_}I fancy I'm a bit loony."
canbe10{_}1531{_}"You look all right," the physician said.
canbe10{_}1532{_}"You shall judge--I have hallucinations.
canbe10{_}1533{_}I wake every night and see in my room, intently watching me, a big black Newfoundland dog with a white forefoot."
canbe10{_}1534{_}"You say you wake; are you sure about that?
canbe10{_}1535{_}'Hallucinations' are sometimes only dreams."
canbe10{_}1536{_}"Oh, I wake, all right.
canbe10{_}1537{_}Sometimes I lie still a long time, looking at the dog as earnestly as the dog looks at me--I always leave the light going.
canbe10{_}1538{_}When I can't endure it any longer I sit up in bed--and nothing is there!"

canbe10{_}1540{_}"It seems to me sinister.
canbe10{_}1541{_}Of course I know that, except in art, an animal's face in repose has always the same expression.
canbe10{_}1542{_}But this is not a real animal.
canbe10{_}1543{_}Newfoundland dogs are pretty mild looking, you know; what's the matter with this one?"
canbe10{_}1544{_}"Really, my diagnosis would have no value:  I am not going to treat the dog."
canbe10{_}1545{_}The physician laughed at his own pleasantry, but narrowly watched his patient from the corner of his eye.
canbe10{_}1546{_}Presently he said:  "Fleming, your description of the beast fits the dog of the late Atwell Barton."
canbe10{_}1547{_}Fleming half-rose from his chair, sat again and made a visible attempt at indifference.

canbe10{_}1550{_}He had been stabbed to death.
canbe10{_}1551{_}There have been no arrests; there was no clew.

canbe10{_}1553{_}I had one.
canbe10{_}1554{_}Have you?"

canbe10{_}1557{_}You remember that I left for Europe almost immediately afterward--a considerable time afterward.
canbe10{_}1558{_}In the few weeks since my return you could not expect me to construct a 'theory.'
canbe10{_}1559{_}In fact, I have not given the matter a thought.

canbe10{_}1564{_}Staley Fleming did not, or he would perhaps not have sprung to his feet as the night wind brought in through the open window the long wailing howl of a distant dog.
canbe10{_}1565{_}He strode several times across the room in the steadfast gaze of the physician; then, abruptly confronting him, almost shouted:  "What has all this to do with my trouble, Dr. Halderman?
canbe10{_}1566{_}You forget why you were sent for."

canbe10{_}1573{_}If anything disturbs you push the button without sitting up.
canbe10{_}1574{_}Good night."
canbe10{_}1575{_}Comfortably installed in an armchair the man of medicine stared into the glowing coals and thought deeply and long, but apparently to little purpose, for he frequently rose and opening a door leading to the staircase, listened intently; then resumed his seat.
canbe10{_}1576{_}Presently, however, he fell asleep, and when he woke it was past midnight.

canbe10{_}1579{_}He opened it at random and began to read:  "Forasmuch as it is ordained of God that all flesh hath spirit and thereby taketh on spiritual powers, so, also, the spirit hath powers of the flesh, even when it is gone out of the flesh and liveth as a thing apart, as many a violence performed by wraith and lemure sheweth.
canbe10{_}1580{_}And there be who say that man is not single in this, but the beasts have the like evil inducement, and--"  The reading was interrupted by a shaking of the house, as by the fall of a heavy object.
canbe10{_}1581{_}The reader flung down the book, rushed from the room and mounted the stairs to Fleming's bed-chamber.
canbe10{_}1582{_}He tried the door, but contrary to his instructions it was locked.
canbe10{_}1583{_}He set his shoulder against it with such force that it gave way.

canbe10{_}1588{_}But there was no animal.
canbe10{_}1589{_}A RESUMED IDENTITY    I--THE REVIEW AS A FORM OF WELCOME  One summer night a man stood on a low hill overlooking a wide expanse of forest and field.
canbe10{_}1590{_}By the full moon hanging low in the west he knew what he might not have known otherwise:  that it was near the hour of dawn.
canbe10{_}1591{_}A light mist lay along the earth, partly veiling the lower features of the landscape, but above it the taller trees showed in well-defined masses against a clear sky.
canbe10{_}1592{_}Two or three farmhouses were visible through the haze, but in none of them, naturally, was a light.
canbe10{_}1593{_}Nowhere, indeed, was any sign or suggestion of life except the barking of a distant dog, which, repeated with mechanical iteration, served rather to accentuate than dispel the loneliness of the scene.
canbe10{_}1594{_}The man looked curiously about him on all sides, as one who among familiar surroundings is unable to determine his exact place and part in the scheme of things.
canbe10{_}1595{_}It is so, perhaps, that we shall act when, risen from the dead, we await the call to judgment.
canbe10{_}1596{_}A hundred yards away was a straight road, showing white in the moonlight.
canbe10{_}1597{_}Endeavoring to orient himself, as a surveyor or navigator might say, the man moved his eyes slowly along its visible length and at a distance of a quarter-mile to the south of his station saw, dim and gray in the haze, a group of horsemen riding to the north.
canbe10{_}1598{_}Behind them were men afoot, marching in column, with dimly gleaming rifles aslant above their shoulders.
canbe10{_}1599{_}They moved slowly and in silence.
canbe10{_}1600{_}Another group of horsemen, another regiment of infantry, another and another--all in unceasing motion toward the man's point of view, past it, and beyond.
canbe10{_}1601{_}A battery of artillery followed, the cannoneers riding with folded arms on limber and caisson.
canbe10{_}1602{_}And still the interminable procession came out of the obscurity to south and passed into the obscurity to north, with never a sound of voice, nor hoof, nor wheel.
canbe10{_}1603{_}The man could not rightly understand:  he thought himself deaf; said so, and heard his own voice, although it had an unfamiliar quality that almost alarmed him; it disappointed his ear's expectancy in the matter of timbre and resonance.
canbe10{_}1604{_}But he was not deaf, and that for the moment sufficed.
canbe10{_}1605{_}Then he remembered that there are natural phenomena to which some one has given the name "acoustic shadows."
canbe10{_}1606{_}If you stand in an acoustic shadow there is one direction from which you will hear nothing.
canbe10{_}1607{_}At the battle of Gaines's Mill, one of the fiercest conflicts of the Civil War, with a hundred guns in play, spectators a mile and a half away on the opposite side of the Chickahominy valley heard nothing of what they clearly saw.
canbe10{_}1608{_}The bombardment of Port Royal, heard and felt at St.  Augustine, a hundred and fifty miles to the south, was inaudible two miles to the north in a still atmosphere.
canbe10{_}1609{_}A few days before the surrender at Appomattox a thunderous engagement between the commands of Sheridan and Pickett was unknown to the latter commander, a mile in the rear of his own line.
canbe10{_}1610{_}These instances were not known to the man of whom we write, but less striking ones of the same character had not escaped his observation.
canbe10{_}1611{_}He was profoundly disquieted, but for another reason than the uncanny silence of that moonlight march.
canbe10{_}1612{_}"Good Lord!"
canbe10{_}1613{_}he said to himself--and again it was as if another had spoken his thought--"if those people are what I take them to be we have lost the battle and they are moving on Nashville!"
canbe10{_}1614{_}Then came a thought of self--an apprehension--a strong sense of personal peril, such as in another we call fear.
canbe10{_}1615{_}He stepped quickly into the shadow of a tree.
canbe10{_}1616{_}And still the silent battalions moved slowly forward in the haze.
canbe10{_}1617{_}The chill of a sudden breeze upon the back of his neck drew his attention to the quarter whence it came, and turning to the east he saw a faint gray light along the horizon--the first sign of returning day.
canbe10{_}1618{_}This increased his apprehension.
canbe10{_}1619{_}"I must get away from here," he thought, "or I shall be discovered and taken."
canbe10{_}1620{_}He moved out of the shadow, walking rapidly toward the graying east.
canbe10{_}1621{_}From the safer seclusion of a clump of cedars he looked back.
canbe10{_}1622{_}The entire column had passed out of sight:  the straight white road lay bare and desolate in the moonlight!
canbe10{_}1623{_}Puzzled before, he was now inexpressibly astonished.
canbe10{_}1624{_}So swift a passing of so slow an army!--he could not comprehend it.
canbe10{_}1625{_}Minute after minute passed unnoted; he had lost his sense of time.
canbe10{_}1626{_}He sought with a terrible earnestness a solution of the mystery, but sought in vain.
canbe10{_}1627{_}When at last he roused himself from his abstraction the sun's rim was visible above the hills, but in the new conditions he found no other light than that of day; his understanding was involved as darkly in doubt as before.
canbe10{_}1628{_}On every side lay cultivated fields showing no sign of war and war's ravages.
canbe10{_}1629{_}From the chimneys of the farmhouses thin ascensions of blue smoke signaled preparations for a day's peaceful toil.
canbe10{_}1630{_}Having stilled its immemorial allocution to the moon, the watch-dog was assisting a negro who, prefixing a team of mules to the plow, was flatting and sharping contentedly at his task.
canbe10{_}1631{_}The hero of this tale stared stupidly at the pastoral picture as if he had never seen such a thing in all his life; then he put his hand to his head, passed it through his hair and, withdrawing it, attentively considered the palm--a singular thing to do.
canbe10{_}1632{_}Apparently reassured by the act, he walked confidently toward the road.
canbe10{_}1633{_}II--WHEN YOU HAVE LOST YOUR LIFE CONSULT A PHYSICIAN   Dr. Stilling Malson, of Murfreesboro, having visited a patient six or seven miles away, on the Nashville road, had remained with him all night.
canbe10{_}1634{_}At daybreak he set out for home on horseback, as was the custom of doctors of the time and region.
canbe10{_}1635{_}He had passed into the neighborhood of Stone's River battlefield when a man approached him from the roadside and saluted in the military fashion, with a movement of the right hand to the hat-brim.
canbe10{_}1636{_}But the hat was not a military hat, the man was not in uniform and had not a martial bearing.
canbe10{_}1637{_}The doctor nodded civilly, half thinking that the stranger's uncommon greeting was perhaps in deference to the historic surroundings.
canbe10{_}1638{_}As the stranger evidently desired speech with him he courteously reined in his horse and waited.
canbe10{_}1639{_}"Sir," said the stranger, "although a civilian, you are perhaps an enemy."
canbe10{_}1640{_}"I am a physician," was the non-committal reply.
canbe10{_}1641{_}"Thank you," said the other.
canbe10{_}1642{_}"I am a lieutenant, of the staff of General Hazen."
canbe10{_}1643{_}He paused a moment and looked sharply at the person whom he was addressing, then added, "Of the Federal army."
canbe10{_}1644{_}The physician merely nodded.
canbe10{_}1645{_}"Kindly tell me," continued the other, "what has happened here.
canbe10{_}1646{_}Where are the armies?
canbe10{_}1647{_}Which has won the battle?"
canbe10{_}1648{_}The physician regarded his questioner curiously with half-shut eyes.
canbe10{_}1649{_}After a professional scrutiny, prolonged to the limit of politeness, "Pardon me," he said; "one asking information should be willing to impart it.
canbe10{_}1650{_}Are you wounded?"
canbe10{_}1651{_}he added, smiling.
canbe10{_}1652{_}"Not seriously--it seems."
canbe10{_}1653{_}The man removed the unmilitary hat, put his hand to his head, passed it through his hair and, withdrawing it, attentively considered the palm.
canbe10{_}1654{_}"I was struck by a bullet and have been unconscious.
canbe10{_}1655{_}It must have been a light, glancing blow:  I find no blood and feel no pain.
canbe10{_}1656{_}I will not trouble you for treatment, but will you kindly direct me to my command--to any part of the Federal army--if you know?"
canbe10{_}1657{_}Again the doctor did not immediately reply:  he was recalling much that is recorded in the books of his profession--something about lost identity and the effect of familiar scenes in restoring it.
canbe10{_}1658{_}At length he looked the man in the face, smiled, and said:  "Lieutenant, you are not wearing the uniform of your rank and service."
canbe10{_}1659{_}At this the man glanced down at his civilian attire, lifted his eyes, and said with hesitation:  "That is true.
canbe10{_}1660{_}I--I don't quite understand."
canbe10{_}1661{_}Still regarding him sharply but not unsympathetically the man of science bluntly inquired:  "How old are you?"
canbe10{_}1662{_}"Twenty-three--if that has anything to do with it."
canbe10{_}1663{_}"You don't look it; I should hardly have guessed you to be just that."
canbe10{_}1664{_}The man was growing impatient.
canbe10{_}1665{_}"We need not discuss that," he said; "I want to know about the army.
canbe10{_}1666{_}Not two hours ago I saw a column of troops moving northward on this road.
canbe10{_}1667{_}You must have met them.
canbe10{_}1668{_}Be good enough to tell me the color of their clothing, which I was unable to make out, and I'll trouble you no more."
canbe10{_}1669{_}"You are quite sure that you saw them?"
canbe10{_}1670{_}"Sure?
canbe10{_}1671{_}My God, sir, I could have counted them!"
canbe10{_}1672{_}"Why, really," said the physician, with an amusing consciousness of his own resemblance to the loquacious barber of the Arabian Nights, "this is very interesting.
canbe10{_}1673{_}I met no troops."
canbe10{_}1674{_}The man looked at him coldly, as if he had himself observed the likeness to the barber.
canbe10{_}1675{_}"It is plain," he said, "that you do not care to assist me.
canbe10{_}1676{_}Sir, you may go to the devil!"
canbe10{_}1677{_}He turned and strode away, very much at random, across the dewy fields, his half-penitent tormentor quietly watching him from his point of vantage in the saddle till he disappeared beyond an array of trees.
canbe10{_}1678{_}III--THE DANGER OF LOOKING INTO A POOL OF WATER   After leaving the road the man slackened his pace, and now went forward, rather deviously, with a distinct feeling of fatigue.
canbe10{_}1679{_}He could not account for this, though truly the interminable loquacity of that country doctor offered itself in explanation.
canbe10{_}1680{_}Seating himself upon a rock, he laid one hand upon his knee, back upward, and casually looked at it.
canbe10{_}1681{_}It was lean and withered.
canbe10{_}1682{_}He lifted both hands to his face.
canbe10{_}1683{_}It was seamed and furrowed; he could trace the lines with the tips of his fingers.
canbe10{_}1684{_}How strange!--a mere bullet- stroke and a brief unconsciousness should not make one a physical wreck.
canbe10{_}1685{_}"I must have been a long time in hospital," he said aloud.
canbe10{_}1686{_}"Why, what a fool I am!
canbe10{_}1687{_}The battle was in December, and it is now summer!"
canbe10{_}1688{_}He laughed.
canbe10{_}1689{_}"No wonder that fellow thought me an escaped lunatic.
canbe10{_}1690{_}He was wrong:  I am only an escaped patient."
canbe10{_}1691{_}At a little distance a small plot of ground enclosed by a stone wall caught his attention.
canbe10{_}1692{_}With no very definite intent he rose and went to it.
canbe10{_}1693{_}In the center was a square, solid monument of hewn stone.
canbe10{_}1694{_}It was brown with age, weather-worn at the angles, spotted with moss and lichen.
canbe10{_}1695{_}Between the massive blocks were strips of grass the leverage of whose roots had pushed them apart.
canbe10{_}1696{_}In answer to the challenge of this ambitious structure Time had laid his destroying hand upon it, and it would soon be "one with Nineveh and Tyre."
canbe10{_}1697{_}In an inscription on one side his eye caught a familiar name.
canbe10{_}1698{_}Shaking with excitement, he craned his body across the wall and read:   HAZEN'S BRIGADE to The Memory of Its Soldiers who fell at Stone River, Dec. 31, 1862.
canbe10{_}1699{_}The man fell back from the wall, faint and sick.
canbe10{_}1700{_}Almost within an arm's length was a little depression in the earth; it had been filled by a recent rain--a pool of clear water.
canbe10{_}1701{_}He crept to it to revive himself, lifted the upper part of his body on his trembling arms, thrust forward his head and saw the reflection of his face, as in a mirror.
canbe10{_}1702{_}He uttered a terrible cry.
canbe10{_}1703{_}His arms gave way; he fell, face downward, into the pool and yielded up the life that had spanned another life.
canbe10{_}1704{_}A BABY TRAMP    If you had seen little Jo standing at the street corner in the rain, you would hardly have admired him.
canbe10{_}1705{_}It was apparently an ordinary autumn rainstorm, but the water which fell upon Jo (who was hardly old enough to be either just or unjust, and so perhaps did not come under the law of impartial distribution) appeared to have some property peculiar to itself:  one would have said it was dark and adhesive--sticky.
canbe10{_}1706{_}But that could hardly be so, even in Blackburg, where things certainly did occur that were a good deal out of the common.
canbe10{_}1707{_}For example, ten or twelve years before, a shower of small frogs had fallen, as is credibly attested by a contemporaneous chronicle, the record concluding with a somewhat obscure statement to the effect that the chronicler considered it good growing-weather for Frenchmen.
canbe10{_}1708{_}Some years later Blackburg had a fall of crimson snow; it is cold in Blackburg when winter is on, and the snows are frequent and deep.
canbe10{_}1709{_}There can be no doubt of it--the snow in this instance was of the color of blood and melted into water of the same hue, if water it was, not blood.
canbe10{_}1710{_}The phenomenon had attracted wide attention, and science had as many explanations as there were scientists who knew nothing about it.
canbe10{_}1711{_}But the men of Blackburg--men who for many years had lived right there where the red snow fell, and might be supposed to know a good deal about the matter--shook their heads and said something would come of it.
canbe10{_}1712{_}And something did, for the next summer was made memorable by the prevalence of a mysterious disease--epidemic, endemic, or the Lord knows what, though the physicians didn't--which carried away a full half of the population.
canbe10{_}1713{_}Most of the other half carried themselves away and were slow to return, but finally came back, and were now increasing and multiplying as before, but Blackburg had not since been altogether the same.
canbe10{_}1714{_}Of quite another kind, though equally "out of the common," was the incident of Hetty Parlow's ghost.
canbe10{_}1715{_}Hetty Parlow's maiden name had been Brownon, and in Blackburg that meant more than one would think.
canbe10{_}1716{_}The Brownons had from time immemorial--from the very earliest of the old colonial days--been the leading family of the town.
canbe10{_}1717{_}It was the richest and it was the best, and Blackburg would have shed the last drop of its plebeian blood in defense of the Brownon fair fame.
canbe10{_}1718{_}As few of the family's members had ever been known to live permanently away from Blackburg, although most of them were educated elsewhere and nearly all had traveled, there was quite a number of them.
canbe10{_}1719{_}The men held most of the public offices, and the women were foremost in all good works.
canbe10{_}1720{_}Of these latter, Hetty was most beloved by reason of the sweetness of her disposition, the purity of her character and her singular personal beauty.
canbe10{_}1721{_}She married in Boston a young scapegrace named Parlow, and like a good Brownon brought him to Blackburg forthwith and made a man and a town councilman of him.
canbe10{_}1722{_}They had a child which they named Joseph and dearly loved, as was then the fashion among parents in all that region.
canbe10{_}1723{_}Then they died of the mysterious disorder already mentioned, and at the age of one whole year Joseph set up as an orphan.
canbe10{_}1724{_}Unfortunately for Joseph the disease which had cut off his parents did not stop at that; it went on and extirpated nearly the whole Brownon contingent and its allies by marriage; and those who fled did not return.
canbe10{_}1725{_}The tradition was broken, the Brownon estates passed into alien hands and the only Brownons remaining in that place were underground in Oak Hill Cemetery, where, indeed, was a colony of them powerful enough to resist the encroachment of surrounding tribes and hold the best part of the grounds.
canbe10{_}1726{_}But about the ghost:  One night, about three years after the death of Hetty Parlow, a number of the young people of Blackburg were passing Oak Hill Cemetery in a wagon--if you have been there you will remember that the road to Greenton runs alongside it on the south.
canbe10{_}1727{_}They had been attending a May Day festival at Greenton; and that serves to fix the date.
canbe10{_}1728{_}Altogether there may have been a dozen, and a jolly party they were, considering the legacy of gloom left by the town's recent somber experiences.
canbe10{_}1729{_}As they passed the cemetery the man driving suddenly reined in his team with an exclamation of surprise.
canbe10{_}1730{_}It was sufficiently surprising, no doubt, for just ahead, and almost at the roadside, though inside the cemetery, stood the ghost of Hetty Parlow.
canbe10{_}1731{_}There could be no doubt of it, for she had been personally known to every youth and maiden in the party.
canbe10{_}1732{_}That established the thing's identity; its character as ghost was signified by all the customary signs--the shroud, the long, undone hair, the "far-away look"--everything.
canbe10{_}1733{_}This disquieting apparition was stretching out its arms toward the west, as if in supplication for the evening star, which, certainly, was an alluring object, though obviously out of reach.
canbe10{_}1734{_}As they all sat silent (so the story goes) every member of that party of merrymakers--they had merry-made on coffee and lemonade only--distinctly heard that ghost call the name "Joey, Joey!"
canbe10{_}1735{_}A moment later nothing was there.
canbe10{_}1736{_}Of course one does not have to believe all that.
canbe10{_}1737{_}Now, at that moment, as was afterward ascertained, Joey was wandering about in the sage-brush on the opposite side of the continent, near Winnemucca, in the State of Nevada.
canbe10{_}1738{_}He had been taken to that town by some good persons distantly related to his dead father, and by them adopted and tenderly cared for.
canbe10{_}1739{_}But on that evening the poor child had strayed from home and was lost in the desert.
canbe10{_}1740{_}His after history is involved in obscurity and has gaps which conjecture alone can fill.
canbe10{_}1741{_}It is known that he was found by a family of Piute Indians, who kept the little wretch with them for a time and then sold him--actually sold him for money to a woman on one of the east-bound trains, at a station a long way from Winnemucca.
canbe10{_}1742{_}The woman professed to have made all manner of inquiries, but all in vain:  so, being childless and a widow, she adopted him herself.
canbe10{_}1743{_}At this point of his career Jo seemed to be getting a long way from the condition of orphanage; the interposition of a multitude of parents between himself and that woeful state promised him a long immunity from its disadvantages.
canbe10{_}1744{_}Mrs. Darnell, his newest mother, lived in Cleveland, Ohio.
canbe10{_}1745{_}But her adopted son did not long remain with her.
canbe10{_}1746{_}He was seen one afternoon by a policeman, new to that beat, deliberately toddling away from her house, and being questioned answered that he was "a doin' home."
canbe10{_}1747{_}He must have traveled by rail, somehow, for three days later he was in the town of Whiteville, which, as you know, is a long way from Blackburg.
canbe10{_}1748{_}His clothing was in pretty fair condition, but he was sinfully dirty.
canbe10{_}1749{_}Unable to give any account of himself he was arrested as a vagrant and sentenced to imprisonment in the Infants' Sheltering Home--where he was washed.
canbe10{_}1750{_}Jo ran away from the Infants' Sheltering Home at Whiteville--just took to the woods one day, and the Home knew him no more forever.
canbe10{_}1751{_}We find him next, or rather get back to him, standing forlorn in the cold autumn rain at a suburban street corner in Blackburg; and it seems right to explain now that the raindrops falling upon him there were really not dark and gummy; they only failed to make his face and hands less so.
canbe10{_}1752{_}Jo was indeed fearfully and wonderfully besmirched, as by the hand of an artist.
canbe10{_}1753{_}And the forlorn little tramp had no shoes; his feet were bare, red, and swollen, and when he walked he limped with both legs.
canbe10{_}1754{_}As to clothing--ah, you would hardly have had the skill to name any single garment that he wore, or say by what magic he kept it upon him.
canbe10{_}1755{_}That he was cold all over and all through did not admit of a doubt; he knew it himself.
canbe10{_}1756{_}Anyone would have been cold there that evening; but, for that reason, no one else was there.
canbe10{_}1757{_}How Jo came to be there himself, he could not for the flickering little life of him have told, even if gifted with a vocabulary exceeding a hundred words.
canbe10{_}1758{_}From the way he stared about him one could have seen that he had not the faintest notion of where (nor why) he was.
canbe10{_}1759{_}Yet he was not altogether a fool in his day and generation; being cold and hungry, and still able to walk a little by bending his knees very much indeed and putting his feet down toes first, he decided to enter one of the houses which flanked the street at long intervals and looked so bright and warm.
canbe10{_}1760{_}But when he attempted to act upon that very sensible decision a burly dog came bowsing out and disputed his right.
canbe10{_}1761{_}Inexpressibly frightened and believing, no doubt (with some reason, too) that brutes without meant brutality within, he hobbled away from all the houses, and with gray, wet fields to right of him and gray, wet fields to left of him--with the rain half blinding him and the night coming in mist and darkness, held his way along the road that leads to Greenton.
canbe10{_}1762{_}That is to say, the road leads those to Greenton who succeed in passing the Oak Hill Cemetery.
canbe10{_}1763{_}A considerable number every year do not.
canbe10{_}1764{_}Jo did not.
canbe10{_}1765{_}They found him there the next morning, very wet, very cold, but no longer hungry.
canbe10{_}1766{_}He had apparently entered the cemetery gate--hoping, perhaps, that it led to a house where there was no dog--and gone blundering about in the darkness, falling over many a grave, no doubt, until he had tired of it all and given up.
canbe10{_}1767{_}The little body lay upon one side, with one soiled cheek upon one soiled hand, the other hand tucked away among the rags to make it warm, the other cheek washed clean and white at last, as for a kiss from one of God's great angels.
canbe10{_}1768{_}It was observed--though nothing was thought of it at the time, the body being as yet unidentified--that the little fellow was lying upon the grave of Hetty Parlow.
canbe10{_}1769{_}The grave, however, had not opened to receive him.
canbe10{_}1770{_}That is a circumstance which, without actual irreverence, one may wish had been ordered otherwise.
canbe10{_}1771{_}THE NIGHT-DOINGS AT "DEADMAN'S" A STORY THAT IS UNTRUE    It was a singularly sharp night, and clear as the heart of a diamond.
canbe10{_}1772{_}Clear nights have a trick of being keen.
canbe10{_}1773{_}In darkness you may be cold and not know it; when you see, you suffer.
canbe10{_}1774{_}This night was bright enough to bite like a serpent.
canbe10{_}1775{_}The moon was moving mysteriously along behind the giant pines crowning the South Mountain, striking a cold sparkle from the crusted snow, and bringing out against the black west the ghostly outlines of the Coast Range, beyond which lay the invisible Pacific.
canbe10{_}1776{_}The snow had piled itself, in the open spaces along the bottom of the gulch, into long ridges that seemed to heave, and into hills that appeared to toss and scatter spray.
canbe10{_}1777{_}The spray was sunlight, twice reflected:  dashed once from the moon, once from the snow.
canbe10{_}1778{_}In this snow many of the shanties of the abandoned mining camp were obliterated, (a sailor might have said they had gone down) and at irregular intervals it had overtopped the tall trestles which had once supported a river called a flume; for, of course, "flume" is flumen.
canbe10{_}1779{_}Among the advantages of which the mountains cannot deprive the gold-hunter is the privilege of speaking Latin.
canbe10{_}1780{_}He says of his dead neighbor, "He has gone up the flume."
canbe10{_}1781{_}This is not a bad way to say, "His life has returned to the Fountain of Life."
canbe10{_}1782{_}While putting on its armor against the assaults of the wind, this snow had neglected no coign of vantage.
canbe10{_}1783{_}Snow pursued by the wind is not wholly unlike a retreating army.
canbe10{_}1784{_}In the open field it ranges itself in ranks and battalions; where it can get a foothold it makes a stand; where it can take cover it does so.
canbe10{_}1785{_}You may see whole platoons of snow cowering behind a bit of broken wall.
canbe10{_}1786{_}The devious old road, hewn out of the mountain side, was full of it.
canbe10{_}1787{_}Squadron upon squadron had struggled to escape by this line, when suddenly pursuit had ceased.
canbe10{_}1788{_}A more desolate and dreary spot than Deadman's Gulch in a winter midnight it is impossible to imagine.
canbe10{_}1789{_}Yet Mr. Hiram Beeson elected to live there, the sole inhabitant.
canbe10{_}1790{_}Away up the side of the North Mountain his little pine-log shanty projected from its single pane of glass a long, thin beam of light, and looked not altogether unlike a black beetle fastened to the hillside with a bright new pin.
canbe10{_}1791{_}Within it sat Mr. Beeson himself, before a roaring fire, staring into its hot heart as if he had never before seen such a thing in all his life.
canbe10{_}1792{_}He was not a comely man.
canbe10{_}1793{_}He was gray; he was ragged and slovenly in his attire; his face was wan and haggard; his eyes were too bright.
canbe10{_}1794{_}As to his age, if one had attempted to guess it, one might have said forty-seven, then corrected himself and said seventy-four.
canbe10{_}1795{_}He was really twenty-eight.
canbe10{_}1796{_}Emaciated he was; as much, perhaps, as he dared be, with a needy undertaker at Bentley's Flat and a new and enterprising coroner at Sonora.
canbe10{_}1797{_}Poverty and zeal are an upper and a nether millstone.
canbe10{_}1798{_}It is dangerous to make a third in that kind of sandwich.
canbe10{_}1799{_}As Mr. Beeson sat there, with his ragged elbows on his ragged knees, his lean jaws buried in his lean hands, and with no apparent intention of going to bed, he looked as if the slightest movement would tumble him to pieces.
canbe10{_}1800{_}Yet during the last hour he had winked no fewer than three times.
canbe10{_}1801{_}There was a sharp rapping at the door.
canbe10{_}1802{_}A rap at that time of night and in that weather might have surprised an ordinary mortal who had dwelt two years in the gulch without seeing a human face, and could not fail to know that the country was impassable; but Mr. Beeson did not so much as pull his eyes out of the coals.
canbe10{_}1803{_}And even when the door was pushed open he only shrugged a little more closely into himself, as one does who is expecting something that he would rather not see.
canbe10{_}1804{_}You may observe this movement in women when, in a mortuary chapel, the coffin is borne up the aisle behind them.
canbe10{_}1805{_}But when a long old man in a blanket overcoat, his head tied up in a handkerchief and nearly his entire face in a muffler, wearing green goggles and with a complexion of glittering whiteness where it could be seen, strode silently into the room, laying a hard, gloved hand on Mr. Beeson's shoulder, the latter so far forgot himself as to look up with an appearance of no small astonishment; whomever he may have been expecting, he had evidently not counted on meeting anyone like this.
canbe10{_}1806{_}Nevertheless, the sight of this unexpected guest produced in Mr. Beeson the following sequence:  a feeling of astonishment; a sense of gratification; a sentiment of profound good will.
canbe10{_}1807{_}Rising from his seat, he took the knotty hand from his shoulder, and shook it up and down with a fervor quite unaccountable; for in the old man's aspect was nothing to attract, much to repel.
canbe10{_}1808{_}However, attraction is too general a property for repulsion to be without it.
canbe10{_}1809{_}The most attractive object in the world is the face we instinctively cover with a cloth.
canbe10{_}1810{_}When it becomes still more attractive-- fascinating--we put seven feet of earth above it.
canbe10{_}1811{_}"Sir," said Mr. Beeson, releasing the old man's hand, which fell passively against his thigh with a quiet clack, "it is an extremely disagreeable night.
canbe10{_}1812{_}Pray be seated; I am very glad to see you."
canbe10{_}1813{_}Mr. Beeson spoke with an easy good breeding that one would hardly have expected, considering all things.
canbe10{_}1814{_}Indeed, the contrast between his appearance and his manner was sufficiently surprising to be one of the commonest of social phenomena in the mines.
canbe10{_}1815{_}The old man advanced a step toward the fire, glowing cavernously in the green goggles.
canbe10{_}1816{_}Mr. Beeson resumed:  "You bet your life I am!"
canbe10{_}1817{_}Mr. Beeson's elegance was not too refined; it had made reasonable concessions to local taste.
canbe10{_}1818{_}He paused a moment, letting his eyes drop from the muffled head of his guest, down along the row of moldy buttons confining the blanket overcoat, to the greenish cowhide boots powdered with snow, which had begun to melt and run along the floor in little rills.
canbe10{_}1819{_}He took an inventory of his guest, and appeared satisfied.
canbe10{_}1820{_}Who would not have been?
canbe10{_}1821{_}Then he continued:  "The cheer I can offer you is, unfortunately, in keeping with my surroundings; but I shall esteem myself highly favored if it is your pleasure to partake of it, rather than seek better at Bentley's Flat."
canbe10{_}1822{_}With a singular refinement of hospitable humility Mr. Beeson spoke as if a sojourn in his warm cabin on such a night, as compared with walking fourteen miles up to the throat in snow with a cutting crust, would be an intolerable hardship.
canbe10{_}1823{_}By way of reply, his guest unbuttoned the blanket overcoat.
canbe10{_}1824{_}The host laid fresh fuel on the fire, swept the hearth with the tail of a wolf, and added:  "But _I_ think you'd better skedaddle."
canbe10{_}1825{_}The old man took a seat by the fire, spreading his broad soles to the heat without removing his hat.
canbe10{_}1826{_}In the mines the hat is seldom removed except when the boots are.
canbe10{_}1827{_}Without further remark Mr. Beeson also seated himself in a chair which had been a barrel, and which, retaining much of its original character, seemed to have been designed with a view to preserving his dust if it should please him to crumble.
canbe10{_}1828{_}For a moment there was silence; then, from somewhere among the pines, came the snarling yelp of a coyote; and simultaneously the door rattled in its frame.
canbe10{_}1829{_}There was no other connection between the two incidents than that the coyote has an aversion to storms, and the wind was rising; yet there seemed somehow a kind of supernatural conspiracy between the two, and Mr. Beeson shuddered with a vague sense of terror.
canbe10{_}1830{_}He recovered himself in a moment and again addressed his guest.
canbe10{_}1831{_}"There are strange doings here.
canbe10{_}1832{_}I will tell you everything, and then if you decide to go I shall hope to accompany you over the worst of the way; as far as where Baldy Peterson shot Ben Hike--I dare say you know the place."
canbe10{_}1833{_}The old man nodded emphatically, as intimating not merely that he did, but that he did indeed.
canbe10{_}1834{_}"Two years ago," began Mr. Beeson, "I, with two companions, occupied this house; but when the rush to the Flat occurred we left, along with the rest.
canbe10{_}1835{_}In ten hours the Gulch was deserted.
canbe10{_}1836{_}That evening, however, I discovered I had left behind me a valuable pistol (that is it) and returned for it, passing the night here alone, as I have passed every night since.
canbe10{_}1837{_}I must explain that a few days before we left, our Chinese domestic had the misfortune to die while the ground was frozen so hard that it was impossible to dig a grave in the usual way.
canbe10{_}1838{_}So, on the day of our hasty departure, we cut through the floor there, and gave him such burial as we could.
canbe10{_}1839{_}But before putting him down I had the extremely bad taste to cut off his pigtail and spike it to that beam above his grave, where you may see it at this moment, or, preferably, when warmth has given you leisure for observation.
canbe10{_}1840{_}"I stated, did I not, that the Chinaman came to his death from natural causes?
canbe10{_}1841{_}I had, of course, nothing to do with that, and returned through no irresistible attraction, or morbid fascination, but only because I had forgotten a pistol.
canbe10{_}1842{_}This is clear to you, is it not, sir?"
canbe10{_}1843{_}The visitor nodded gravely.
canbe10{_}1844{_}He appeared to be a man of few words, if any.
canbe10{_}1845{_}Mr. Beeson continued:  "According to the Chinese faith, a man is like a kite:  he cannot go to heaven without a tail.
canbe10{_}1846{_}Well, to shorten this tedious story-- which, however, I thought it my duty to relate--on that night, while I was here alone and thinking of anything but him, that Chinaman came back for his pigtail.
canbe10{_}1847{_}"He did not get it."
canbe10{_}1848{_}At this point Mr. Beeson relapsed into blank silence.
canbe10{_}1849{_}Perhaps he was fatigued by the unwonted exercise of speaking; perhaps he had conjured up a memory that demanded his undivided attention.
canbe10{_}1850{_}The wind was now fairly abroad, and the pines along the mountainside sang with singular distinctness.
canbe10{_}1851{_}The narrator continued:  "You say you do not see much in that, and I must confess I do not myself.
canbe10{_}1852{_}"But he keeps coming!"
canbe10{_}1853{_}There was another long silence, during which both stared into the fire without the movement of a limb.
canbe10{_}1854{_}Then Mr. Beeson broke out, almost fiercely, fixing his eyes on what he could see of the impassive face of his auditor:  "Give it him?
canbe10{_}1855{_}Sir, in this matter I have no intention of troubling anyone for advice.
canbe10{_}1856{_}You will pardon me, I am sure"--here he became singularly persuasive--"but I have ventured to nail that pigtail fast, and have assumed the somewhat onerous obligation of guarding it.
canbe10{_}1857{_}So it is quite impossible to act on your considerate suggestion.
canbe10{_}1858{_}"Do you play me for a Modoc?"
canbe10{_}1859{_}Nothing could exceed the sudden ferocity with which he thrust this indignant remonstrance into the ear of his guest.

canbe10{_}1864{_}Do you play me for a Chinaman?
canbe10{_}1865{_}is a question frequently addressed to the ear of the suddenly dead.
canbe10{_}1866{_}Mr. Beeson's buffet produced no effect, and after a moment's pause, during which the wind thundered in the chimney like the sound of clods upon a coffin, he resumed:  "But, as you say, it is wearing me out.

canbe10{_}1875{_}Mr. Beeson was speaking with his eyes shut, and he wandered.
canbe10{_}1876{_}His last word was a snore.

canbe10{_}1879{_}Then the aged stranger, who had not uttered one word since his arrival, arose from his seat and deliberately laid off his outer clothing, looking as angular in his flannels as the late Signorina Festorazzi, an Irish woman, six feet in height, and weighing fifty- six pounds, who used to exhibit herself in her chemise to the people of San Francisco.
canbe10{_}1880{_}He then crept into one of the "bunks," having first placed a revolver in easy reach, according to the custom of the country.
canbe10{_}1881{_}This revolver he took from a shelf, and it was the one which Mr. Beeson had mentioned as that for which he had returned to the Gulch two years before.
canbe10{_}1882{_}In a few moments Mr. Beeson awoke, and seeing that his guest had retired he did likewise.
canbe10{_}1883{_}But before doing so he approached the long, plaited wisp of pagan hair and gave it a powerful tug, to assure himself that it was fast and firm.
canbe10{_}1884{_}The two beds--mere shelves covered with blankets not overclean--faced each other from opposite sides of the room, the little square trapdoor that had given access to the Chinaman's grave being midway between.
canbe10{_}1885{_}This, by the way, was crossed by a double row of spike-heads.
canbe10{_}1886{_}In his resistance to the supernatural, Mr. Beeson had not disdained the use of material precautions.

canbe10{_}1889{_}The song of the pines outside had now risen to the dignity of a triumphal hymn.

canbe10{_}1894{_}Mr. Beeson awoke, and without rising, pressed his fingers into his eyes.
canbe10{_}1895{_}He shuddered; his teeth chattered.
canbe10{_}1896{_}His guest was now reclining on one elbow, watching the proceedings with the goggles that glowed like lamps.

canbe10{_}1900{_}But now another actor appeared upon the scene.

canbe10{_}1902{_}Mr. Beeson groaned, and again spread his hands upon his face.
canbe10{_}1903{_}A mild odor of opium pervaded the place.

canbe10{_}1909{_}Mr. Beeson cowered in his bed.

canbe10{_}1911{_}The old man sat erect and quietly laid hold of the revolver.
canbe10{_}1912{_}Bang!

canbe10{_}1914{_}The trapdoor turned over, shutting down with a snap.
canbe10{_}1915{_}The swarthy little gentleman from San Francisco sprang nimbly from his perch, caught something in the air with his hat, as a boy catches a butterfly, and vanished into the chimney as if drawn up by suction.
canbe10{_}1916{_}From away somewhere in the outer darkness floated in through the open door a faint, far cry--a long, sobbing wail, as of a child death- strangled in the desert, or a lost soul borne away by the Adversary.
canbe10{_}1917{_}It may have been the coyote.
canbe10{_}1918{_}In the early days of the following spring a party of miners on their way to new diggings passed along the Gulch, and straying through the deserted shanties found in one of them the body of Hiram Beeson, stretched upon a bunk, with a bullet hole through the heart.
canbe10{_}1919{_}The ball had evidently been fired from the opposite side of the room, for in one of the oaken beams overhead was a shallow blue dint, where it had struck a knot and been deflected downward to the breast of its victim.
canbe10{_}1920{_}Strongly attached to the same beam was what appeared to be an end of a rope of braided horsehair, which had been cut by the bullet in its passage to the knot.
canbe10{_}1921{_}Nothing else of interest was noted, excepting a suit of moldy and incongruous clothing, several articles of which were afterward identified by respectable witnesses as those in which certain deceased citizens of Deadman's had been buried years before.
canbe10{_}1922{_}But it is not easy to understand how that could be, unless, indeed, the garments had been worn as a disguise by Death himself--which is hardly credible.
canbe10{_}1923{_}BEYOND THE WALL    Many years ago, on my way from Hongkong to New York, I assed a week in San Francisco.
canbe10{_}1924{_}A long time had gone by since I had been in that city, during which my ventures in the Orient had prospered beyond my hope; I was rich and could afford to revisit my own country to renew my friendship with such of the companions of my youth as still lived and remembered me with the old affection.
canbe10{_}1925{_}Chief of these, I hoped, was Mohun Dampier, an old schoolmate with whom I had held a desultory correspondence which had long ceased, as is the way of correspondence between men.
canbe10{_}1926{_}You may have observed that the indisposition to write a merely social letter is in the ratio of the square of the distance between you and your correspondent.
canbe10{_}1927{_}It is a law.
canbe10{_}1928{_}I remembered Dampier as a handsome, strong young fellow of scholarly tastes, with an aversion to work and a marked indifference to many of the things that the world cares for, including wealth, of which, however, he had inherited enough to put him beyond the reach of want.
canbe10{_}1929{_}In his family, one of the oldest and most aristocratic in the country, it was, I think, a matter of pride that no member of it had ever been in trade nor politics, nor suffered any kind of distinction.
canbe10{_}1930{_}Mohun was a trifle sentimental, and had in him a singular element of superstition, which led him to the study of all manner of occult subjects, although his sane mental health safeguarded him against fantastic and perilous faiths.
canbe10{_}1931{_}He made daring incursions into the realm of the unreal without renouncing his residence in the partly surveyed and charted region of what we are pleased to call certitude.
canbe10{_}1932{_}The night of my visit to him was stormy.
canbe10{_}1933{_}The Californian winter was on, and the incessant rain plashed in the deserted streets, or, lifted by irregular gusts of wind, was hurled against the houses with incredible fury.
canbe10{_}1934{_}With no small difficulty my cabman found the right place, away out toward the ocean beach, in a sparsely populated suburb.
canbe10{_}1935{_}The dwelling, a rather ugly one, apparently, stood in the center of its grounds, which as nearly as I could make out in the gloom were destitute of either flowers or grass.
canbe10{_}1936{_}Three or four trees, writhing and moaning in the torment of the tempest, appeared to be trying to escape from their dismal environment and take the chance of finding a better one out at sea.
canbe10{_}1937{_}The house was a two-story brick structure with a tower, a story higher, at one corner.
canbe10{_}1938{_}In a window of that was the only visible light.
canbe10{_}1939{_}Something in the appearance of the place made me shudder, a performance that may have been assisted by a rill of rain-water down my back as I scuttled to cover in the doorway.
canbe10{_}1940{_}In answer to my note apprising him of my wish to call, Dampier had written, "Don't ring--open the door and come up."
canbe10{_}1941{_}I did so.
canbe10{_}1942{_}The staircase was dimly lighted by a single gas-jet at the top of the second flight.
canbe10{_}1943{_}I managed to reach the landing without disaster and entered by an open door into the lighted square room of the tower.
canbe10{_}1944{_}Dampier came forward in gown and slippers to receive me, giving me the greeting that I wished, and if I had held a thought that it might more fitly have been accorded me at the front door the first look at him dispelled any sense of his inhospitality.
canbe10{_}1945{_}He was not the same.
canbe10{_}1946{_}Hardly past middle age, he had gone gray and had acquired a pronounced stoop.
canbe10{_}1947{_}His figure was thin and angular, his face deeply lined, his complexion dead-white, without a touch of color.
canbe10{_}1948{_}His eyes, unnaturally large, glowed with a fire that was almost uncanny.
canbe10{_}1949{_}He seated me, proffered a cigar, and with grave and obvious sincerity assured me of the pleasure that it gave him to meet me.
canbe10{_}1950{_}Some unimportant conversation followed, but all the while I was dominated by a melancholy sense of the great change in him.
canbe10{_}1951{_}This he must have perceived, for he suddenly said with a bright enough smile, "You are disappointed in me--non sum qualis eram."
canbe10{_}1952{_}I hardly knew what to reply, but managed to say:  "Why, really, I don't know:  your Latin is about the same."
canbe10{_}1953{_}He brightened again.
canbe10{_}1954{_}"No," he said, "being a dead language, it grows in appropriateness.
canbe10{_}1955{_}But please have the patience to wait:  where I am going there is perhaps a better tongue.
canbe10{_}1956{_}Will you care to have a message in it?"
canbe10{_}1957{_}The smile faded as he spoke, and as he concluded he was looking into my eyes with a gravity that distressed me.
canbe10{_}1958{_}Yet I would not surrender myself to his mood, nor permit him to see how deeply his prescience of death affected me.
canbe10{_}1959{_}"I fancy that it will be long," I said, "before human speech will cease to serve our need; and then the need, with its possibilities of service, will have passed."
canbe10{_}1960{_}He made no reply, and I too was silent, for the talk had taken a dispiriting turn, yet I knew not how to give it a more agreeable character.
canbe10{_}1961{_}Suddenly, in a pause of the storm, when the dead silence was almost startling by contrast with the previous uproar, I heard a gentle tapping, which appeared to come from the wall behind my chair.
canbe10{_}1962{_}The sound was such as might have been made by a human hand, not as upon a door by one asking admittance, but rather, I thought, as an agreed signal, an assurance of someone's presence in an adjoining room; most of us, I fancy, have had more experience of such communications than we should care to relate.
canbe10{_}1963{_}I glanced at Dampier.
canbe10{_}1964{_}If possibly there was something of amusement in the look he did not observe it.
canbe10{_}1965{_}He appeared to have forgotten my presence, and was staring at the wall behind me with an expression in his eyes that I am unable to name, although my memory of it is as vivid to-day as was my sense of it then.
canbe10{_}1966{_}The situation was embarrassing; I rose to take my leave.
canbe10{_}1967{_}At this he seemed to recover himself.
canbe10{_}1968{_}"Please be seated," he said; "it is nothing--no one is there."
canbe10{_}1969{_}But the tapping was repeated, and with the same gentle, slow insistence as before.
canbe10{_}1970{_}"Pardon me," I said, "it is late.
canbe10{_}1971{_}May I call to-morrow?"
canbe10{_}1972{_}He smiled--a little mechanically, I thought.
canbe10{_}1973{_}"It is very delicate of you," said he, "but quite needless.
canbe10{_}1974{_}Really, this is the only room in the tower, and no one is there.
canbe10{_}1975{_}At least--" He left the sentence incomplete, rose, and threw up a window, the only opening in the wall from which the sound seemed to come.
canbe10{_}1976{_}"See."
canbe10{_}1977{_}Not clearly knowing what else to do I followed him to the window and looked out.
canbe10{_}1978{_}A street-lamp some little distance away gave enough light through the murk of the rain that was again falling in torrents to make it entirely plain that "no one was there."
canbe10{_}1979{_}In truth there was nothing but the sheer blank wall of the tower.
canbe10{_}1980{_}Dampier closed the window and signing me to my seat resumed his own.
canbe10{_}1981{_}The incident was not in itself particularly mysterious; any one of a dozen explanations was possible (though none has occurred to me), yet it impressed me strangely, the more, perhaps, from my friend's effort to reassure me, which seemed to dignify it with a certain significance and importance.
canbe10{_}1982{_}He had proved that no one was there, but in that fact lay all the interest; and he proffered no explanation.
canbe10{_}1983{_}His silence was irritating and made me resentful.
canbe10{_}1984{_}"My good friend," I said, somewhat ironically, I fear, "I am not disposed to question your right to harbor as many spooks as you find agreeable to your taste and consistent with your notions of companionship; that is no business of mine.
canbe10{_}1985{_}But being just a plain man of affairs, mostly of this world, I find spooks needless to my peace and comfort.
canbe10{_}1986{_}I am going to my hotel, where my fellow-guests are still in the flesh."
canbe10{_}1987{_}It was not a very civil speech, but he manifested no feeling about it.
canbe10{_}1988{_}"Kindly remain," he said.
canbe10{_}1989{_}"I am grateful for your presence here.
canbe10{_}1990{_}What you have heard to-night I believe myself to have heard twice before.
canbe10{_}1991{_}Now I KNOW it was no illusion.
canbe10{_}1992{_}That is much to me-- more than you know.
canbe10{_}1993{_}Have a fresh cigar and a good stock of patience while I tell you the story."
canbe10{_}1994{_}The rain was now falling more steadily, with a low, monotonous susurration, interrupted at long intervals by the sudden slashing of the boughs of the trees as the wind rose and failed.
canbe10{_}1995{_}The night was well advanced, but both sympathy and curiosity held me a willing listener to my friend's monologue, which I did not interrupt by a single word from beginning to end.
canbe10{_}1996{_}"Ten years ago," he said, "I occupied a ground-floor apartment in one of a row of houses, all alike, away at the other end of the town, on what we call Rincon Hill.
canbe10{_}1997{_}This had been the best quarter of San Francisco, but had fallen into neglect and decay, partly because the primitive character of its domestic architecture no longer suited the maturing tastes of our wealthy citizens, partly because certain public improvements had made a wreck of it.
canbe10{_}1998{_}The row of dwellings in one of which I lived stood a little way back from the street, each having a miniature garden, separated from its neighbors by low iron fences and bisected with mathematical precision by a box-bordered gravel walk from gate to door.
canbe10{_}1999{_}"One morning as I was leaving my lodging I observed a young girl entering the adjoining garden on the left.
canbe10{_}2000{_}It was a warm day in June, and she was lightly gowned in white.
canbe10{_}2001{_}From her shoulders hung a broad straw hat profusely decorated with flowers and wonderfully beribboned in the fashion of the time.
canbe10{_}2002{_}My attention was not long held by the exquisite simplicity of her costume, for no one could look at her face and think of anything earthly.
canbe10{_}2003{_}Do not fear; I shall not profane it by description; it was beautiful exceedingly.
canbe10{_}2004{_}All that I had ever seen or dreamed of loveliness was in that matchless living picture by the hand of the Divine Artist.
canbe10{_}2005{_}So deeply did it move me that, without a thought of the impropriety of the act, I unconsciously bared my head, as a devout Catholic or well-bred Protestant uncovers before an image of the Blessed Virgin.
canbe10{_}2006{_}The maiden showed no displeasure; she merely turned her glorious dark eyes upon me with a look that made me catch my breath, and without other recognition of my act passed into the house.
canbe10{_}2007{_}For a moment I stood motionless, hat in hand, painfully conscious of my rudeness, yet so dominated by the emotion inspired by that vision of incomparable beauty that my penitence was less poignant than it should have been.
canbe10{_}2008{_}Then I went my way, leaving my heart behind.
canbe10{_}2009{_}In the natural course of things I should probably have remained away until nightfall, but by the middle of the afternoon I was back in the little garden, affecting an interest in the few foolish flowers that I had never before observed.
canbe10{_}2010{_}My hope was vain; she did not appear.
canbe10{_}2011{_}"To a night of unrest succeeded a day of expectation and disappointment, but on the day after, as I wandered aimlessly about the neighborhood, I met her.
canbe10{_}2012{_}Of course I did not repeat my folly of uncovering, nor venture by even so much as too long a look to manifest an interest in her; yet my heart was beating audibly.
canbe10{_}2013{_}I trembled and consciously colored as she turned her big black eyes upon me with a look of obvious recognition entirely devoid of boldness or coquetry.
canbe10{_}2014{_}"I will not weary you with particulars; many times afterward I met the maiden, yet never either addressed her or sought to fix her attention.
canbe10{_}2015{_}Nor did I take any action toward making her acquaintance.
canbe10{_}2016{_}Perhaps my forbearance, requiring so supreme an effort of self- denial, will not be entirely clear to you.
canbe10{_}2017{_}That I was heels over head in love is true, but who can overcome his habit of thought, or reconstruct his character?
canbe10{_}2018{_}"I was what some foolish persons are pleased to call, and others, more foolish, are pleased to be called--an aristocrat; and despite her beauty, her charms and graces, the girl was not of my class.
canbe10{_}2019{_}I had learned her name--which it is needless to speak--and something of her family.
canbe10{_}2020{_}She was an orphan, a dependent niece of the impossible elderly fat woman in whose lodging-house she lived.
canbe10{_}2021{_}My income was small and I lacked the talent for marrying; it is perhaps a gift.
canbe10{_}2022{_}An alliance with that family would condemn me to its manner of life, part me from my books and studies, and in a social sense reduce me to the ranks.
canbe10{_}2023{_}It is easy to deprecate such considerations as these and I have not retained myself for the defense.
canbe10{_}2024{_}Let judgment be entered against me, but in strict justice all my ancestors for generations should be made co-defendants and I be permitted to plead in mitigation of punishment the imperious mandate of heredity.
canbe10{_}2025{_}To a mesalliance of that kind every globule of my ancestral blood spoke in opposition.
canbe10{_}2026{_}In brief, my tastes, habits, instinct, with whatever of reason my love had left me--all fought against it.
canbe10{_}2027{_}Moreover, I was an irreclaimable sentimentalist, and found a subtle charm in an impersonal and spiritual relation which acquaintance might vulgarize and marriage would certainly dispel.
canbe10{_}2028{_}No woman, I argued, is what this lovely creature seems.
canbe10{_}2029{_}Love is a delicious dream; why should I bring about my own awakening?
canbe10{_}2030{_}"The course dictated by all this sense and sentiment was obvious.
canbe10{_}2031{_}Honor, pride, prudence, preservation of my ideals--all commanded me to go away, but for that I was too weak.
canbe10{_}2032{_}The utmost that I could do by a mighty effort of will was to cease meeting the girl, and that I did.
canbe10{_}2033{_}I even avoided the chance encounters of the garden, leaving my lodging only when I knew that she had gone to her music lessons, and returning after nightfall.
canbe10{_}2034{_}Yet all the while I was as one in a trance, indulging the most fascinating fancies and ordering my entire intellectual life in accordance with my dream.
canbe10{_}2035{_}Ah, my friend, as one whose actions have a traceable relation to reason, you cannot know the fool's paradise in which I lived.
canbe10{_}2036{_}"One evening the devil put it into my head to be an unspeakable idiot.
canbe10{_}2037{_}By apparently careless and purposeless questioning I learned from my gossipy landlady that the young woman's bedroom adjoined my own, a party-wall between.
canbe10{_}2038{_}Yielding to a sudden and coarse impulse I gently rapped on the wall.
canbe10{_}2039{_}There was no response, naturally, but I was in no mood to accept a rebuke.
canbe10{_}2040{_}A madness was upon me and I repeated the folly, the offense, but again ineffectually, and I had the decency to desist.
canbe10{_}2041{_}"An hour later, while absorbed in some of my infernal studies, I heard, or thought I heard, my signal answered.
canbe10{_}2042{_}Flinging down my books I sprang to the wall and as steadily as my beating heart would permit gave three slow taps upon it.
canbe10{_}2043{_}This time the response was distinct, unmistakable:  one, two, three--an exact repetition of my signal.
canbe10{_}2044{_}That was all I could elicit, but it was enough--too much.
canbe10{_}2045{_}"The next evening, and for many evenings afterward, that folly went on, I always having 'the last word.'
canbe10{_}2046{_}During the whole period I was deliriously happy, but with the perversity of my nature I persevered in my resolution not to see her.
canbe10{_}2047{_}Then, as I should have expected, I got no further answers.
canbe10{_}2048{_}'She is disgusted,' I said to myself, 'with what she thinks my timidity in making no more definite advances'; and I resolved to seek her and make her acquaintance and--what?
canbe10{_}2049{_}I did not know, nor do I now know, what might have come of it.
canbe10{_}2050{_}I know only that I passed days and days trying to meet her, and all in vain; she was invisible as well as inaudible.
canbe10{_}2051{_}I haunted the streets where we had met, but she did not come.
canbe10{_}2052{_}From my window I watched the garden in front of her house, but she passed neither in nor out.
canbe10{_}2053{_}I fell into the deepest dejection, believing that she had gone away, yet took no steps to resolve my doubt by inquiry of my landlady, to whom, indeed, I had taken an unconquerable aversion from her having once spoken of the girl with less of reverence than I thought befitting.
canbe10{_}2054{_}"There came a fateful night.
canbe10{_}2055{_}Worn out with emotion, irresolution and despondency, I had retired early and fallen into such sleep as was still possible to me.
canbe10{_}2056{_}In the middle of the night something--some malign power bent upon the wrecking of my peace forever--caused me to open my eyes and sit up, wide awake and listening intently for I knew not what.
canbe10{_}2057{_}Then I thought I heard a faint tapping on the wall--the mere ghost of the familiar signal.
canbe10{_}2058{_}In a few moments it was repeated: one, two, three--no louder than before, but addressing a sense alert and strained to receive it.
