canbe10{_}2059{_}I was about to reply when the Adversary of Peace again intervened in my affairs with a rascally suggestion of retaliation.
canbe10{_}2060{_}She had long and cruelly ignored me; now I would ignore her.
canbe10{_}2061{_}Incredible fatuity--may God forgive it!
canbe10{_}2062{_}All the rest of the night I lay awake, fortifying my obstinacy with shameless justifications and--listening.
canbe10{_}2063{_}"Late the next morning, as I was leaving the house, I met my landlady, entering.
canbe10{_}2064{_}"'Good morning, Mr. Dampier,' she said.
canbe10{_}2065{_}'Have you heard the news?'
canbe10{_}2066{_}"I replied in words that I had heard no news; in manner, that I did not care to hear any.
canbe10{_}2067{_}The manner escaped her observation.
canbe10{_}2068{_}"'About the sick young lady next door,' she babbled on.
canbe10{_}2069{_}'What!
canbe10{_}2070{_}you did not know?
canbe10{_}2071{_}Why, she has been ill for weeks.
canbe10{_}2072{_}And now--'  "I almost sprang upon her.
canbe10{_}2073{_}'And now,' I cried, 'now what?'
canbe10{_}2074{_}"'She is dead.'
canbe10{_}2075{_}"That is not the whole story.
canbe10{_}2076{_}In the middle of the night, as I learned later, the patient, awakening from a long stupor after a week of delirium, had asked--it was her last utterance--that her bed be moved to the opposite side of the room.
canbe10{_}2077{_}Those in attendance had thought the request a vagary of her delirium, but had complied.
canbe10{_}2078{_}And there the poor passing soul had exerted its failing will to restore a broken connection--a golden thread of sentiment between its innocence and a monstrous baseness owning a blind, brutal allegiance to the Law of Self.
canbe10{_}2079{_}"What reparation could I make?
canbe10{_}2080{_}Are there masses that can be said for the repose of souls that are abroad such nights as this--spirits 'blown about by the viewless winds'--coming in the storm and darkness with signs and portents, hints of memory and presages of doom?
canbe10{_}2081{_}"This is the third visitation.
canbe10{_}2082{_}On the first occasion I was too skeptical to do more than verify by natural methods the character of the incident; on the second, I responded to the signal after it had been several times repeated, but without result.
canbe10{_}2083{_}To-night's recurrence completes the 'fatal triad' expounded by Parapelius Necromantius.
canbe10{_}2084{_}There is no more to tell."
canbe10{_}2085{_}When Dampier had finished his story I could think of nothing relevant that I cared to say, and to question him would have been a hideous impertinence.
canbe10{_}2086{_}I rose and bade him good night in a way to convey to him a sense of my sympathy, which he silently acknowledged by a pressure of the hand.
canbe10{_}2087{_}That night, alone with his sorrow and remorse, he passed into the Unknown.
canbe10{_}2088{_}A PSYCHOLOGICAL SHIPWRECK    In the summer of 1874 I was in Liverpool, whither I had gone on business for the mercantile house of Bronson & Jarrett, New York.
canbe10{_}2089{_}I am William Jarrett; my partner was Zenas Bronson.
canbe10{_}2090{_}The firm failed last year, and unable to endure the fall from affluence to poverty he died.
canbe10{_}2091{_}Having finished my business, and feeling the lassitude and exhaustion incident to its dispatch, I felt that a protracted sea voyage would be both agreeable and beneficial, so instead of embarking for my return on one of the many fine passenger steamers I booked for New York on the sailing vessel Morrow, upon which I had shipped a large and valuable invoice of the goods I had bought.
canbe10{_}2092{_}The Morrow was an English ship with, of course, but little accommodation for passengers, of whom there were only myself, a young woman and her servant, who was a middle-aged negress.
canbe10{_}2093{_}I thought it singular that a traveling English girl should be so attended, but she afterward explained to me that the woman had been left with her family by a man and his wife from South Carolina, both of whom had died on the same day at the house of the young lady's father in Devonshire--a circumstance in itself sufficiently uncommon to remain rather distinctly in my memory, even had it not afterward transpired in conversation with the young lady that the name of the man was William Jarrett, the same as my own.
canbe10{_}2094{_}I knew that a branch of my family had settled in South Carolina, but of them and their history I was ignorant.
canbe10{_}2095{_}The Morrow sailed from the mouth of the Mersey on the 15th of June and for several weeks we had fair breezes and unclouded skies.
canbe10{_}2096{_}The skipper, an admirable seaman but nothing more, favored us with very little of his society, except at his table; and the young woman, Miss Janette Harford, and I became very well acquainted.
canbe10{_}2097{_}We were, in truth, nearly always together, and being of an introspective turn of mind I often endeavored to analyze and define the novel feeling with which she inspired me--a secret, subtle, but powerful attraction which constantly impelled me to seek her; but the attempt was hopeless.
canbe10{_}2098{_}I could only be sure that at least it was not love.
canbe10{_}2099{_}Having assured myself of this and being certain that she was quite as whole-hearted, I ventured one evening (I remember it was on the 3d of July) as we sat on deck to ask her, laughingly, if she could assist me to resolve my psychological doubt.
canbe10{_}2100{_}For a moment she was silent, with averted face, and I began to fear I had been extremely rude and indelicate; then she fixed her eyes gravely on my own.
canbe10{_}2101{_}In an instant my mind was dominated by as strange a fancy as ever entered human consciousness.
canbe10{_}2102{_}It seemed as if she were looking at me, not WITH, but THROUGH, those eyes--from an immeasurable distance behind them--and that a number of other persons, men, women and children, upon whose faces I caught strangely familiar evanescent expressions, clustered about her, struggling with gentle eagerness to look at me through the same orbs.
canbe10{_}2103{_}Ship, ocean, sky--all had vanished.
canbe10{_}2104{_}I was conscious of nothing but the figures in this extraordinary and fantastic scene.
canbe10{_}2105{_}Then all at once darkness fell upon me, and anon from out of it, as to one who grows accustomed by degrees to a dimmer light, my former surroundings of deck and mast and cordage slowly resolved themselves.
canbe10{_}2106{_}Miss Harford had closed her eyes and was leaning back in her chair, apparently asleep, the book she had been reading open in her lap.
canbe10{_}2107{_}Impelled by surely I cannot say what motive, I glanced at the top of the page; it was a copy of that rare and curious work, "Denneker's Meditations," and the lady's index finger rested on this passage:  "To sundry it is given to be drawn away, and to be apart from the body for a season; for, as concerning rills which would flow across each other the weaker is borne along by the stronger, so there be certain of kin whose paths intersecting, their souls do bear company, the while their bodies go fore-appointed ways, unknowing."
canbe10{_}2108{_}Miss Harford arose, shuddering; the sun had sunk below the horizon, but it was not cold.
canbe10{_}2109{_}There was not a breath of wind; there were no clouds in the sky, yet not a star was visible.
canbe10{_}2110{_}A hurried tramping sounded on the deck; the captain, summoned from below, joined the first officer, who stood looking at the barometer.
canbe10{_}2111{_}"Good God!"
canbe10{_}2112{_}I heard him exclaim.
canbe10{_}2113{_}An hour later the form of Janette Harford, invisible in the darkness and spray, was torn from my grasp by the cruel vortex of the sinking ship, and I fainted in the cordage of the floating mast to which I had lashed myself.
canbe10{_}2114{_}It was by lamplight that I awoke.
canbe10{_}2115{_}I lay in a berth amid the familiar surroundings of the stateroom of a steamer.
canbe10{_}2116{_}On a couch opposite sat a man, half undressed for bed, reading a book.
canbe10{_}2117{_}I recognized the face of my friend Gordon Doyle, whom I had met in Liverpool on the day of my embarkation, when he was himself about to sail on the steamer City of Prague, on which he had urged me to accompany him.
canbe10{_}2118{_}After some moments I now spoke his name.
canbe10{_}2119{_}He simply said, "Well," and turned a leaf in his book without removing his eyes from the page.
canbe10{_}2120{_}"Doyle," I repeated, "did they save HER?"
canbe10{_}2121{_}He now deigned to look at me and smiled as if amused.
canbe10{_}2122{_}He evidently thought me but half awake.
canbe10{_}2123{_}"Her?
canbe10{_}2124{_}Whom do you mean?"
canbe10{_}2125{_}"Janette Harford."
canbe10{_}2126{_}His amusement turned to amazement; he stared at me fixedly, saying nothing.
canbe10{_}2127{_}"You will tell me after a while," I continued; "I suppose you will tell me after a while."
canbe10{_}2128{_}A moment later I asked:  "What ship is this?"
canbe10{_}2129{_}Doyle stared again.
canbe10{_}2130{_}"The steamer City of Prague, bound from Liverpool to New York, three weeks out with a broken shaft.
canbe10{_}2131{_}Principal passenger, Mr. Gordon Doyle; ditto lunatic, Mr. William Jarrett.
canbe10{_}2132{_}These two distinguished travelers embarked together, but they are about to part, it being the resolute intention of the former to pitch the latter overboard."
canbe10{_}2133{_}I sat bolt upright.
canbe10{_}2134{_}"Do you mean to say that I have been for three weeks a passenger on this steamer?"
canbe10{_}2135{_}"Yes, pretty nearly; this is the 3d of July."
canbe10{_}2136{_}"Have I been ill?"
canbe10{_}2137{_}"Right as a trivet all the time, and punctual at your meals."
canbe10{_}2138{_}"My God!
canbe10{_}2139{_}Doyle, there is some mystery here; do have the goodness to be serious.
canbe10{_}2140{_}Was I not rescued from the wreck of the ship Morrow?"
canbe10{_}2141{_}Doyle changed color, and approaching me, laid his fingers on my wrist.
canbe10{_}2142{_}A moment later, "What do you know of Janette Harford?"
canbe10{_}2143{_}he asked very calmly.
canbe10{_}2144{_}"First tell me what YOU know of her?"
canbe10{_}2145{_}Mr. Doyle gazed at me for some moments as if thinking what to do, then seating himself again on the couch, said:  "Why should I not?
canbe10{_}2146{_}I am engaged to marry Janette Harford, whom I met a year ago in London.
canbe10{_}2147{_}Her family, one of the wealthiest in Devonshire, cut up rough about it, and we eloped--are eloping rather, for on the day that you and I walked to the landing stage to go aboard this steamer she and her faithful servant, a negress, passed us, driving to the ship Morrow.
canbe10{_}2148{_}She would not consent to go in the same vessel with me, and it had been deemed best that she take a sailing vessel in order to avoid observation and lessen the risk of detection.
canbe10{_}2149{_}I am now alarmed lest this cursed breaking of our machinery may detain us so long that the Morrow will get to New York before us, and the poor girl will not know where to go."
canbe10{_}2150{_}I lay still in my berth--so still I hardly breathed.
canbe10{_}2151{_}But the subject was evidently not displeasing to Doyle, and after a short pause he resumed:  "By the way, she is only an adopted daughter of the Harfords.
canbe10{_}2152{_}Her mother was killed at their place by being thrown from a horse while hunting, and her father, mad with grief, made away with himself the same day.
canbe10{_}2153{_}No one ever claimed the child, and after a reasonable time they adopted her.
canbe10{_}2154{_}She has grown up in the belief that she is their daughter."
canbe10{_}2155{_}"Doyle, what book are you reading?"
canbe10{_}2156{_}"Oh, it's called 'Denneker's Meditations.'
canbe10{_}2157{_}It's a rum lot, Janette gave it to me; she happened to have two copies.
canbe10{_}2158{_}Want to see it?"
canbe10{_}2159{_}He tossed me the volume, which opened as it fell.
canbe10{_}2160{_}On one of the exposed pages was a marked passage:  "To sundry it is given to be drawn away, and to be apart from the body for a season; for, as concerning rills which would flow across each other the weaker is borne along by the stronger, so there be certain of kin whose paths intersecting, their souls do bear company, the while their bodies go fore-appointed ways, unknowing."
canbe10{_}2161{_}"She had--she has--a singular taste in reading," I managed to say, mastering my agitation.
canbe10{_}2162{_}"Yes.
canbe10{_}2163{_}And now perhaps you will have the kindness to explain how you knew her name and that of the ship she sailed in."
canbe10{_}2164{_}"You talked of her in your sleep," I said.
canbe10{_}2165{_}A week later we were towed into the port of New York.
canbe10{_}2166{_}But the Morrow was never heard from.
canbe10{_}2167{_}THE MIDDLE TOE OF THE RIGHT FOOT    I  It is well known that the old Manton house is haunted.
canbe10{_}2168{_}In all the rural district near about, and even in the town of Marshall, a mile away, not one person of unbiased mind entertains a doubt of it; incredulity is confined to those opinionated persons who will be called "cranks" as soon as the useful word shall have penetrated the intellectual demesne of the Marshall Advance.
canbe10{_}2169{_}The evidence that the house is haunted is of two kinds:  the testimony of disinterested witnesses who have had ocular proof, and that of the house itself.
canbe10{_}2170{_}The former may be disregarded and ruled out on any of the various grounds of objection which may be urged against it by the ingenious; but facts within the observation of all are material and controlling.
canbe10{_}2171{_}In the first place, the Manton house has been unoccupied by mortals for more than ten years, and with its outbuildings is slowly falling into decay--a circumstance which in itself the judicious will hardly venture to ignore.
canbe10{_}2172{_}It stands a little way off the loneliest reach of the Marshall and Harriston road, in an opening which was once a farm and is still disfigured with strips of rotting fence and half covered with brambles overrunning a stony and sterile soil long unacquainted with the plow.
canbe10{_}2173{_}The house itself is in tolerably good condition, though badly weather-stained and in dire need of attention from the glazier, the smaller male population of the region having attested in the manner of its kind its disapproval of dwelling without dwellers.
canbe10{_}2174{_}It is two stories in height, nearly square, its front pierced by a single doorway flanked on each side by a window boarded up to the very top.
canbe10{_}2175{_}Corresponding windows above, not protected, serve to admit light and rain to the rooms of the upper floor.
canbe10{_}2176{_}Grass and weeds grow pretty rankly all about, and a few shade trees, somewhat the worse for wind, and leaning all in one direction, seem to be making a concerted effort to run away.
canbe10{_}2177{_}In short, as the Marshall town humorist explained in the columns of the Advance, "the proposition that the Manton house is badly haunted is the only logical conclusion from the premises."
canbe10{_}2178{_}The fact that in this dwelling Mr. Manton thought it expedient one night some ten years ago to rise and cut the throats of his wife and two small children, removing at once to another part of the country, has no doubt done its share in directing public attention to the fitness of the place for supernatural phenomena.
canbe10{_}2179{_}To this house, one summer evening, came four men in a wagon.
canbe10{_}2180{_}Three of them promptly alighted, and the one who had been driving hitched the team to the only remaining post of what had been a fence.
canbe10{_}2181{_}The fourth remained seated in the wagon.
canbe10{_}2182{_}"Come," said one of his companions, approaching him, while the others moved away in the direction of the dwelling--"this is the place."
canbe10{_}2183{_}The man addressed did not move.
canbe10{_}2184{_}"By God!"
canbe10{_}2185{_}he said harshly, "this is a trick, and it looks to me as if you were in it."
canbe10{_}2186{_}"Perhaps I am," the other said, looking him straight in the face and speaking in a tone which had something of contempt in it.
canbe10{_}2187{_}"You will remember, however, that the choice of place was with your own assent left to the other side.
canbe10{_}2188{_}Of course if you are afraid of spooks--"  "I am afraid of nothing," the man interrupted with another oath, and sprang to the ground.
canbe10{_}2189{_}The two then joined the others at the door, which one of them had already opened with some difficulty, caused by rust of lock and hinge.
canbe10{_}2190{_}All entered.
canbe10{_}2191{_}Inside it was dark, but the man who had unlocked the door produced a candle and matches and made a light.
canbe10{_}2192{_}He then unlocked a door on their right as they stood in the passage.
canbe10{_}2193{_}This gave them entrance to a large, square room that the candle but dimly lighted.
canbe10{_}2194{_}The floor had a thick carpeting of dust, which partly muffled their footfalls.
canbe10{_}2195{_}Cobwebs were in the angles of the walls and depended from the ceiling like strips of rotting lace, making undulatory movements in the disturbed air.
canbe10{_}2196{_}The room had two windows in adjoining sides, but from neither could anything be seen except the rough inner surfaces of boards a few inches from the glass.
canbe10{_}2197{_}There was no fireplace, no furniture; there was nothing: besides the cobwebs and the dust, the four men were the only objects there which were not a part of the structure.
canbe10{_}2198{_}Strange enough they looked in the yellow light of the candle.
canbe10{_}2199{_}The one who had so reluctantly alighted was especially spectacular--he might have been called sensational.
canbe10{_}2200{_}He was of middle age, heavily built, deep chested and broad shouldered.
canbe10{_}2201{_}Looking at his figure, one would have said that he had a giant's strength; at his features, that he would use it like a giant.
canbe10{_}2202{_}He was clean shaven, his hair rather closely cropped and gray.
canbe10{_}2203{_}His low forehead was seamed with wrinkles above the eyes, and over the nose these became vertical.
canbe10{_}2204{_}The heavy black brows followed the same law, saved from meeting only by an upward turn at what would otherwise have been the point of contact.
canbe10{_}2205{_}Deeply sunken beneath these, glowed in the obscure light a pair of eyes of uncertain color, but obviously enough too small.
canbe10{_}2206{_}There was something forbidding in their expression, which was not bettered by the cruel mouth and wide jaw.
canbe10{_}2207{_}The nose was well enough, as noses go; one does not expect much of noses.
canbe10{_}2208{_}All that was sinister in the man's face seemed accentuated by an unnatural pallor--he appeared altogether bloodless.
canbe10{_}2209{_}The appearance of the other men was sufficiently commonplace:  they were such persons as one meets and forgets that he met.
canbe10{_}2210{_}All were younger than the man described, between whom and the eldest of the others, who stood apart, there was apparently no kindly feeling.
canbe10{_}2211{_}They avoided looking at each other.
canbe10{_}2212{_}"Gentlemen," said the man holding the candle and keys, "I believe everything is right.
canbe10{_}2213{_}Are you ready, Mr.
canbe10{_}2214{_}Rosser?"
canbe10{_}2215{_}The man standing apart from the group bowed and smiled.
canbe10{_}2216{_}"And you, Mr.
canbe10{_}2217{_}Grossmith?"
canbe10{_}2218{_}The heavy man bowed and scowled.
canbe10{_}2219{_}"You will be pleased to remove your outer clothing."
canbe10{_}2220{_}Their hats, coats, waistcoats and neckwear were soon removed and thrown outside the door, in the passage.
canbe10{_}2221{_}The man with the candle now nodded, and the fourth man--he who had urged Grossmith to leave the wagon--produced from the pocket of his overcoat two long, murderous- looking bowie-knives, which he drew now from their leather scabbards.
canbe10{_}2222{_}"They are exactly alike," he said, presenting one to each of the two principals--for by this time the dullest observer would have understood the nature of this meeting.
canbe10{_}2223{_}It was to be a duel to the death.
canbe10{_}2224{_}Each combatant took a knife, examined it critically near the candle and tested the strength of blade and handle across his lifted knee.
canbe10{_}2225{_}Their persons were then searched in turn, each by the second of the other.
canbe10{_}2226{_}"If it is agreeable to you, Mr. Grossmith," said the man holding the light, "you will place yourself in that corner."
canbe10{_}2227{_}He indicated the angle of the room farthest from the door, whither Grossmith retired, his second parting from him with a grasp of the hand which had nothing of cordiality in it.
canbe10{_}2228{_}In the angle nearest the door Mr. Rosser stationed himself, and after a whispered consultation his second left him, joining the other near the door.
canbe10{_}2229{_}At that moment the candle was suddenly extinguished, leaving all in profound darkness.
canbe10{_}2230{_}This may have been done by a draught from the opened door; whatever the cause, the effect was startling.
canbe10{_}2231{_}"Gentlemen," said a voice which sounded strangely unfamiliar in the altered condition affecting the relations of the senses--"gentlemen, you will not move until you hear the closing of the outer door."
canbe10{_}2232{_}A sound of trampling ensued, then the closing of the inner door; and finally the outer one closed with a concussion which shook the entire building.
canbe10{_}2233{_}A few minutes afterward a belated farmer's boy met a light wagon which was being driven furiously toward the town of Marshall.
canbe10{_}2234{_}He declared that behind the two figures on the front seat stood a third, with its hands upon the bowed shoulders of the others, who appeared to struggle vainly to free themselves from its grasp.
canbe10{_}2235{_}This figure, unlike the others, was clad in white, and had undoubtedly boarded the wagon as it passed the haunted house.
canbe10{_}2236{_}As the lad could boast a considerable former experience with the supernatural thereabouts his word had the weight justly due to the testimony of an expert.
canbe10{_}2237{_}The story (in connection with the next day's events) eventually appeared in the Advance, with some slight literary embellishments and a concluding intimation that the gentlemen referred to would be allowed the use of the paper's columns for their version of the night's adventure.
canbe10{_}2238{_}But the privilege remained without a claimant.
canbe10{_}2239{_}II  The events that led up to this "duel in the dark" were simple enough.
canbe10{_}2240{_}One evening three young men of the town of Marshall were sitting in a quiet corner of the porch of the village hotel, smoking and discussing such matters as three educated young men of a Southern village would naturally find interesting.
canbe10{_}2241{_}Their names were King, Sancher and Rosser.
canbe10{_}2242{_}At a little distance, within easy hearing, but taking no part in the conversation, sat a fourth.
canbe10{_}2243{_}He was a stranger to the others.
canbe10{_}2244{_}They merely knew that on his arrival by the stage- coach that afternoon he had written in the hotel register the name Robert Grossmith.
canbe10{_}2245{_}He had not been observed to speak to anyone except the hotel clerk.
canbe10{_}2246{_}He seemed, indeed, singularly fond of his own company--or, as the PERSONNEL of the Advance expressed it, "grossly addicted to evil associations."
canbe10{_}2247{_}But then it should be said in justice to the stranger that the PERSONNEL was himself of a too convivial disposition fairly to judge one differently gifted, and had, moreover, experienced a slight rebuff in an effort at an "interview."
canbe10{_}2248{_}"I hate any kind of deformity in a woman," said King, "whether natural or--acquired.
canbe10{_}2249{_}I have a theory that any physical defect has its correlative mental and moral defect."
canbe10{_}2250{_}"I infer, then," said Rosser, gravely, "that a lady lacking the moral advantage of a nose would find the struggle to become Mrs. King an arduous enterprise."
canbe10{_}2251{_}"Of course you may put it that way," was the reply; "but, seriously, I once threw over a most charming girl on learning quite accidentally that she had suffered amputation of a toe.
canbe10{_}2252{_}My conduct was brutal if you like, but if I had married that girl I should have been miserable for life and should have made her so."
canbe10{_}2253{_}"Whereas," said Sancher, with a light laugh, "by marrying a gentleman of more liberal views she escaped with a parted throat."
canbe10{_}2254{_}"Ah, you know to whom I refer.
canbe10{_}2255{_}Yes, she married Manton, but I don't know about his liberality; I'm not sure but he cut her throat because he discovered that she lacked that excellent thing in woman, the middle toe of the right foot."
canbe10{_}2256{_}"Look at that chap!"
canbe10{_}2257{_}said Rosser in a low voice, his eyes fixed upon the stranger.
canbe10{_}2258{_}That chap was obviously listening intently to the conversation.
canbe10{_}2259{_}"Damn his impudence!"
canbe10{_}2260{_}muttered King--"what ought we to do?"
canbe10{_}2261{_}"That's an easy one," Rosser replied, rising.
canbe10{_}2262{_}"Sir," he continued, addressing the stranger, "I think it would be better if you would remove your chair to the other end of the veranda.
canbe10{_}2263{_}The presence of gentlemen is evidently an unfamiliar situation to you."
canbe10{_}2264{_}The man sprang to his feet and strode forward with clenched hands, his face white with rage.
canbe10{_}2265{_}All were now standing.
canbe10{_}2266{_}Sancher stepped between the belligerents.
canbe10{_}2267{_}"You are hasty and unjust," he said to Rosser; "this gentleman has done nothing to deserve such language."
canbe10{_}2268{_}But Rosser would not withdraw a word.
canbe10{_}2269{_}By the custom of the country and the time there could be but one outcome to the quarrel.
canbe10{_}2270{_}"I demand the satisfaction due to a gentleman," said the stranger, who had become more calm.
canbe10{_}2271{_}"I have not an acquaintance in this region.
canbe10{_}2272{_}Perhaps you, sir," bowing to Sancher, "will be kind enough to represent me in this matter."
canbe10{_}2273{_}Sancher accepted the trust--somewhat reluctantly it must be confessed, for the man's appearance and manner were not at all to his liking.
canbe10{_}2274{_}King, who during the colloquy had hardly removed his eyes from the stranger's face and had not spoken a word, consented with a nod to act for Rosser, and the upshot of it was that, the principals having retired, a meeting was arranged for the next evening.
canbe10{_}2275{_}The nature of the arrangements has been already disclosed.
canbe10{_}2276{_}The duel with knives in a dark room was once a commoner feature of Southwestern life than it is likely to be again.
canbe10{_}2277{_}How thin a veneering of "chivalry" covered the essential brutality of the code under which such encounters were possible we shall see.
canbe10{_}2278{_}III  In the blaze of a midsummer noonday the old Manton house was hardly true to its traditions.
canbe10{_}2279{_}It was of the earth, earthy.
canbe10{_}2280{_}The sunshine caressed it warmly and affectionately, with evident disregard of its bad reputation.
canbe10{_}2281{_}The grass greening all the expanse in its front seemed to grow, not rankly, but with a natural and joyous exuberance, and the weeds blossomed quite like plants.
canbe10{_}2282{_}Full of charming lights and shadows and populous with pleasant-voiced birds, the neglected shade trees no longer struggled to run away, but bent reverently beneath their burdens of sun and song.
canbe10{_}2283{_}Even in the glassless upper windows was an expression of peace and contentment, due to the light within.
canbe10{_}2284{_}Over the stony fields the visible heat danced with a lively tremor incompatible with the gravity which is an attribute of the supernatural.
canbe10{_}2285{_}Such was the aspect under which the place presented itself to Sheriff Adams and two other men who had come out from Marshall to look at it.
canbe10{_}2286{_}One of these men was Mr. King, the sheriff's deputy; the other, whose name was Brewer, was a brother of the late Mrs. Manton.
canbe10{_}2287{_}Under a beneficent law of the State relating to property which has been for a certain period abandoned by an owner whose residence cannot be ascertained, the sheriff was legal custodian of the Manton farm and appurtenances thereunto belonging.
canbe10{_}2288{_}His present visit was in mere perfunctory compliance with some order of a court in which Mr.
canbe10{_}2289{_}Brewer had an action to get possession of the property as heir to his deceased sister.
canbe10{_}2290{_}By a mere coincidence, the visit was made on the day after the night that Deputy King had unlocked the house for another and very different purpose.
canbe10{_}2291{_}His presence now was not of his own choosing:  he had been ordered to accompany his superior and at the moment could think of nothing more prudent than simulated alacrity in obedience to the command.
canbe10{_}2292{_}Carelessly opening the front door, which to his surprise was not locked, the sheriff was amazed to see, lying on the floor of the passage into which it opened, a confused heap of men's apparel.
canbe10{_}2293{_}Examination showed it to consist of two hats, and the same number of coats, waistcoats and scarves, all in a remarkably good state of preservation, albeit somewhat defiled by the dust in which they lay.
canbe10{_}2294{_}Mr.
canbe10{_}2295{_}Brewer was equally astonished, but Mr. King's emotion is not of record.
canbe10{_}2296{_}With a new and lively interest in his own actions the sheriff now unlatched and pushed open a door on the right, and the three entered.
canbe10{_}2297{_}The room was apparently vacant--no; as their eyes became accustomed to the dimmer light something was visible in the farthest angle of the wall.
canbe10{_}2298{_}It was a human figure--that of a man crouching close in the corner.
canbe10{_}2299{_}Something in the attitude made the intruders halt when they had barely passed the threshold.
canbe10{_}2300{_}The figure more and more clearly defined itself.
canbe10{_}2301{_}The man was upon one knee, his back in the angle of the wall, his shoulders elevated to the level of his ears, his hands before his face, palms outward, the fingers spread and crooked like claws; the white face turned upward on the retracted neck had an expression of unutterable fright, the mouth half open, the eyes incredibly expanded.
canbe10{_}2302{_}He was stone dead.
canbe10{_}2303{_}Yet, with the exception of a bowie-knife, which had evidently fallen from his own hand, not another object was in the room.
canbe10{_}2304{_}In thick dust that covered the floor were some confused footprints near the door and along the wall through which it opened.
canbe10{_}2305{_}Along one of the adjoining walls, too, past the boarded-up windows, was the trail made by the man himself in reaching his corner.
canbe10{_}2306{_}Instinctively in approaching the body the three men followed that trail.
canbe10{_}2307{_}The sheriff grasped one of the outthrown arms; it was as rigid as iron, and the application of a gentle force rocked the entire body without altering the relation of its parts.
canbe10{_}2308{_}Brewer, pale with excitement, gazed intently into the distorted face.
canbe10{_}2309{_}"God of mercy!"
canbe10{_}2310{_}he suddenly cried, "it is Manton!"
canbe10{_}2311{_}"You are right," said King, with an evident attempt at calmness:  "I knew Manton.
canbe10{_}2312{_}He then wore a full beard and his hair long, but this is he."
canbe10{_}2313{_}He might have added:  "I recognized him when he challenged Rosser.
canbe10{_}2314{_}I told Rosser and Sancher who he was before we played him this horrible trick.
canbe10{_}2315{_}When Rosser left this dark room at our heels, forgetting his outer clothing in the excitement, and driving away with us in his shirt sleeves--all through the discreditable proceedings we knew whom we were dealing with, murderer and coward that he was!"
canbe10{_}2316{_}But nothing of this did Mr. King say.
canbe10{_}2317{_}With his better light he was trying to penetrate the mystery of the man's death.
canbe10{_}2318{_}That he had not once moved from the corner where he had been stationed; that his posture was that of neither attack nor defense; that he had dropped his weapon; that he had obviously perished of sheer horror of something that he saw--these were circumstances which Mr. King's disturbed intelligence could not rightly comprehend.
canbe10{_}2319{_}Groping in intellectual darkness for a clew to his maze of doubt, his gaze, directed mechanically downward in the way of one who ponders momentous matters, fell upon something which, there, in the light of day and in the presence of living companions, affected him with terror.
canbe10{_}2320{_}In the dust of years that lay thick upon the floor--leading from the door by which they had entered, straight across the room to within a yard of Manton's crouching corpse--were three parallel lines of footprints--light but definite impressions of bare feet, the outer ones those of small children, the inner a woman's.
canbe10{_}2321{_}From the point at which they ended they did not return; they pointed all one way.
canbe10{_}2322{_}Brewer, who had observed them at the same moment, was leaning forward in an attitude of rapt attention, horribly pale.
canbe10{_}2323{_}"Look at that!"
canbe10{_}2324{_}he cried, pointing with both hands at the nearest print of the woman's right foot, where she had apparently stopped and stood.
canbe10{_}2325{_}"The middle toe is missing--it was Gertrude!"
canbe10{_}2326{_}Gertrude was the late Mrs. Manton, sister to Mr.
canbe10{_}2327{_}Brewer.
canbe10{_}2328{_}JOHN MORTONSON'S FUNERAL {1}    John Mortonson was dead:  his lines in "the tragedy 'Man'" had all been spoken and he had left the stage.
canbe10{_}2329{_}The body rested in a fine mahogany coffin fitted with a plate of glass.
canbe10{_}2330{_}All arrangements for the funeral had been so well attended to that had the deceased known he would doubtless have approved.
canbe10{_}2331{_}The face, as it showed under the glass, was not disagreeable to look upon:  it bore a faint smile, and as the death had been painless, had not been distorted beyond the repairing power of the undertaker.
canbe10{_}2332{_}At two o'clock of the afternoon the friends were to assemble to pay their last tribute of respect to one who had no further need of friends and respect.
canbe10{_}2333{_}The surviving members of the family came severally every few minutes to the casket and wept above the placid features beneath the glass.
canbe10{_}2334{_}This did them no good; it did no good to John Mortonson; but in the presence of death reason and philosophy are silent.
canbe10{_}2335{_}As the hour of two approached the friends began to arrive and after offering such consolation to the stricken relatives as the proprieties of the occasion required, solemnly seated themselves about the room with an augmented consciousness of their importance in the scheme funereal.
canbe10{_}2336{_}Then the minister came, and in that overshadowing presence the lesser lights went into eclipse.
canbe10{_}2337{_}His entrance was followed by that of the widow, whose lamentations filled the room.
canbe10{_}2338{_}She approached the casket and after leaning her face against the cold glass for a moment was gently led to a seat near her daughter.
canbe10{_}2339{_}Mournfully and low the man of God began his eulogy of the dead, and his doleful voice, mingled with the sobbing which it was its purpose to stimulate and sustain, rose and fell, seemed to come and go, like the sound of a sullen sea.
canbe10{_}2340{_}The gloomy day grew darker as he spoke; a curtain of cloud underspread the sky and a few drops of rain fell audibly.
canbe10{_}2341{_}It seemed as if all nature were weeping for John Mortonson.
canbe10{_}2342{_}When the minister had finished his eulogy with prayer a hymn was sung and the pall-bearers took their places beside the bier.
canbe10{_}2343{_}As the last notes of the hymn died away the widow ran to the coffin, cast herself upon it and sobbed hysterically.
canbe10{_}2344{_}Gradually, however, she yielded to dissuasion, becoming more composed; and as the minister was in the act of leading her away her eyes sought the face of the dead beneath the glass.
canbe10{_}2345{_}She threw up her arms and with a shriek fell backward insensible.
canbe10{_}2346{_}The mourners sprang forward to the coffin, the friends followed, and as the clock on the mantel solemnly struck three all were staring down upon the face of John Mortonson, deceased.
canbe10{_}2347{_}They turned away, sick and faint.
canbe10{_}2348{_}One man, trying in his terror to escape the awful sight, stumbled against the coffin so heavily as to knock away one of its frail supports.
canbe10{_}2349{_}The coffin fell to the floor, the glass was shattered to bits by the concussion.
canbe10{_}2350{_}From the opening crawled John Mortonson's cat, which lazily leapt to the floor, sat up, tranquilly wiped its crimson muzzle with a forepaw, then walked with dignity from the room.
canbe10{_}2351{_}THE REALM OF THE UNREAL    For a part of the distance between Auburn and Newcastle the road-- first on one side of a creek and then on the other--occupies the whole bottom of the ravine, being partly cut out of the steep hillside, and partly built up with bowlders removed from the creek- bed by the miners.
canbe10{_}2352{_}The hills are wooded, the course of the ravine is sinuous.
canbe10{_}2353{_}In a dark night careful driving is required in order not to go off into the water.
canbe10{_}2354{_}The night that I have in memory was dark, the creek a torrent, swollen by a recent storm.
canbe10{_}2355{_}I had driven up from Newcastle and was within about a mile of Auburn in the darkest and narrowest part of the ravine, looking intently ahead of my horse for the roadway.
canbe10{_}2356{_}Suddenly I saw a man almost under the animal's nose, and reined in with a jerk that came near setting the creature upon its haunches.
canbe10{_}2357{_}"I beg your pardon," I said; "I did not see you, sir."
canbe10{_}2358{_}"You could hardly be expected to see me," the man replied, civilly, approaching the side of the vehicle; "and the noise of the creek prevented my hearing you."
canbe10{_}2359{_}I at once recognized the voice, although five years had passed since I had heard it.
canbe10{_}2360{_}I was not particularly well pleased to hear it now.
canbe10{_}2361{_}"You are Dr. Dorrimore, I think," said I.
canbe10{_}2362{_}"Yes; and you are my good friend Mr. Manrich.
canbe10{_}2363{_}I am more than glad to see you--the excess," he added, with a light laugh, "being due to the fact that I am going your way, and naturally expect an invitation to ride with you."
canbe10{_}2364{_}"Which I extend with all my heart."
canbe10{_}2365{_}That was not altogether true.
canbe10{_}2366{_}Dr. Dorrimore thanked me as he seated himself beside me, and I drove cautiously forward, as before.
canbe10{_}2367{_}Doubtless it is fancy, but it seems to me now that the remaining distance was made in a chill fog; that I was uncomfortably cold; that the way was longer than ever before, and the town, when we reached it, cheerless, forbidding, and desolate.
canbe10{_}2368{_}It must have been early in the evening, yet I do not recollect a light in any of the houses nor a living thing in the streets.
canbe10{_}2369{_}Dorrimore explained at some length how he happened to be there, and where he had been during the years that had elapsed since I had seen him.
canbe10{_}2370{_}I recall the fact of the narrative, but none of the facts narrated.
canbe10{_}2371{_}He had been in foreign countries and had returned--this is all that my memory retains, and this I already knew.
canbe10{_}2372{_}As to myself I cannot remember that I spoke a word, though doubtless I did.
canbe10{_}2373{_}Of one thing I am distinctly conscious:  the man's presence at my side was strangely distasteful and disquieting--so much so that when I at last pulled up under the lights of the Putnam House I experienced a sense of having escaped some spiritual peril of a nature peculiarly forbidding.
canbe10{_}2374{_}This sense of relief was somewhat modified by the discovery that Dr. Dorrimore was living at the same hotel.
canbe10{_}2375{_}II  In partial explanation of my feelings regarding Dr. Dorrimore I will relate briefly the circumstances under which I had met him some years before.
canbe10{_}2376{_}One evening a half-dozen men of whom I was one were sitting in the library of the Bohemian Club in San Francisco.
canbe10{_}2377{_}The conversation had turned to the subject of sleight-of-hand and the feats of the prestidigitateurs, one of whom was then exhibiting at a local theatre.
canbe10{_}2378{_}"These fellows are pretenders in a double sense," said one of the party; "they can do nothing which it is worth one's while to be made a dupe by.
canbe10{_}2379{_}The humblest wayside juggler in India could mystify them to the verge of lunacy."
canbe10{_}2380{_}"For example, how?"
canbe10{_}2381{_}asked another, lighting a cigar.
canbe10{_}2382{_}"For example, by all their common and familiar performances--throwing large objects into the air which never come down; causing plants to sprout, grow visibly and blossom, in bare ground chosen by spectators; putting a man into a wicker basket, piercing him through and through with a sword while he shrieks and bleeds, and then--the basket being opened nothing is there; tossing the free end of a silken ladder into the air, mounting it and disappearing."
canbe10{_}2383{_}"Nonsense!"
canbe10{_}2384{_}I said, rather uncivilly, I fear.
canbe10{_}2385{_}"You surely do not believe such things?"
canbe10{_}2386{_}"Certainly not:  I have seen them too often."
canbe10{_}2387{_}"But I do," said a journalist of considerable local fame as a picturesque reporter.
canbe10{_}2388{_}"I have so frequently related them that nothing but observation could shake my conviction.
canbe10{_}2389{_}Why, gentlemen, I have my own word for it."
canbe10{_}2390{_}Nobody laughed--all were looking at something behind me.
canbe10{_}2391{_}Turning in my seat I saw a man in evening dress who had just entered the room.
canbe10{_}2392{_}He was exceedingly dark, almost swarthy, with a thin face, black- bearded to the lips, an abundance of coarse black hair in some disorder, a high nose and eyes that glittered with as soulless an expression as those of a cobra.
canbe10{_}2393{_}One of the group rose and introduced him as Dr. Dorrimore, of Calcutta.
canbe10{_}2394{_}As each of us was presented in turn he acknowledged the fact with a profound bow in the Oriental manner, but with nothing of Oriental gravity.
canbe10{_}2395{_}His smile impressed me as cynical and a trifle contemptuous.
canbe10{_}2396{_}His whole demeanor I can describe only as disagreeably engaging.
canbe10{_}2397{_}His presence led the conversation into other channels.
canbe10{_}2398{_}He said little--I do not recall anything of what he did say.
canbe10{_}2399{_}I thought his voice singularly rich and melodious, but it affected me in the same way as his eyes and smile.
canbe10{_}2400{_}In a few minutes I rose to go.
canbe10{_}2401{_}He also rose and put on his overcoat.
canbe10{_}2402{_}"Mr. Manrich," he said, "I am going your way."
canbe10{_}2403{_}"The devil you are!"
canbe10{_}2404{_}I thought.
canbe10{_}2405{_}"How do you know which way I am going?"
canbe10{_}2406{_}Then I said, "I shall be pleased to have your company."
canbe10{_}2407{_}We left the building together.
canbe10{_}2408{_}No cabs were in sight, the street cars had gone to bed, there was a full moon and the cool night air was delightful; we walked up the California street hill.
canbe10{_}2409{_}I took that direction thinking he would naturally wish to take another, toward one of the hotels.
canbe10{_}2410{_}"You do not believe what is told of the Hindu jugglers," he said abruptly.
canbe10{_}2411{_}"How do you know that?"
canbe10{_}2412{_}I asked.
canbe10{_}2413{_}Without replying he laid his hand lightly upon my arm and with the other pointed to the stone sidewalk directly in front.
canbe10{_}2414{_}There, almost at our feet, lay the dead body of a man, the face upturned and white in the moonlight!
canbe10{_}2415{_}A sword whose hilt sparkled with gems stood fixed and upright in the breast; a pool of blood had collected on the stones of the sidewalk.
canbe10{_}2416{_}I was startled and terrified--not only by what I saw, but by the circumstances under which I saw it.
canbe10{_}2417{_}Repeatedly during our ascent of the hill my eyes, I thought, had traversed the whole reach of that sidewalk, from street to street.
canbe10{_}2418{_}How could they have been insensible to this dreadful object now so conspicuous in the white moonlight?
canbe10{_}2419{_}As my dazed faculties cleared I observed that the body was in evening dress; the overcoat thrown wide open revealed the dress-coat, the white tie, the broad expanse of shirt front pierced by the sword.
canbe10{_}2420{_}And--horrible revelation!--the face, except for its pallor, was that of my companion!
canbe10{_}2421{_}It was to the minutest detail of dress and feature Dr. Dorrimore himself.
canbe10{_}2422{_}Bewildered and horrified, I turned to look for the living man.
canbe10{_}2423{_}He was nowhere visible, and with an added terror I retired from the place, down the hill in the direction whence I had come.
canbe10{_}2424{_}I had taken but a few strides when a strong grasp upon my shoulder arrested me.
canbe10{_}2425{_}I came near crying out with terror:  the dead man, the sword still fixed in his breast, stood beside me!
canbe10{_}2426{_}Pulling out the sword with his disengaged hand, he flung it from him, the moonlight glinting upon the jewels of its hilt and the unsullied steel of its blade.
canbe10{_}2427{_}It fell with a clang upon the sidewalk ahead and--vanished!
canbe10{_}2428{_}The man, swarthy as before, relaxed his grasp upon my shoulder and looked at me with the same cynical regard that I had observed on first meeting him.
canbe10{_}2429{_}The dead have not that look--it partly restored me, and turning my head backward, I saw the smooth white expanse of sidewalk, unbroken from street to street.
canbe10{_}2430{_}"What is all this nonsense, you devil?"
canbe10{_}2431{_}I demanded, fiercely enough, though weak and trembling in every limb.
canbe10{_}2432{_}"It is what some are pleased to call jugglery," he answered, with a light, hard laugh.
canbe10{_}2433{_}He turned down Dupont street and I saw him no more until we met in the Auburn ravine.
canbe10{_}2434{_}III  On the day after my second meeting with Dr. Dorrimore I did not see him:  the clerk in the Putnam House explained that a slight illness confined him to his rooms.
canbe10{_}2435{_}That afternoon at the railway station I was surprised and made happy by the unexpected arrival of Miss Margaret Corray and her mother, from Oakland.
canbe10{_}2436{_}This is not a love story.
canbe10{_}2437{_}I am no storyteller, and love as it is cannot be portrayed in a literature dominated and enthralled by the debasing tyranny which "sentences letters" in the name of the Young Girl.
canbe10{_}2438{_}Under the Young Girl's blighting reign--or rather under the rule of those false Ministers of the Censure who have appointed themselves to the custody of her welfare--love      veils her sacred fires, And, unaware, Morality expires,   famished upon the sifted meal and distilled water of a prudish purveyance.
canbe10{_}2439{_}Let it suffice that Miss Corray and I were engaged in marriage.
canbe10{_}2440{_}She and her mother went to the hotel at which I lived, and for two weeks I saw her daily.
canbe10{_}2441{_}That I was happy needs hardly be said; the only bar to my perfect enjoyment of those golden days was the presence of Dr. Dorrimore, whom I had felt compelled to introduce to the ladies.
canbe10{_}2442{_}By them he was evidently held in favor.
canbe10{_}2443{_}What could I say?
canbe10{_}2444{_}I knew absolutely nothing to his discredit.
canbe10{_}2445{_}His manners were those of a cultivated and considerate gentleman; and to women a man's manner is the man.
canbe10{_}2446{_}On one or two occasions when I saw Miss Corray walking with him I was furious, and once had the indiscretion to protest.
canbe10{_}2447{_}Asked for reasons, I had none to give and fancied I saw in her expression a shade of contempt for the vagaries of a jealous mind.
canbe10{_}2448{_}In time I grew morose and consciously disagreeable, and resolved in my madness to return to San Francisco the next day.
canbe10{_}2449{_}Of this, however, I said nothing.
canbe10{_}2450{_}IV  There was at Auburn an old, abandoned cemetery.
canbe10{_}2451{_}It was nearly in the heart of the town, yet by night it was as gruesome a place as the most dismal of human moods could crave.
canbe10{_}2452{_}The railings about the plats were prostrate, decayed, or altogether gone.
canbe10{_}2453{_}Many of the graves were sunken, from others grew sturdy pines, whose roots had committed unspeakable sin.
canbe10{_}2454{_}The headstones were fallen and broken across; brambles overran the ground; the fence was mostly gone, and cows and pigs wandered there at will; the place was a dishonor to the living, a calumny on the dead, a blasphemy against God.
canbe10{_}2455{_}The evening of the day on which I had taken my madman's resolution to depart in anger from all that was dear to me found me in that congenial spot.
canbe10{_}2456{_}The light of the half moon fell ghostly through the foliage of trees in spots and patches, revealing much that was unsightly, and the black shadows seemed conspiracies withholding to the proper time revelations of darker import.
canbe10{_}2457{_}Passing along what had been a gravel path, I saw emerging from shadow the figure of Dr. Dorrimore.
canbe10{_}2458{_}I was myself in shadow, and stood still with clenched hands and set teeth, trying to control the impulse to leap upon and strangle him.
canbe10{_}2459{_}A moment later a second figure joined him and clung to his arm.
canbe10{_}2460{_}It was Margaret Corray!
canbe10{_}2461{_}I cannot rightly relate what occurred.
canbe10{_}2462{_}I know that I sprang forward, bent upon murder; I know that I was found in the gray of the morning, bruised and bloody, with finger marks upon my throat.
canbe10{_}2463{_}I was taken to the Putnam House, where for days I lay in a delirium.
canbe10{_}2464{_}All this I know, for I have been told.
canbe10{_}2465{_}And of my own knowledge I know that when consciousness returned with convalescence I sent for the clerk of the hotel.
canbe10{_}2466{_}"Are Mrs. Corray and her daughter still here?"
canbe10{_}2467{_}I asked.
canbe10{_}2468{_}"What name did you say?"
canbe10{_}2469{_}"Corray."
canbe10{_}2470{_}"Nobody of that name has been here."
canbe10{_}2471{_}"I beg you will not trifle with me," I said petulantly.
canbe10{_}2472{_}"You see that I am all right now; tell me the truth."
canbe10{_}2473{_}"I give you my word," he replied with evident sincerity, "we have had no guests of that name."
canbe10{_}2474{_}His words stupefied me.
canbe10{_}2475{_}I lay for a few moments in silence; then I asked:  "Where is Dr.
canbe10{_}2476{_}Dorrimore?"
canbe10{_}2477{_}"He left on the morning of your fight and has not been heard of since.
canbe10{_}2478{_}It was a rough deal he gave you."
canbe10{_}2479{_}V  Such are the facts of this case.
canbe10{_}2480{_}Margaret Corray is now my wife.
canbe10{_}2481{_}She has never seen Auburn, and during the weeks whose history as it shaped itself in my brain I have endeavored to relate, was living at her home in Oakland, wondering where her lover was and why he did not write.
canbe10{_}2482{_}The other day I saw in the Baltimore Sun the following paragraph:  "Professor Valentine Dorrimore, the hypnotist, had a large audience last night.
canbe10{_}2483{_}The lecturer, who has lived most of his life in India, gave some marvelous exhibitions of his power, hypnotizing anyone who chose to submit himself to the experiment, by merely looking at him.
canbe10{_}2484{_}In fact, he twice hypnotized the entire audience (reporters alone exempted), making all entertain the most extraordinary illusions.
canbe10{_}2485{_}The most valuable feature of the lecture was the disclosure of the methods of the Hindu jugglers in their famous performances, familiar in the mouths of travelers.
canbe10{_}2486{_}The professor declares that these thaumaturgists have acquired such skill in the art which he learned at their feet that they perform their miracles by simply throwing the 'spectators' into a state of hypnosis and telling them what to see and hear.
canbe10{_}2487{_}His assertion that a peculiarly susceptible subject may be kept in the realm of the unreal for weeks, months, and even years, dominated by whatever delusions and hallucinations the operator may from time to time suggest, is a trifle disquieting."
canbe10{_}2488{_}JOHN BARTINE'S WATCH A STORY BY A PHYSICIAN    "The exact time?
canbe10{_}2489{_}Good God!
canbe10{_}2490{_}my friend, why do you insist?
canbe10{_}2491{_}One would think--but what does it matter; it is easily bedtime--isn't that near enough?
canbe10{_}2492{_}But, here, if you must set your watch, take mine and see for yourself."
canbe10{_}2493{_}With that he detached his watch--a tremendously heavy, old-fashioned one--from the chain, and handed it to me; then turned away, and walking across the room to a shelf of books, began an examination of their backs.
canbe10{_}2494{_}His agitation and evident distress surprised me; they appeared reasonless.
canbe10{_}2495{_}Having set my watch by his, I stepped over to where he stood and said, "Thank you."
canbe10{_}2496{_}As he took his timepiece and reattached it to the guard I observed that his hands were unsteady.
canbe10{_}2497{_}With a tact upon which I greatly prided myself, I sauntered carelessly to the sideboard and took some brandy and water; then, begging his pardon for my thoughtlessness, asked him to have some and went back to my seat by the fire, leaving him to help himself, as was our custom.
canbe10{_}2498{_}He did so and presently joined me at the hearth, as tranquil as ever.
canbe10{_}2499{_}This odd little incident occurred in my apartment, where John Bartine was passing an evening.
canbe10{_}2500{_}We had dined together at the club, had come home in a cab and--in short, everything had been done in the most prosaic way; and why John Bartine should break in upon the natural and established order of things to make himself spectacular with a display of emotion, apparently for his own entertainment, I could nowise understand.
canbe10{_}2501{_}The more I thought of it, while his brilliant conversational gifts were commending themselves to my inattention, the more curious I grew, and of course had no difficulty in persuading myself that my curiosity was friendly solicitude.
canbe10{_}2502{_}That is the disguise that curiosity usually assumes to evade resentment.
canbe10{_}2503{_}So I ruined one of the finest sentences of his disregarded monologue by cutting it short without ceremony.
canbe10{_}2504{_}"John Bartine," I said, "you must try to forgive me if I am wrong, but with the light that I have at present I cannot concede your right to go all to pieces when asked the time o' night.
canbe10{_}2505{_}I cannot admit that it is proper to experience a mysterious reluctance to look your own watch in the face and to cherish in my presence, without explanation, painful emotions which are denied to me, and which are none of my business."
canbe10{_}2506{_}To this ridiculous speech Bartine made no immediate reply, but sat looking gravely into the fire.
canbe10{_}2507{_}Fearing that I had offended I was about to apologize and beg him to think no more about the matter, when looking me calmly in the eyes he said:  "My dear fellow, the levity of your manner does not at all disguise the hideous impudence of your demand; but happily I had already decided to tell you what you wish to know, and no manifestation of your unworthiness to hear it shall alter my decision.
canbe10{_}2508{_}Be good enough to give me your attention and you shall hear all about the matter.
canbe10{_}2509{_}"This watch," he said, "had been in my family for three generations before it fell to me.
canbe10{_}2510{_}Its original owner, for whom it was made, was my great-grandfather, Bramwell Olcott Bartine, a wealthy planter of Colonial Virginia, and as stanch a Tory as ever lay awake nights contriving new kinds of maledictions for the head of Mr. Washington, and new methods of aiding and abetting good King George.
canbe10{_}2511{_}One day this worthy gentleman had the deep misfortune to perform for his cause a service of capital importance which was not recognized as legitimate by those who suffered its disadvantages.
canbe10{_}2512{_}It does not matter what it was, but among its minor consequences was my excellent ancestor's arrest one night in his own house by a party of Mr. Washington's rebels.
canbe10{_}2513{_}He was permitted to say farewell to his weeping family, and was then marched away into the darkness which swallowed him up forever.
canbe10{_}2514{_}Not the slenderest clew to his fate was ever found.
canbe10{_}2515{_}After the war the most diligent inquiry and the offer of large rewards failed to turn up any of his captors or any fact concerning his disappearance.
canbe10{_}2516{_}He had disappeared, and that was all."
canbe10{_}2517{_}Something in Bartine's manner that was not in his words--I hardly knew what it was--prompted me to ask:  "What is your view of the matter--of the justice of it?"
canbe10{_}2518{_}"My view of it," he flamed out, bringing his clenched hand down upon the table as if he had been in a public house dicing with blackguards--"my view of it is that it was a characteristically dastardly assassination by that damned traitor, Washington, and his ragamuffin rebels!"
canbe10{_}2519{_}For some minutes nothing was said:  Bartine was recovering his temper, and I waited.
canbe10{_}2520{_}Then I said:  "Was that all?"
canbe10{_}2521{_}"No--there was something else.
canbe10{_}2522{_}A few weeks after my great- grandfather's arrest his watch was found lying on the porch at the front door of his dwelling.
canbe10{_}2523{_}It was wrapped in a sheet of letter paper bearing the name of Rupert Bartine, his only son, my grandfather.
canbe10{_}2524{_}I am wearing that watch."
canbe10{_}2525{_}Bartine paused.
canbe10{_}2526{_}His usually restless black eyes were staring fixedly into the grate, a point of red light in each, reflected from the glowing coals.
canbe10{_}2527{_}He seemed to have forgotten me.
canbe10{_}2528{_}A sudden threshing of the branches of a tree outside one of the windows, and almost at the same instant a rattle of rain against the glass, recalled him to a sense of his surroundings.
canbe10{_}2529{_}A storm had risen, heralded by a single gust of wind, and in a few moments the steady plash of the water on the pavement was distinctly heard.
canbe10{_}2530{_}I hardly know why I relate this incident; it seemed somehow to have a certain significance and relevancy which I am unable now to discern.
canbe10{_}2531{_}It at least added an element of seriousness, almost solemnity.
canbe10{_}2532{_}Bartine resumed:  "I have a singular feeling toward this watch--a kind of affection for it; I like to have it about me, though partly from its weight, and partly for a reason I shall now explain, I seldom carry it.
canbe10{_}2533{_}The reason is this:  Every evening when I have it with me I feel an unaccountable desire to open and consult it, even if I can think of no reason for wishing to know the time.
canbe10{_}2534{_}But if I yield to it, the moment my eyes rest upon the dial I am filled with a mysterious apprehension--a sense of imminent calamity.
canbe10{_}2535{_}And this is the more insupportable the nearer it is to eleven o'clock--by this watch, no matter what the actual hour may be.
canbe10{_}2536{_}After the hands have registered eleven the desire to look is gone; I am entirely indifferent.
canbe10{_}2537{_}Then I can consult the thing as often as I like, with no more emotion than you feel in looking at your own.
canbe10{_}2538{_}Naturally I have trained myself not to look at that watch in the evening before eleven; nothing could induce me.
canbe10{_}2539{_}Your insistence this evening upset me a trifle.
canbe10{_}2540{_}I felt very much as I suppose an opium-eater might feel if his yearning for his special and particular kind of hell were re-enforced by opportunity and advice.
canbe10{_}2541{_}"Now that is my story, and I have told it in the interest of your trumpery science; but if on any evening hereafter you observe me wearing this damnable watch, and you have the thoughtfulness to ask me the hour, I shall beg leave to put you to the inconvenience of being knocked down."
canbe10{_}2542{_}His humor did not amuse me.
canbe10{_}2543{_}I could see that in relating his delusion he was again somewhat disturbed.
canbe10{_}2544{_}His concluding smile was positively ghastly, and his eyes had resumed something more than their old restlessness; they shifted hither and thither about the room with apparent aimlessness and I fancied had taken on a wild expression, such as is sometimes observed in cases of dementia.
canbe10{_}2545{_}Perhaps this was my own imagination, but at any rate I was now persuaded that my friend was afflicted with a most singular and interesting monomania.
canbe10{_}2546{_}Without, I trust, any abatement of my affectionate solicitude for him as a friend, I began to regard him as a patient, rich in possibilities of profitable study.
canbe10{_}2547{_}Why not?
canbe10{_}2548{_}Had he not described his delusion in the interest of science?
canbe10{_}2549{_}Ah, poor fellow, he was doing more for science than he knew:  not only his story but himself was in evidence.
canbe10{_}2550{_}I should cure him if I could, of course, but first I should make a little experiment in psychology-- nay, the experiment itself might be a step in his restoration.
canbe10{_}2551{_}"That is very frank and friendly of you, Bartine," I said cordially, "and I'm rather proud of your confidence.
canbe10{_}2552{_}It is all very odd, certainly.
canbe10{_}2553{_}Do you mind showing me the watch?"
canbe10{_}2554{_}He detached it from his waistcoat, chain and all, and passed it to me without a word.
canbe10{_}2555{_}The case was of gold, very thick and strong, and singularly engraved.
canbe10{_}2556{_}After closely examining the dial and observing that it was nearly twelve o'clock, I opened it at the back and was interested to observe an inner case of ivory, upon which was painted a miniature portrait in that exquisite and delicate manner which was in vogue during the eighteenth century.
canbe10{_}2557{_}"Why, bless my soul!"
canbe10{_}2558{_}I exclaimed, feeling a sharp artistic delight-- "how under the sun did you get that done?
canbe10{_}2559{_}I thought miniature painting on ivory was a lost art."
canbe10{_}2560{_}"That," he replied, gravely smiling, "is not I; it is my excellent great-grandfather, the late Bramwell Olcott Bartine, Esquire, of Virginia.
canbe10{_}2561{_}He was younger then than later--about my age, in fact.
canbe10{_}2562{_}It is said to resemble me; do you think so?"
canbe10{_}2563{_}"Resemble you?
canbe10{_}2564{_}I should say so!
canbe10{_}2565{_}Barring the costume, which I supposed you to have assumed out of compliment to the art--or for vraisemblance, so to say--and the no mustache, that portrait is you in every feature, line, and expression."
canbe10{_}2566{_}No more was said at that time.
canbe10{_}2567{_}Bartine took a book from the table and began reading.
canbe10{_}2568{_}I heard outside the incessant plash of the rain in the street.
canbe10{_}2569{_}There were occasional hurried footfalls on the sidewalks; and once a slower, heavier tread seemed to cease at my door--a policeman, I thought, seeking shelter in the doorway.
canbe10{_}2570{_}The boughs of the trees tapped significantly on the window panes, as if asking for admittance.
canbe10{_}2571{_}I remember it all through these years and years of a wiser, graver life.
canbe10{_}2572{_}Seeing myself unobserved, I took the old-fashioned key that dangled from the chain and quickly turned back the hands of the watch a full hour; then, closing the case, I handed Bartine his property and saw him replace it on his person.
canbe10{_}2573{_}"I think you said," I began, with assumed carelessness, "that after eleven the sight of the dial no longer affects you.
canbe10{_}2574{_}As it is now nearly twelve"--looking at my own timepiece--"perhaps, if you don't resent my pursuit of proof, you will look at it now."
canbe10{_}2575{_}He smiled good-humoredly, pulled out the watch again, opened it, and instantly sprang to his feet with a cry that Heaven has not had the mercy to permit me to forget!
canbe10{_}2576{_}His eyes, their blackness strikingly intensified by the pallor of his face, were fixed upon the watch, which he clutched in both hands.
canbe10{_}2577{_}For some time he remained in that attitude without uttering another sound; then, in a voice that I should not have recognized as his, he said:  "Damn you!
canbe10{_}2578{_}it is two minutes to eleven!"
canbe10{_}2579{_}I was not unprepared for some such outbreak, and without rising replied, calmly enough:  "I beg your pardon; I must have misread your watch in setting my own by it."
canbe10{_}2580{_}He shut the case with a sharp snap and put the watch in his pocket.
canbe10{_}2581{_}He looked at me and made an attempt to smile, but his lower lip quivered and he seemed unable to close his mouth.
canbe10{_}2582{_}His hands, also, were shaking, and he thrust them, clenched, into the pockets of his sack-coat.
canbe10{_}2583{_}The courageous spirit was manifestly endeavoring to subdue the coward body.
canbe10{_}2584{_}The effort was too great; he began to sway from side to side, as from vertigo, and before I could spring from my chair to support him his knees gave way and he pitched awkwardly forward and fell upon his face.
canbe10{_}2585{_}I sprang to assist him to rise; but when John Bartine rises we shall all rise.
canbe10{_}2586{_}The post-mortem examination disclosed nothing; every organ was normal and sound.
canbe10{_}2587{_}But when the body had been prepared for burial a faint dark circle was seen to have developed around the neck; at least I was so assured by several persons who said they saw it, but of my own knowledge I cannot say if that was true.
canbe10{_}2588{_}Nor can I set limitations to the law of heredity.
canbe10{_}2589{_}I do not know that in the spiritual world a sentiment or emotion may not survive the heart that held it, and seek expression in a kindred life, ages removed.
canbe10{_}2590{_}Surely, if I were to guess at the fate of Bramwell Olcott Bartine, I should guess that he was hanged at eleven o'clock in the evening, and that he had been allowed several hours in which to prepare for the change.
canbe10{_}2591{_}As to John Bartine, my friend, my patient for five minutes, and-- Heaven forgive me!--my victim for eternity, there is no more to say.
canbe10{_}2592{_}He is buried, and his watch with him--I saw to that.
canbe10{_}2593{_}May God rest his soul in Paradise, and the soul of his Virginian ancestor, if, indeed, they are two souls.
canbe10{_}2594{_}THE DAMNED THING    I--ONE DOES NOT ALWAYS EAT WHAT IS ON THE TABLE  By the light of a tallow candle which had been placed on one end of a rough table a man was reading something written in a book.
canbe10{_}2595{_}It was an old account book, greatly worn; and the writing was not, apparently, very legible, for the man sometimes held the page close to the flame of the candle to get a stronger light on it.
canbe10{_}2596{_}The shadow of the book would then throw into obscurity a half of the room, darkening a number of faces and figures; for besides the reader, eight other men were present.
canbe10{_}2597{_}Seven of them sat against the rough log walls, silent, motionless, and the room being small, not very far from the table.
canbe10{_}2598{_}By extending an arm any one of them could have touched the eighth man, who lay on the table, face upward, partly covered by a sheet, his arms at his sides.
canbe10{_}2599{_}He was dead.
canbe10{_}2600{_}The man with the book was not reading aloud, and no one spoke; all seemed to be waiting for something to occur; the dead man only was without expectation.
canbe10{_}2601{_}From the blank darkness outside came in, through the aperture that served for a window, all the ever unfamiliar noises of night in the wilderness--the long nameless note of a distant coyote; the stilly pulsing thrill of tireless insects in trees; strange cries of night birds, so different from those of the birds of day; the drone of great blundering beetles, and all that mysterious chorus of small sounds that seem always to have been but half heard when they have suddenly ceased, as if conscious of an indiscretion.
canbe10{_}2602{_}But nothing of all this was noted in that company; its members were not overmuch addicted to idle interest in matters of no practical importance; that was obvious in every line of their rugged faces--obvious even in the dim light of the single candle.
canbe10{_}2603{_}They were evidently men of the vicinity--farmers and woodsmen.
canbe10{_}2604{_}The person reading was a trifle different; one would have said of him that he was of the world, worldly, albeit there was that in his attire which attested a certain fellowship with the organisms of his environment.
canbe10{_}2605{_}His coat would hardly have passed muster in San Francisco; his foot-gear was not of urban origin, and the hat that lay by him on the floor (he was the only one uncovered) was such that if one had considered it as an article of mere personal adornment he would have missed its meaning.
canbe10{_}2606{_}In countenance the man was rather prepossessing, with just a hint of sternness; though that he may have assumed or cultivated, as appropriate to one in authority.
canbe10{_}2607{_}For he was a coroner.
canbe10{_}2608{_}It was by virtue of his office that he had possession of the book in which he was reading; it had been found among the dead man's effects--in his cabin, where the inquest was now taking place.
canbe10{_}2609{_}When the coroner had finished reading he put the book into his breast pocket.
canbe10{_}2610{_}At that moment the door was pushed open and a young man entered.
canbe10{_}2611{_}He, clearly, was not of mountain birth and breeding:  he was clad as those who dwell in cities.
canbe10{_}2612{_}His clothing was dusty, however, as from travel.
canbe10{_}2613{_}He had, in fact, been riding hard to attend the inquest.
canbe10{_}2614{_}The coroner nodded; no one else greeted him.
canbe10{_}2615{_}"We have waited for you," said the coroner.
canbe10{_}2616{_}"It is necessary to have done with this business to-night."
canbe10{_}2617{_}The young man smiled.
canbe10{_}2618{_}"I am sorry to have kept you," he said.
canbe10{_}2619{_}"I went away, not to evade your summons, but to post to my newspaper an account of what I suppose I am called back to relate."
canbe10{_}2620{_}The coroner smiled.
canbe10{_}2621{_}"The account that you posted to your newspaper," he said, "differs, probably, from that which you will give here under oath."
canbe10{_}2622{_}"That," replied the other, rather hotly and with a visible flush, "is as you please.
canbe10{_}2623{_}I used manifold paper and have a copy of what I sent.
canbe10{_}2624{_}It was not written as news, for it is incredible, but as fiction.
canbe10{_}2625{_}It may go as a part of my testimony under oath."
canbe10{_}2626{_}"But you say it is incredible."
canbe10{_}2627{_}"That is nothing to you, sir, if I also swear that it is true."
canbe10{_}2628{_}The coroner was silent for a time, his eyes upon the floor.
canbe10{_}2629{_}The men about the sides of the cabin talked in whispers, but seldom withdrew their gaze from the face of the corpse.
canbe10{_}2630{_}Presently the coroner lifted his eyes and said:  "We will resume the inquest."
canbe10{_}2631{_}The men removed their hats.
canbe10{_}2632{_}The witness was sworn.
canbe10{_}2633{_}"What is your name?"
canbe10{_}2634{_}the coroner asked.
canbe10{_}2635{_}"William Harker."
canbe10{_}2636{_}"Age?"
canbe10{_}2637{_}"Twenty-seven."
canbe10{_}2638{_}"You knew the deceased, Hugh Morgan?"
canbe10{_}2639{_}"Yes."
canbe10{_}2640{_}"You were with him when he died?"
canbe10{_}2641{_}"Near him."
canbe10{_}2642{_}"How did that happen--your presence, I mean?"
canbe10{_}2643{_}"I was visiting him at this place to shoot and fish.
canbe10{_}2644{_}A part of my purpose, however, was to study him and his odd, solitary way of life.
canbe10{_}2645{_}He seemed a good model for a character in fiction.
canbe10{_}2646{_}I sometimes write stories."
canbe10{_}2647{_}"I sometimes read them."
canbe10{_}2648{_}"Thank you."
canbe10{_}2649{_}"Stories in general--not yours."
canbe10{_}2650{_}Some of the jurors laughed.
canbe10{_}2651{_}Against a sombre background humor shows high lights.
canbe10{_}2652{_}Soldiers in the intervals of battle laugh easily, and a jest in the death chamber conquers by surprise.
canbe10{_}2653{_}"Relate the circumstances of this man's death," said the coroner.
canbe10{_}2654{_}"You may use any notes or memoranda that you please."
canbe10{_}2655{_}The witness understood.
canbe10{_}2656{_}Pulling a manuscript from his breast pocket he held it near the candle and turning the leaves until he found the passage that he wanted began to read.
canbe10{_}2657{_}II--WHAT MAY HAPPEN IN A FIELD OF WILD OATS  " .
canbe10{_}2658{_}.
canbe10{_}2659{_}.
canbe10{_}2660{_}The sun had hardly risen when we left the house.
canbe10{_}2661{_}We were looking for quail, each with a shotgun, but we had only one dog.
canbe10{_}2662{_}Morgan said that our best ground was beyond a certain ridge that he pointed out, and we crossed it by a trail through the chaparral.
canbe10{_}2663{_}On the other side was comparatively level ground, thickly covered with wild oats.
canbe10{_}2664{_}As we emerged from the chaparral Morgan was but a few yards in advance.
canbe10{_}2665{_}Suddenly we heard, at a little distance to our right and partly in front, a noise as of some animal thrashing about in the bushes, which we could see were violently agitated.
canbe10{_}2666{_}"'We've started a deer,' I said.
canbe10{_}2667{_}'I wish we had brought a rifle.'
canbe10{_}2668{_}"Morgan, who had stopped and was intently watching the agitated chaparral, said nothing, but had cocked both barrels of his gun and was holding it in readiness to aim.
canbe10{_}2669{_}I thought him a trifle excited, which surprised me, for he had a reputation for exceptional coolness, even in moments of sudden and imminent peril.
canbe10{_}2670{_}"'O, come,' I said.
canbe10{_}2671{_}'You are not going to fill up a deer with quail- shot, are you?'
canbe10{_}2672{_}"Still he did not reply; but catching a sight of his face as he turned it slightly toward me I was struck by the intensity of his look.
canbe10{_}2673{_}Then I understood that we had serious business in hand and my first conjecture was that we had 'jumped' a grizzly.
canbe10{_}2674{_}I advanced to Morgan's side, cocking my piece as I moved.
canbe10{_}2675{_}"The bushes were now quiet and the sounds had ceased, but Morgan was as attentive to the place as before.
canbe10{_}2676{_}"'What is it?
canbe10{_}2677{_}What the devil is it?'
canbe10{_}2678{_}I asked.
canbe10{_}2679{_}"'That Damned Thing!'
canbe10{_}2680{_}he replied, without turning his head.
canbe10{_}2681{_}His voice was husky and unnatural.
canbe10{_}2682{_}He trembled visibly.
canbe10{_}2683{_}"I was about to speak further, when I observed the wild oats near the place of the disturbance moving in the most inexplicable way.
canbe10{_}2684{_}I can hardly describe it.
canbe10{_}2685{_}It seemed as if stirred by a streak of wind, which not only bent it, but pressed it down--crushed it so that it did not rise; and this movement was slowly prolonging itself directly toward us.
canbe10{_}2686{_}"Nothing that I had ever seen had affected me so strangely as this unfamiliar and unaccountable phenomenon, yet I am unable to recall any sense of fear.
canbe10{_}2687{_}I remember--and tell it here because, singularly enough, I recollected it then--that once in looking carelessly out of an open window I momentarily mistook a small tree close at hand for one of a group of larger trees at a little distance away.
canbe10{_}2688{_}It looked the same size as the others, but being more distinctly and sharply defined in mass and detail seemed out of harmony with them.
canbe10{_}2689{_}It was a mere falsification of the law of aerial perspective, but it startled, almost terrified me.
canbe10{_}2690{_}We so rely upon the orderly operation of familiar natural laws that any seeming suspension of them is noted as a menace to our safety, a warning of unthinkable calamity.
canbe10{_}2691{_}So now the apparently causeless movement of the herbage and the slow, undeviating approach of the line of disturbance were distinctly disquieting.
canbe10{_}2692{_}My companion appeared actually frightened, and I could hardly credit my senses when I saw him suddenly throw his gun to his shoulder and fire both barrels at the agitated grain!
canbe10{_}2693{_}Before the smoke of the discharge had cleared away I heard a loud savage cry--a scream like that of a wild animal--and flinging his gun upon the ground Morgan sprang away and ran swiftly from the spot.
canbe10{_}2694{_}At the same instant I was thrown violently to the ground by the impact of something unseen in the smoke--some soft, heavy substance that seemed thrown against me with great force.
canbe10{_}2695{_}"Before I could get upon my feet and recover my gun, which seemed to have been struck from my hands, I heard Morgan crying out as if in mortal agony, and mingling with his cries were such hoarse, savage sounds as one hears from fighting dogs.
canbe10{_}2696{_}Inexpressibly terrified, I struggled to my feet and looked in the direction of Morgan's retreat; and may Heaven in mercy spare me from another sight like that!
canbe10{_}2697{_}At a distance of less than thirty yards was my friend, down upon one knee, his head thrown back at a frightful angle, hatless, his long hair in disorder and his whole body in violent movement from side to side, backward and forward.
canbe10{_}2698{_}His right arm was lifted and seemed to lack the hand--at least, I could see none.
canbe10{_}2699{_}The other arm was invisible.
canbe10{_}2700{_}At times, as my memory now reports this extraordinary scene, I could discern but a part of his body; it was as if he had been partly blotted out--I cannot otherwise express it--then a shifting of his position would bring it all into view again.
canbe10{_}2701{_}"All this must have occurred within a few seconds, yet in that time Morgan assumed all the postures of a determined wrestler vanquished by superior weight and strength.
canbe10{_}2702{_}I saw nothing but him, and him not always distinctly.
canbe10{_}2703{_}During the entire incident his shouts and curses were heard, as if through an enveloping uproar of such sounds of rage and fury as I had never heard from the throat of man or brute!
