canbe10{_}2704{_}"For a moment only I stood irresolute, then throwing down my gun I ran forward to my friend's assistance.
canbe10{_}2705{_}I had a vague belief that he was suffering from a fit, or some form of convulsion.
canbe10{_}2706{_}Before I could reach his side he was down and quiet.
canbe10{_}2707{_}All sounds had ceased, but with a feeling of such terror as even these awful events had not inspired I now saw again the mysterious movement of the wild oats, prolonging itself from the trampled area about the prostrate man toward the edge of a wood.
canbe10{_}2708{_}It was only when it had reached the wood that I was able to withdraw my eyes and look at my companion.
canbe10{_}2709{_}He was dead."
canbe10{_}2710{_}III--A MAN THOUGH NAKED MAY BE IN RAGS  The coroner rose from his seat and stood beside the dead man.
canbe10{_}2711{_}Lifting an edge of the sheet he pulled it away, exposing the entire body, altogether naked and showing in the candle-light a claylike yellow.
canbe10{_}2712{_}It had, however, broad maculations of bluish black, obviously caused by extravasated blood from contusions.
canbe10{_}2713{_}The chest and sides looked as if they had been beaten with a bludgeon.
canbe10{_}2714{_}There were dreadful lacerations; the skin was torn in strips and shreds.
canbe10{_}2715{_}The coroner moved round to the end of the table and undid a silk handkerchief which had been passed under the chin and knotted on the top of the head.
canbe10{_}2716{_}When the handkerchief was drawn away it exposed what had been the throat.
canbe10{_}2717{_}Some of the jurors who had risen to get a better view repented their curiosity and turned away their faces.
canbe10{_}2718{_}Witness Harker went to the open window and leaned out across the sill, faint and sick.
canbe10{_}2719{_}Dropping the handkerchief upon the dead man's neck the coroner stepped to an angle of the room and from a pile of clothing produced one garment after another, each of which he held up a moment for inspection.
canbe10{_}2720{_}All were torn, and stiff with blood.
canbe10{_}2721{_}The jurors did not make a closer inspection.
canbe10{_}2722{_}They seemed rather uninterested.
canbe10{_}2723{_}They had, in truth, seen all this before; the only thing that was new to them being Harker's testimony.
canbe10{_}2724{_}"Gentlemen," the coroner said, "we have no more evidence, I think.
canbe10{_}2725{_}Your duty has been already explained to you; if there is nothing you wish to ask you may go outside and consider your verdict."
canbe10{_}2726{_}The foreman rose--a tall, bearded man of sixty, coarsely clad.
canbe10{_}2727{_}"I should like to ask one question, Mr. Coroner," he said.
canbe10{_}2728{_}"What asylum did this yer last witness escape from?"
canbe10{_}2729{_}"Mr. Harker," said the coroner, gravely and tranquilly, "from what asylum did you last escape?"
canbe10{_}2730{_}Harker flushed crimson again, but said nothing, and the seven jurors rose and solemnly filed out of the cabin.
canbe10{_}2731{_}"If you have done insulting me, sir," said Harker, as soon as he and the officer were left alone with the dead man, "I suppose I am at liberty to go?"
canbe10{_}2732{_}"Yes."
canbe10{_}2733{_}Harker started to leave, but paused, with his hand on the door latch.
canbe10{_}2734{_}The habit of his profession was strong in him--stronger than his sense of personal dignity.
canbe10{_}2735{_}He turned about and said:  "The book that you have there--I recognize it as Morgan's diary.
canbe10{_}2736{_}You seemed greatly interested in it; you read in it while I was testifying.
canbe10{_}2737{_}May I see it?
canbe10{_}2738{_}The public would like--"  "The book will cut no figure in this matter," replied the official, slipping it into his coat pocket; "all the entries in it were made before the writer's death."
canbe10{_}2739{_}As Harker passed out of the house the jury reentered and stood about the table, on which the now covered corpse showed under the sheet with sharp definition.
canbe10{_}2740{_}The foreman seated himself near the candle, produced from his breast pocket a pencil and scrap of paper and wrote rather laboriously the following verdict, which with various degrees of effort all signed:  "We, the jury, do find that the remains come to their death at the hands of a mountain lion, but some of us thinks, all the same, they had fits."
canbe10{_}2741{_}IV--AN EXPLANATION FROM THE TOMB  In the diary of the late Hugh Morgan are certain interesting entries having, possibly, a scientific value as suggestions.
canbe10{_}2742{_}At the inquest upon his body the book was not put in evidence; possibly the coroner thought it not worth while to confuse the jury.

canbe10{_}2746{_}would run in a half-circle, keeping his head turned always toward the centre, and again he would stand still, barking furiously.
canbe10{_}2747{_}At last he ran away into the brush as fast as he could go.

canbe10{_}2781{_}7.--I have the solution of the mystery; it came to me last night--suddenly, as by revelation.
canbe10{_}2782{_}How simple--how terribly simple!
canbe10{_}2783{_}"There are sounds that we cannot hear.
canbe10{_}2784{_}At either end of the scale are notes that stir no chord of that imperfect instrument, the human ear.
canbe10{_}2785{_}They are too high or too grave.
canbe10{_}2786{_}I have observed a flock of blackbirds occupying an entire tree-top--the tops of several trees-- and all in full song.
canbe10{_}2787{_}Suddenly--in a moment--at absolutely the same instant--all spring into the air and fly away.
canbe10{_}2788{_}How?
canbe10{_}2789{_}They could not all see one another--whole tree-tops intervened.
canbe10{_}2790{_}At no point could a leader have been visible to all.
canbe10{_}2791{_}There must have been a signal of warning or command, high and shrill above the din, but by me unheard.
canbe10{_}2792{_}I have observed, too, the same simultaneous flight when all were silent, among not only blackbirds, but other birds--quail, for example, widely separated by bushes--even on opposite sides of a hill.
canbe10{_}2793{_}"It is known to seamen that a school of whales basking or sporting on the surface of the ocean, miles apart, with the convexity of the earth between, will sometimes dive at the same instant--all gone out of sight in a moment.
canbe10{_}2794{_}The signal has been sounded--too grave for the ear of the sailor at the masthead and his comrades on the deck--who nevertheless feel its vibrations in the ship as the stones of a cathedral are stirred by the bass of the organ.
canbe10{_}2795{_}"As with sounds, so with colors.
canbe10{_}2796{_}At each end of the solar spectrum the chemist can detect the presence of what are known as 'actinic' rays.
canbe10{_}2797{_}They represent colors--integral colors in the composition of light--which we are unable to discern.
canbe10{_}2798{_}The human eye is an imperfect instrument; its range is but a few octaves of the real 'chromatic scale.'
canbe10{_}2799{_}I am not mad; there are colors that we cannot see.
canbe10{_}2800{_}"And, God help me!
canbe10{_}2801{_}the Damned Thing is of such a color!"
canbe10{_}2802{_}HAITA THE SHEPHERD    In the heart of Haita the illusions of youth had not been supplanted by those of age and experience.
canbe10{_}2803{_}His thoughts were pure and pleasant, for his life was simple and his soul devoid of ambition.
canbe10{_}2804{_}He rose with the sun and went forth to pray at the shrine of Hastur, the god of shepherds, who heard and was pleased.
canbe10{_}2805{_}After performance of this pious rite Haita unbarred the gate of the fold and with a cheerful mind drove his flock afield, eating his morning meal of curds and oat cake as he went, occasionally pausing to add a few berries, cold with dew, or to drink of the waters that came away from the hills to join the stream in the middle of the valley and be borne along with it, he knew not whither.
canbe10{_}2806{_}During the long summer day, as his sheep cropped the good grass which the gods had made to grow for them, or lay with their forelegs doubled under their breasts and chewed the cud, Haita, reclining in the shadow of a tree, or sitting upon a rock, played so sweet music upon his reed pipe that sometimes from the corner of his eye he got accidental glimpses of the minor sylvan deities, leaning forward out of the copse to hear; but if he looked at them directly they vanished.
canbe10{_}2807{_}From this--for he must be thinking if he would not turn into one of his own sheep--he drew the solemn inference that happiness may come if not sought, but if looked for will never be seen; for next to the favor of Hastur, who never disclosed himself, Haita most valued the friendly interest of his neighbors, the shy immortals of the wood and stream.
canbe10{_}2808{_}At nightfall he drove his flock back to the fold, saw that the gate was secure and retired to his cave for refreshment and for dreams.
canbe10{_}2809{_}So passed his life, one day like another, save when the storms uttered the wrath of an offended god.
canbe10{_}2810{_}Then Haita cowered in his cave, his face hidden in his hands, and prayed that he alone might be punished for his sins and the world saved from destruction.
canbe10{_}2811{_}Sometimes when there was a great rain, and the stream came out of its banks, compelling him to urge his terrified flock to the uplands, he interceded for the people in the cities which he had been told lay in the plain beyond the two blue hills forming the gateway of his valley.
canbe10{_}2812{_}"It is kind of thee, O Hastur," so he prayed, "to give me mountains so near to my dwelling and my fold that I and my sheep can escape the angry torrents; but the rest of the world thou must thyself deliver in some way that I know not of, or I will no longer worship thee."
canbe10{_}2813{_}And Hastur, knowing that Haita was a youth who kept his word, spared the cities and turned the waters into the sea.
canbe10{_}2814{_}So he had lived since he could remember.
canbe10{_}2815{_}He could not rightly conceive any other mode of existence.
canbe10{_}2816{_}The holy hermit who dwelt at the head of the valley, a full hour's journey away, from whom he had heard the tale of the great cities where dwelt people--poor souls!-- who had no sheep, gave him no knowledge of that early time, when, so he reasoned, he must have been small and helpless like a lamb.
canbe10{_}2817{_}It was through thinking on these mysteries and marvels, and on that horrible change to silence and decay which he felt sure must some time come to him, as he had seen it come to so many of his flock--as it came to all living things except the birds--that Haita first became conscious how miserable and hopeless was his lot.
canbe10{_}2818{_}"It is necessary," he said, "that I know whence and how I came; for how can one perform his duties unless able to judge what they are by the way in which he was intrusted with them?
canbe10{_}2819{_}And what contentment can I have when I know not how long it is going to last?
canbe10{_}2820{_}Perhaps before another sun I may be changed, and then what will become of the sheep?
canbe10{_}2821{_}What, indeed, will have become of me?"
canbe10{_}2822{_}Pondering these things Haita became melancholy and morose.
canbe10{_}2823{_}He no longer spoke cheerfully to his flock, nor ran with alacrity to the shrine of Hastur.
canbe10{_}2824{_}In every breeze he heard whispers of malign deities whose existence he now first observed.
canbe10{_}2825{_}Every cloud was a portent signifying disaster, and the darkness was full of terrors.
canbe10{_}2826{_}His reed pipe when applied to his lips gave out no melody, but a dismal wail; the sylvan and riparian intelligences no longer thronged the thicket-side to listen, but fled from the sound, as he knew by the stirred leaves and bent flowers.
canbe10{_}2827{_}He relaxed his vigilance and many of his sheep strayed away into the hills and were lost.
canbe10{_}2828{_}Those that remained became lean and ill for lack of good pasturage, for he would not seek it for them, but conducted them day after day to the same spot, through mere abstraction, while puzzling about life and death--of immortality he knew not.
canbe10{_}2829{_}One day while indulging in the gloomiest reflections he suddenly sprang from the rock upon which he sat, and with a determined gesture of the right hand exclaimed:  "I will no longer be a suppliant for knowledge which the gods withhold.
canbe10{_}2830{_}Let them look to it that they do me no wrong.
canbe10{_}2831{_}I will do my duty as best I can and if I err upon their own heads be it!"
canbe10{_}2832{_}Suddenly, as he spoke, a great brightness fell about him, causing him to look upward, thinking the sun had burst through a rift in the clouds; but there were no clouds.
canbe10{_}2833{_}No more than an arm's length away stood a beautiful maiden.
canbe10{_}2834{_}So beautiful she was that the flowers about her feet folded their petals in despair and bent their heads in token of submission; so sweet her look that the humming birds thronged her eyes, thrusting their thirsty bills almost into them, and the wild bees were about her lips.
canbe10{_}2835{_}And such was her brightness that the shadows of all objects lay divergent from her feet, turning as she moved.
canbe10{_}2836{_}Haita was entranced.
canbe10{_}2837{_}Rising, he knelt before her in adoration, and she laid her hand upon his head.
canbe10{_}2838{_}"Come," she said in a voice that had the music of all the bells of his flock--"come, thou art not to worship me, who am no goddess, but if thou art truthful and dutiful I will abide with thee."
canbe10{_}2839{_}Haita seized her hand, and stammering his joy and gratitude arose, and hand in hand they stood and smiled into each other's eyes.
canbe10{_}2840{_}He gazed on her with reverence and rapture.
canbe10{_}2841{_}He said:  "I pray thee, lovely maid, tell me thy name and whence and why thou comest."
canbe10{_}2842{_}At this she laid a warning finger on her lip and began to withdraw.
canbe10{_}2843{_}Her beauty underwent a visible alteration that made him shudder, he knew not why, for still she was beautiful.
canbe10{_}2844{_}The landscape was darkened by a giant shadow sweeping across the valley with the speed of a vulture.
canbe10{_}2845{_}In the obscurity the maiden's figure grew dim and indistinct and her voice seemed to come from a distance, as she said, in a tone of sorrowful reproach:  "Presumptuous and ungrateful youth!
canbe10{_}2846{_}must I then so soon leave thee?
canbe10{_}2847{_}Would nothing do but thou must at once break the eternal compact?"
canbe10{_}2848{_}Inexpressibly grieved, Haita fell upon his knees and implored her to remain--rose and sought her in the deepening darkness--ran in circles, calling to her aloud, but all in vain.
canbe10{_}2849{_}She was no longer visible, but out of the gloom he heard her voice saying:  "Nay, thou shalt not have me by seeking.
canbe10{_}2850{_}Go to thy duty, faithless shepherd, or we shall never meet again."
canbe10{_}2851{_}Night had fallen; the wolves were howling in the hills and the terrified sheep crowding about Haita's feet.
canbe10{_}2852{_}In the demands of the hour he forgot his disappointment, drove his sheep to the fold and repairing to the place of worship poured out his heart in gratitude to Hastur for permitting him to save his flock, then retired to his cave and slept.
canbe10{_}2853{_}When Haita awoke the sun was high and shone in at the cave, illuminating it with a great glory.
canbe10{_}2854{_}And there, beside him, sat the maiden.
canbe10{_}2855{_}She smiled upon him with a smile that seemed the visible music of his pipe of reeds.
canbe10{_}2856{_}He dared not speak, fearing to offend her as before, for he knew not what he could venture to say.
canbe10{_}2857{_}"Because," she said, "thou didst thy duty by the flock, and didst not forget to thank Hastur for staying the wolves of the night, I am come to thee again.
canbe10{_}2858{_}Wilt thou have me for a companion?"
canbe10{_}2859{_}"Who would not have thee forever?"
canbe10{_}2860{_}replied Haita.
canbe10{_}2861{_}"Oh!
canbe10{_}2862{_}never again leave me until--until I--change and become silent and motionless."
canbe10{_}2863{_}Haita had no word for death.
canbe10{_}2864{_}"I wish, indeed," he continued, "that thou wert of my own sex, that we might wrestle and run races and so never tire of being together."
canbe10{_}2865{_}At these words the maiden arose and passed out of the cave, and Haita, springing from his couch of fragrant boughs to overtake and detain her, observed to his astonishment that the rain was falling and the stream in the middle of the valley had come out of its banks.
canbe10{_}2866{_}The sheep were bleating in terror, for the rising waters had invaded their fold.
canbe10{_}2867{_}And there was danger for the unknown cities of the distant plain.
canbe10{_}2868{_}It was many days before Haita saw the maiden again.
canbe10{_}2869{_}One day he was returning from the head of the valley, where he had gone with ewe's milk and oat cake and berries for the holy hermit, who was too old and feeble to provide himself with food.
canbe10{_}2870{_}"Poor old man!"
canbe10{_}2871{_}he said aloud, as he trudged along homeward.
canbe10{_}2872{_}"I will return to-morrow and bear him on my back to my own dwelling, where I can care for him.
canbe10{_}2873{_}Doubtless it is for this that Hastur has reared me all these many years, and gives me health and strength."
canbe10{_}2874{_}As he spoke, the maiden, clad in glittering garments, met him in the path with a smile that took away his breath.
canbe10{_}2875{_}"I am come again," she said, "to dwell with thee if thou wilt now have me, for none else will.
canbe10{_}2876{_}Thou mayest have learned wisdom, and art willing to take me as I am, nor care to know."
canbe10{_}2877{_}Haita threw himself at her feet.
canbe10{_}2878{_}"Beautiful being," he cried, "if thou wilt but deign to accept all the devotion of my heart and soul-- after Hastur be served--it is thine forever.
canbe10{_}2879{_}But, alas!
canbe10{_}2880{_}thou art capricious and wayward.
canbe10{_}2881{_}Before to-morrow's sun I may lose thee again.
canbe10{_}2882{_}Promise, I beseech thee, that however in my ignorance I may offend, thou wilt forgive and remain always with me."
canbe10{_}2883{_}Scarcely had he finished speaking when a troop of bears came out of the hills, racing toward him with crimson mouths and fiery eyes.
canbe10{_}2884{_}The maiden again vanished, and he turned and fled for his life.
canbe10{_}2885{_}Nor did he stop until he was in the cot of the holy hermit, whence he had set out.
canbe10{_}2886{_}Hastily barring the door against the bears he cast himself upon the ground and wept.
canbe10{_}2887{_}"My son," said the hermit from his couch of straw, freshly gathered that morning by Haita's hands, "it is not like thee to weep for bears--tell me what sorrow hath befallen thee, that age may minister to the hurts of youth with such balms as it hath of its wisdom."
canbe10{_}2888{_}Haita told him all:  how thrice he had met the radiant maid, and thrice she had left him forlorn.
canbe10{_}2889{_}He related minutely all that had passed between them, omitting no word of what had been said.
canbe10{_}2890{_}When he had ended, the holy hermit was a moment silent, then said: "My son, I have attended to thy story, and I know the maiden.
canbe10{_}2891{_}I have myself seen her, as have many.
canbe10{_}2892{_}Know, then, that her name, which she would not even permit thee to inquire, is Happiness.
canbe10{_}2893{_}Thou saidst the truth to her, that she is capricious for she imposeth conditions that man cannot fulfill, and delinquency is punished by desertion.
canbe10{_}2894{_}She cometh only when unsought, and will not be questioned.
canbe10{_}2895{_}One manifestation of curiosity, one sign of doubt, one expression of misgiving, and she is away!
canbe10{_}2896{_}How long didst thou have her at any time before she fled?"
canbe10{_}2897{_}"Only a single instant," answered Haita, blushing with shame at the confession.
canbe10{_}2898{_}"Each time I drove her away in one moment."
canbe10{_}2899{_}"Unfortunate youth!"
canbe10{_}2900{_}said the holy hermit, "but for thine indiscretion thou mightst have had her for two."
canbe10{_}2901{_}AN INHABITANT OF CARCOSA    For there be divers sorts of death--some wherein the body remaineth; and in some it vanisheth quite away with the spirit.
canbe10{_}2902{_}This commonly occurreth only in solitude (such is God's will) and, none seeing the end, we say the man is lost, or gone on a long journey--which indeed he hath; but sometimes it hath happened in sight of many, as abundant testimony showeth.
canbe10{_}2903{_}In one kind of death the spirit also dieth, and this it hath been known to do while yet the body was in vigor for many years.
canbe10{_}2904{_}Sometimes, as is veritably attested, it dieth with the body, but after a season is raised up again in that place where the body did decay.
canbe10{_}2905{_}Pondering these words of Hali (whom God rest) and questioning their full meaning, as one who, having an intimation, yet doubts if there be not something behind, other than that which he has discerned, I noted not whither I had strayed until a sudden chill wind striking my face revived in me a sense of my surroundings.
canbe10{_}2906{_}I observed with astonishment that everything seemed unfamiliar.
canbe10{_}2907{_}On every side of me stretched a bleak and desolate expanse of plain, covered with a tall overgrowth of sere grass, which rustled and whistled in the autumn wind with heaven knows what mysterious and disquieting suggestion.
canbe10{_}2908{_}Protruded at long intervals above it, stood strangely shaped and somber-colored rocks, which seemed to have an understanding with one another and to exchange looks of uncomfortable significance, as if they had reared their heads to watch the issue of some foreseen event.
canbe10{_}2909{_}A few blasted trees here and there appeared as leaders in this malevolent conspiracy of silent expectation.
canbe10{_}2910{_}The day, I thought, must be far advanced, though the sun was invisible; and although sensible that the air was raw and chill my consciousness of that fact was rather mental than physical--I had no feeling of discomfort.
canbe10{_}2911{_}Over all the dismal landscape a canopy of low, lead-colored clouds hung like a visible curse.
canbe10{_}2912{_}In all this there were a menace and a portent--a hint of evil, an intimation of doom.
canbe10{_}2913{_}Bird, beast, or insect there was none.
canbe10{_}2914{_}The wind sighed in the bare branches of the dead trees and the gray grass bent to whisper its dread secret to the earth; but no other sound nor motion broke the awful repose of that dismal place.
canbe10{_}2915{_}I observed in the herbage a number of weather-worn stones, evidently shaped with tools.
canbe10{_}2916{_}They were broken, covered with moss and half sunken in the earth.
canbe10{_}2917{_}Some lay prostrate, some leaned at various angles, none was vertical.
canbe10{_}2918{_}They were obviously headstones of graves, though the graves themselves no longer existed as either mounds or depressions; the years had leveled all.
canbe10{_}2919{_}Scattered here and there, more massive blocks showed where some pompous tomb or ambitious monument had once flung its feeble defiance at oblivion.
canbe10{_}2920{_}So old seemed these relics, these vestiges of vanity and memorials of affection and piety, so battered and worn and stained--so neglected, deserted, forgotten the place, that I could not help thinking myself the discoverer of the burial-ground of a prehistoric race of men whose very name was long extinct.
canbe10{_}2921{_}Filled with these reflections, I was for some time heedless of the sequence of my own experiences, but soon I thought, "How came I hither?"
canbe10{_}2922{_}A moment's reflection seemed to make this all clear and explain at the same time, though in a disquieting way, the singular character with which my fancy had invested all that I saw or heard.
canbe10{_}2923{_}I was ill.
canbe10{_}2924{_}I remembered now that I had been prostrated by a sudden fever, and that my family had told me that in my periods of delirium I had constantly cried out for liberty and air, and had been held in bed to prevent my escape out-of-doors.
canbe10{_}2925{_}Now I had eluded the vigilance of my attendants and had wandered hither to--to where?
canbe10{_}2926{_}I could not conjecture.
canbe10{_}2927{_}Clearly I was at a considerable distance from the city where I dwelt--the ancient and famous city of Carcosa.
canbe10{_}2928{_}No signs of human life were anywhere visible nor audible; no rising smoke, no watch-dog's bark, no lowing of cattle, no shouts of children at play--nothing but that dismal burial-place, with its air of mystery and dread, due to my own disordered brain.
canbe10{_}2929{_}Was I not becoming again delirious, there beyond human aid?
canbe10{_}2930{_}Was it not indeed ALL an illusion of my madness?
canbe10{_}2931{_}I called aloud the names of my wives and sons, reached out my hands in search of theirs, even as I walked among the crumbling stones and in the withered grass.
canbe10{_}2932{_}A noise behind me caused me to turn about.
canbe10{_}2933{_}A wild animal--a lynx-- was approaching.
canbe10{_}2934{_}The thought came to me:  If I break down here in the desert--if the fever return and I fail, this beast will be at my throat.
canbe10{_}2935{_}I sprang toward it, shouting.
canbe10{_}2936{_}It trotted tranquilly by within a hand's breadth of me and disappeared behind a rock.
canbe10{_}2937{_}A moment later a man's head appeared to rise out of the ground a short distance away.
canbe10{_}2938{_}He was ascending the farther slope of a low hill whose crest was hardly to be distinguished from the general level.
canbe10{_}2939{_}His whole figure soon came into view against the background of gray cloud.
canbe10{_}2940{_}He was half naked, half clad in skins.
canbe10{_}2941{_}His hair was unkempt, his beard long and ragged.
canbe10{_}2942{_}In one hand he carried a bow and arrow; the other held a blazing torch with a long trail of black smoke.
canbe10{_}2943{_}He walked slowly and with caution, as if he feared falling into some open grave concealed by the tall grass.
canbe10{_}2944{_}This strange apparition surprised but did not alarm, and taking such a course as to intercept him I met him almost face to face, accosting him with the familiar salutation, "God keep you."
canbe10{_}2945{_}He gave no heed, nor did he arrest his pace.
canbe10{_}2946{_}"Good stranger," I continued, "I am ill and lost.
canbe10{_}2947{_}Direct me, I beseech you, to Carcosa."
canbe10{_}2948{_}The man broke into a barbarous chant in an unknown tongue, passing on and away.
canbe10{_}2949{_}An owl on the branch of a decayed tree hooted dismally and was answered by another in the distance.
canbe10{_}2950{_}Looking upward, I saw through a sudden rift in the clouds Aldebaran and the Hyades!
canbe10{_}2951{_}In all this there was a hint of night--the lynx, the man with the torch, the owl.
canbe10{_}2952{_}Yet I saw--I saw even the stars in absence of the darkness.
canbe10{_}2953{_}I saw, but was apparently not seen nor heard.
canbe10{_}2954{_}Under what awful spell did I exist?
canbe10{_}2955{_}I seated myself at the root of a great tree, seriously to consider what it were best to do.
canbe10{_}2956{_}That I was mad I could no longer doubt, yet recognized a ground of doubt in the conviction.
canbe10{_}2957{_}Of fever I had no trace.
canbe10{_}2958{_}I had, withal, a sense of exhilaration and vigor altogether unknown to me--a feeling of mental and physical exaltation.
canbe10{_}2959{_}My senses seemed all alert; I could feel the air as a ponderous substance; I could hear the silence.
canbe10{_}2960{_}A great root of the giant tree against whose trunk I leaned as I sat held inclosed in its grasp a slab of stone, a part of which protruded into a recess formed by another root.
canbe10{_}2961{_}The stone was thus partly protected from the weather, though greatly decomposed.
canbe10{_}2962{_}Its edges were worn round, its corners eaten away, its surface deeply furrowed and scaled.
canbe10{_}2963{_}Glittering particles of mica were visible in the earth about it--vestiges of its decomposition.
canbe10{_}2964{_}This stone had apparently marked the grave out of which the tree had sprung ages ago.
canbe10{_}2965{_}The tree's exacting roots had robbed the grave and made the stone a prisoner.
canbe10{_}2966{_}A sudden wind pushed some dry leaves and twigs from the uppermost face of the stone; I saw the low-relief letters of an inscription and bent to read it.
canbe10{_}2967{_}God in Heaven!
canbe10{_}2968{_}MY name in full!--the date of MY birth!--the date of MY death!
canbe10{_}2969{_}A level shaft of light illuminated the whole side of the tree as I sprang to my feet in terror.
canbe10{_}2970{_}The sun was rising in the rosy east.
canbe10{_}2971{_}I stood between the tree and his broad red disk--no shadow darkened the trunk!
canbe10{_}2972{_}A chorus of howling wolves saluted the dawn.
canbe10{_}2973{_}I saw them sitting on their haunches, singly and in groups, on the summits of irregular mounds and tumuli filling a half of my desert prospect and extending to the horizon.
canbe10{_}2974{_}And then I knew that these were ruins of the ancient and famous city of Carcosa.
canbe10{_}2975{_}Such are the facts imparted to the medium Bayrolles by the spirit Hoseib Alar Robardin.
canbe10{_}2976{_}THE STRANGER    A man stepped out of the darkness into the little illuminated circle about our failing campfire and seated himself upon a rock.
canbe10{_}2977{_}"You are not the first to explore this region," he said, gravely.
canbe10{_}2978{_}Nobody controverted his statement; he was himself proof of its truth, for he was not of our party and must have been somewhere near when we camped.
canbe10{_}2979{_}Moreover, he must have companions not far away; it was not a place where one would be living or traveling alone.
canbe10{_}2980{_}For more than a week we had seen, besides ourselves and our animals, only such living things as rattlesnakes and horned toads.
canbe10{_}2981{_}In an Arizona desert one does not long coexist with only such creatures as these:  one must have pack animals, supplies, arms--"an outfit."
canbe10{_}2982{_}And all these imply comrades.
canbe10{_}2983{_}It was perhaps a doubt as to what manner of men this unceremonious stranger's comrades might be, together with something in his words interpretable as a challenge, that caused every man of our half-dozen "gentlemen adventurers" to rise to a sitting posture and lay his hand upon a weapon--an act signifying, in that time and place, a policy of expectation.
canbe10{_}2984{_}The stranger gave the matter no attention and began again to speak in the same deliberate, uninflected monotone in which he had delivered his first sentence:  "Thirty years ago Ramon Gallegos, William Shaw, George W. Kent and Berry Davis, all of Tucson, crossed the Santa Catalina mountains and traveled due west, as nearly as the configuration of the country permitted.
canbe10{_}2985{_}We were prospecting and it was our intention, if we found nothing, to push through to the Gila river at some point near Big Bend, where we understood there was a settlement.
canbe10{_}2986{_}We had a good outfit but no guide--just Ramon Gallegos, William Shaw, George W. Kent and Berry Davis."
canbe10{_}2987{_}The man repeated the names slowly and distinctly, as if to fix them in the memories of his audience, every member of which was now attentively observing him, but with a slackened apprehension regarding his possible companions somewhere in the darkness that seemed to enclose us like a black wall; in the manner of this volunteer historian was no suggestion of an unfriendly purpose.
canbe10{_}2988{_}His act was rather that of a harmless lunatic than an enemy.
canbe10{_}2989{_}We were not so new to the country as not to know that the solitary life of many a plainsman had a tendency to develop eccentricities of conduct and character not always easily distinguishable from mental aberration.
canbe10{_}2990{_}A man is like a tree:  in a forest of his fellows he will grow as straight as his generic and individual nature permits; alone in the open, he yields to the deforming stresses and tortions that environ him.
canbe10{_}2991{_}Some such thoughts were in my mind as I watched the man from the shadow of my hat, pulled low to shut out the firelight.
canbe10{_}2992{_}A witless fellow, no doubt, but what could he be doing there in the heart of a desert?
canbe10{_}2993{_}Having undertaken to tell this story, I wish that I could describe the man's appearance; that would be a natural thing to do.
canbe10{_}2994{_}Unfortunately, and somewhat strangely, I find myself unable to do so with any degree of confidence, for afterward no two of us agreed as to what he wore and how he looked; and when I try to set down my own impressions they elude me.
canbe10{_}2995{_}Anyone can tell some kind of story; narration is one of the elemental powers of the race.
canbe10{_}2996{_}But the talent for description is a gift.
canbe10{_}2997{_}Nobody having broken silence the visitor went on to say:  "This country was not then what it is now.
canbe10{_}2998{_}There was not a ranch between the Gila and the Gulf.
canbe10{_}2999{_}There was a little game here and there in the mountains, and near the infrequent water-holes grass enough to keep our animals from starvation.
canbe10{_}3000{_}If we should be so fortunate as to encounter no Indians we might get through.
canbe10{_}3001{_}But within a week the purpose of the expedition had altered from discovery of wealth to preservation of life.
canbe10{_}3002{_}We had gone too far to go back, for what was ahead could be no worse than what was behind; so we pushed on, riding by night to avoid Indians and the intolerable heat, and concealing ourselves by day as best we could.
canbe10{_}3003{_}Sometimes, having exhausted our supply of wild meat and emptied our casks, we were days without food or drink; then a water-hole or a shallow pool in the bottom of an arroyo so restored our strength and sanity that we were able to shoot some of the wild animals that sought it also.
canbe10{_}3004{_}Sometimes it was a bear, sometimes an antelope, a coyote, a cougar-- that was as God pleased; all were food.
canbe10{_}3005{_}"One morning as we skirted a mountain range, seeking a practicable pass, we were attacked by a band of Apaches who had followed our trail up a gulch--it is not far from here.
canbe10{_}3006{_}Knowing that they outnumbered us ten to one, they took none of their usual cowardly precautions, but dashed upon us at a gallop, firing and yelling.
canbe10{_}3007{_}Fighting was out of the question:  we urged our feeble animals up the gulch as far as there was footing for a hoof, then threw ourselves out of our saddles and took to the chaparral on one of the slopes, abandoning our entire outfit to the enemy.
canbe10{_}3008{_}But we retained our rifles, every man--Ramon Gallegos, William Shaw, George W. Kent and Berry Davis."
canbe10{_}3009{_}"Same old crowd," said the humorist of our party.
canbe10{_}3010{_}He was an Eastern man, unfamiliar with the decent observances of social intercourse.
canbe10{_}3011{_}A gesture of disapproval from our leader silenced him and the stranger proceeded with his tale:  "The savages dismounted also, and some of them ran up the gulch beyond the point at which we had left it, cutting off further retreat in that direction and forcing us on up the side.
canbe10{_}3012{_}Unfortunately the chaparral extended only a short distance up the slope, and as we came into the open ground above we took the fire of a dozen rifles; but Apaches shoot badly when in a hurry, and God so willed it that none of us fell.
canbe10{_}3013{_}Twenty yards up the slope, beyond the edge of the brush, were vertical cliffs, in which, directly in front of us, was a narrow opening.
canbe10{_}3014{_}Into that we ran, finding ourselves in a cavern about as large as an ordinary room in a house.
canbe10{_}3015{_}Here for a time we were safe: a single man with a repeating rifle could defend the entrance against all the Apaches in the land.
canbe10{_}3016{_}But against hunger and thirst we had no defense.
canbe10{_}3017{_}Courage we still had, but hope was a memory.
canbe10{_}3018{_}"Not one of those Indians did we afterward see, but by the smoke and glare of their fires in the gulch we knew that by day and by night they watched with ready rifles in the edge of the bush--knew that if we made a sortie not a man of us would live to take three steps into the open.
canbe10{_}3019{_}For three days, watching in turn, we held out before our suffering became insupportable.
canbe10{_}3020{_}Then--it was the morning of the fourth day--Ramon Gallegos said:  "'Senores, I know not well of the good God and what please him.
canbe10{_}3021{_}I have live without religion, and I am not acquaint with that of you.
canbe10{_}3022{_}Pardon, senores, if I shock you, but for me the time is come to beat the game of the Apache.'
canbe10{_}3023{_}"He knelt upon the rock floor of the cave and pressed his pistol against his temple.
canbe10{_}3024{_}'Madre de Dios,' he said, 'comes now the soul of Ramon Gallegos.'
canbe10{_}3025{_}"And so he left us--William Shaw, George W. Kent and Berry Davis.
canbe10{_}3026{_}"I was the leader:  it was for me to speak.
canbe10{_}3027{_}"'He was a brave man,' I said--'he knew when to die, and how.
canbe10{_}3028{_}It is foolish to go mad from thirst and fall by Apache bullets, or be skinned alive--it is in bad taste.
canbe10{_}3029{_}Let us join Ramon Gallegos.'
canbe10{_}3030{_}"'That is right,' said William Shaw.
canbe10{_}3031{_}"'That is right,' said George W. Kent.
canbe10{_}3032{_}"I straightened the limbs of Ramon Gallegos and put a handkerchief over his face.
canbe10{_}3033{_}Then William Shaw said:  'I should like to look like that--a little while.'
canbe10{_}3034{_}"And George W. Kent said that he felt that way, too.
canbe10{_}3035{_}"'It shall be so,' I said:  'the red devils will wait a week.
canbe10{_}3036{_}William Shaw and George W.  Kent, draw and kneel.'
canbe10{_}3037{_}"They did so and I stood before them.
canbe10{_}3038{_}"'Almighty God, our Father,' said I.
canbe10{_}3039{_}"'Almighty God, our Father,' said William Shaw.
canbe10{_}3040{_}"'Almighty God, our Father,' said George W. Kent.
canbe10{_}3041{_}"'Forgive us our sins,' said I.
canbe10{_}3042{_}"'Forgive us our sins,' said they.
canbe10{_}3043{_}"'And receive our souls.'
canbe10{_}3044{_}"'And receive our souls.'
canbe10{_}3045{_}"'Amen!'
canbe10{_}3046{_}"'Amen!'
canbe10{_}3047{_}"I laid them beside Ramon Gallegos and covered their faces."
canbe10{_}3048{_}There was a quick commotion on the opposite side of the campfire: one of our party had sprung to his feet, pistol in hand.
canbe10{_}3049{_}"And you!"
canbe10{_}3050{_}he shouted--"YOU dared to escape?--you dare to be alive?
canbe10{_}3051{_}You cowardly hound, I'll send you to join them if I hang for it!"
canbe10{_}3052{_}But with the leap of a panther the captain was upon him, grasping his wrist.
canbe10{_}3053{_}"Hold it in, Sam Yountsey, hold it in!"
canbe10{_}3054{_}We were now all upon our feet--except the stranger, who sat motionless and apparently inattentive.
canbe10{_}3055{_}Some one seized Yountsey's other arm.
canbe10{_}3056{_}"Captain," I said, "there is something wrong here.
canbe10{_}3057{_}This fellow is either a lunatic or merely a liar--just a plain, every-day liar whom Yountsey has no call to kill.
canbe10{_}3058{_}If this man was of that party it had five members, one of whom--probably himself--he has not named."
canbe10{_}3059{_}"Yes," said the captain, releasing the insurgent, who sat down, "there is something--unusual.
canbe10{_}3060{_}Years ago four dead bodies of white men, scalped and shamefully mutilated, were found about the mouth of that cave.
canbe10{_}3061{_}They are buried there; I have seen the graves--we shall all see them to-morrow."
canbe10{_}3062{_}The stranger rose, standing tall in the light of the expiring fire, which in our breathless attention to his story we had neglected to keep going.
canbe10{_}3063{_}"There were four," he said--"Ramon Gallegos, William Shaw, George W. Kent and Berry Davis."
canbe10{_}3064{_}With this reiterated roll-call of the dead he walked into the darkness and we saw him no more.
canbe10{_}3065{_}At that moment one of our party, who had been on guard, strode in among us, rifle in hand and somewhat excited.
canbe10{_}3066{_}"Captain," he said, "for the last half-hour three men have been standing out there on the mesa."
canbe10{_}3067{_}He pointed in the direction taken by the stranger.
canbe10{_}3068{_}"I could see them distinctly, for the moon is up, but as they had no guns and I had them covered with mine I thought it was their move.
canbe10{_}3069{_}They have made none, but, damn it!
canbe10{_}3070{_}they have got on to my nerves."
canbe10{_}3071{_}"Go back to your post, and stay till you see them again," said the captain.
canbe10{_}3072{_}"The rest of you lie down again, or I'll kick you all into the fire."
canbe10{_}3073{_}The sentinel obediently withdrew, swearing, and did not return.
canbe10{_}3074{_}As we were arranging our blankets the fiery Yountsey said:  "I beg your pardon, Captain, but who the devil do you take them to be?"
canbe10{_}3075{_}"Ramon Gallegos, William Shaw and George W.
canbe10{_}3076{_}Kent."
canbe10{_}3077{_}"But how about Berry Davis?
canbe10{_}3078{_}I ought to have shot him."
canbe10{_}3079{_}"Quite needless; you couldn't have made him any deader.
canbe10{_}3080{_}Go to sleep."
